Message from the Management
The year 2024 marked a period in which BES Engineering Corporation (BES in short) 
advanced with determination amidst uncertainty and continued to lay solid foundations 
amid challenges. Confronted with profound shifts in the global economic structure, 
soaring raw material costs, and increasing complexity in construction management, we 
responded to these challenges with resilience and strategic adaptation. At the same 
time, with the enactment of the "Climate Change Response Act" and the progressively 
clarified action pathways outlined by various ministries, Taiwan's construction industry 
has officially embarked on the journey toward a "net-zero building transformation." 
According to the three-stage blueprint for building transformation announced by the 
Ministry of the Interior in 2023, all new construction projects must achieve "near-zero 
carbon" standards by 2050. This represents not only a new milestone in national policy 
but also an unavoidable responsibility and a prime opportunity for innovation within 
the construction sector.
We are keenly aware that as a key player in Taiwan's engineering and architectural 
development, every ground-breaking mark a tangible commitment to sustainable 
development. In 2024, we not only carried out ISO 14067 carbon footprint verification 
and accelerated the adoption of low-carbon smart building technologies, but also 
used the "BES EcoTech Industrial Park" as a demonstration site to integrate BIM and 
innovative green building design, which received two five-star accolades at the 2024 
International Property Awards —demonstrating our spatial execution capabilities that 
seamlessly integrate intelligence, energy efficiency, and aesthetic excellence.
Upholding our original aspiration to "create a sustainable environment and build 
livable housing," BES continues to incorporate innovative construction methods and 
sustainability governance concepts into various major projects. In 2024, we were 
honored to receive the Silver Award for Sustainability Report at TCSA 2024 for the 
first time, reflecting strong external recognition of both the transparency of our 
sustainability disclosures and the effectiveness of our implementation outcomes.

BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report

Low-Carbon Building Transformation: Pioneering a New 
Paradigm of Smart and Energy-Efficient Development
On the environmental front, we continue to cultivate low-carbon 
construction methods, smart energy-saving systems, and the 
development of a green building materials database. In 2024, our 
green procurement exceeded NTD 500 million. We also promoted 
green building and carbon management technologies on a project-
by-project basis. In the "BES EcoTech Industrial Park," we integrated 
5G + AIoT intelligent systems and obtained the PAS 2080 Carbon 
Management Certification from the UK. The project is expected to 
achieve LEED green building certification by 2025. Through energy 
inventory and the establishment of an energy center, the project is 
projected to significantly reduce overall energy consumption, setting 
a new benchmark for net-zero smart industrial complexes.
In the "Niaozuitan Artificial Lake Project," we implemented 
ecological engineering methods and installed infrared cameras 
to monitor the activity of leopard cats and black winged kites, 
establishing a benchmark for water resource infrastructure that 
coexists harmoniously with the environment. The project is expected 
to supply 210,000 tons of domestic water daily to Changhua and 
40,000 tons to Caotun. It was recognized with the "Gold Award 
for Excellent Construction Site Environmental Protection and 
Management Award" by the Ministry of Environment and the 
"Excellence Award in Public Construction Quality" in the 24th Public 
Construction Commission Golden Quality Awards. In response to 
the challenges of water resource allocation and climate change risks, 
we also participated in the Tainan Desalination Plant and Niaozuitan 
Water Treatment Plant to support national policies aimed at reducing 
groundwater dependency, improving regional water supply stability, 
and securing domestic water usage. These efforts help strengthen 
the overall water supply system in central and southern Taiwan while 
enhancing the efficiency and quality of water resource distribution.
We deeply understand that climate change is no longer a challenge 
for the future; it is an unavoidable responsibility embedded in every 
construction decision made today. BES has already set medium and 
long-term net-zero targets in line with the Science Based Targets 
initiative (SBTi) and is progressively implementing substantive 
carbon reduction actions.
From Construction Site Safety to Community Inclusion: 
Building Trust and Sustainable Talent
We place "safety, inclusion, and development" at the core of our efforts, deepening our culture of 
occupational safety and community engagement. In 2024, we continued to improve occupational 
safety practices, resulting in a notable decrease in major workplace accidents. At the BES EcoTech 
Industrial Park construction site, AI noise detection and smart alert systems were introduced, 
earning us the "New Taipei City Friendly Construction Site Award." On the talent cultivation front, 
we held internship briefings with university departments, organized 11 on-site recruitment events 
in 2024, and offered diverse internal training courses aimed at enhancing professional skills among 
engineering personnel. Meanwhile, the Bi Yan Ge Urban Renewal Project stands as a testament to 
our commitment to community trust. After years of sincere dialogue and negotiation, we successfully 
integrated over one hundred households, demonstrating procedural justice and the spirit of 
consensus-building. The project received the 2024 Urban Renewal and Regeneration Team Award. 
In addition, we actively participated in local charity and educational support, donating scholarships 
to elementary and junior high school students in Tongxiao, and engaging in blood donation and 
community events to promote social inclusion and local economic involvement.
Governance Upgrade: Advancing Infrastructure Innovation
On the governance front, we have implemented a system of ethical corporate management, 
enhanced our risk management and information security mechanisms, and adopted the 
"Whistleblower Reward and Protection Measures." These include the establishment of reporting 
channels and incentive mechanisms to encourage both internal and external stakeholders to report 
illegal activities. Investigations are conducted by an independent unit, forming the first line of 
defense for integrity governance. In addition, we incorporated ESG performance into the executive 
evaluation system for the first time, linking it with compensation to reinforce accountability and 
execution effectiveness in sustainability efforts. In the Corporate Governance Evaluation, BES ranked 
in the top 6% to 20% among all listed companies and in the top 11% to 20% among non-financial 
electronics companies with a market value of over NTD 10 billion. These achievements underscore 
our solid foundation and external trust in governance structure, accountability systems, and 
sustainability information disclosure, providing strong support for advancing ESG practices.
Looking to the future, from smart buildings to digital governance, and from green engineering to 
the establishment of net-zero systems, we will continue to cultivate core sustainability capabilities 
and implement our ESG action blueprint. We will remain committed to creating shared value at the 
intersection of national infrastructure development and social responsibility. We believe that the true sỏa
strength of an enterprise lies in its clear recognition of future responsibilities and its proactive efforts 
to address them.
BES will continue to move forward with solid steps, working hand in hand with this land to shape the 
future and reach new heights.
Chairman
2
Chih-Ming Chou

▍BES Engineering Corporation
BES was originally established as a state-owned enterprise under the Ministry of Economic Affairs, Executive Yuan. It was listed on the Taiwan 
Stock Exchange in 1994 and officially transformed into a private enterprise on June 22, 1995. As of year-end 2024, BES had a paid-in capital of 
NTD 15.31 billion. For details regarding ownership structure, please refer to the "Shareholding Structure and List of Major Shareholders" section 
under the capital raising overview in the BES 2024 Annual Report. By the end of 2024, the total number of employees stood at approximately 
2,138. For more information, please refer to the Talent Recruitment, Retention, and Development (Material Topic) section in this report.
Headquarters
6th Floor, No. 12, Dongxing Road, Songshan District, Taipei City
Site Offices
Located in Taipei City, New Taipei City, Taoyuan City,
Nantou County, Miaoli County, Tainan City, and Kaohsiung
City. In 2024, a total of 28 construction divisions/offices or operating 
locations were engaged in various phases of project implementation.
Overseas Offices
(2) Business Scope
Since its establishment in 1950, BES has played a pivotal role in the development 
of public infrastructure in Taiwan. The company has participated in numerous 
major construction projects that offer economic value, contribute to public 
welfare, and require breakthroughs in innovative technologies. BES operates 
across engineering, construction, and industrial park development. In addition to 
frequently taking part in government public infrastructure projects, BES has also 
undertaken residential and commercial building developments. The company has 
further extended its expertise overseas, leveraging its professional capabilities to 
assist other countries in their urban development and the creation of new cities.

BES is in the building materials and construction industry, primarily undertaking various construction projects. Clients (owners) include government agencies, 
public and private institutions, and private development companies. Since construction projects involve multiple professional divisions of labor, each project 
partners with companies such as construction firms, design units, sales, and relevant consultants and contractors. The roles and division of responsibilities 
from upstream throughout downstream and related units within the overall industry value chain are as follows:

3. Sustainability Accounting Standard
Since 2016, BES has published the "Corporate Social Responsibility Report." In 2022, in response to regulatory requirements, it was renamed the 
"Sustainability Report." The 2024 Sustainability Report is the tenth non-financial disclosure report issued since 2016.
Report Overview and 
Publication Frequency
This sustainability report was 
published in August 2025 and 
will be issued annually on a 
regular basis in the future. 
Stakeholders are welcome to 
download and review this report 
from the BES official website 
and the Market Observation 
Post System.
Report Boundaries and 
Scope
The reporting period for this 
sustainability report spans 
from January 1 to December 
31, 2024. This report is issued 
annually and primarily covers 
the Taipei headquarters and site 
offices involved in operational 
activities during 2024. It does 
not include overseas operating 
locations and subsidiaries. The 
scope of disclosure accounts 
for 94% of the consolidated 
financial statement's net 
revenue. During the reporting 
period, there were no significant 
changes to the organization's 
size, structure, ownership, or 
supply chain.
Restatement of Information
This report includes adjustments to the following relevant data from the 2023 Sustainability Report: Regarding the direct economic 
value generated and distributed over the past three years, the figures for 2022 and 2023 have been adjusted for payments to capital 
providers, encompassing consolidated interest expenses and dividend distributions, to fully reflect the economic distribution to 
capital providers. Newly added disclosures include business tax, income tax, and property tax. Simultaneously, to avoid double 
counting, employee salaries and benefits previously duplicated under "operating costs" (already covered under employee salaries 
and benefits) have been removed. These adjustments enhance the accuracy and transparency of financial information classification, 
yet do not affect the substantive meaning of the overall economic value distribution, and are consistent with the amounts in the 
consolidated financial statements audited and certified by accountants. For details, please refer to the Financial Performance (Material 
Topic) section of this report. Additionally, the occupational injury statistics for BES workers in 2022 and 2023 have been adjusted 
to include contractor-related items and figures, to fully meet indicator requirements. For details, please refer to the Occupational 
Safety and Health (Material Topic) section of this report. Regarding the description of non-compliance incidents and subsequent 
parts, the 2022 environmental category amount was adjusted after internal verification, as the original data compilation period did 
not cover some later additional expenditure items. Furthermore, the originally disclosed 2023 social category amount was found 
to have some duplicate entries or improper classifications after verification and has since been corrected and adjusted. For details, 
please refer to the Regulatory Compliance section. For energy consumption, the original data for 2022 and 2023 has been corrected 
due to misstatements in the various types of non-renewable energy consumption data found during external verification in 2024. 
For details, please refer to the Climate Action section. Regarding BES's total water withdrawal and water withdrawal intensity for 
the past three years, the water withdrawal amounts for 2022 and 2023 disclosed in 2023 were corrected due to misstatements. In 
addition, regarding the number of sites included in the statistics for 2022 and 2023, the original method of counting sites was based 
on the number of site offices rather than actual water withdrawal points, thus a correction has been made to clarify the number of 
water withdrawal sites. For details, please refer to the Environmental Management section. Concerning the three-year comparison of 
BES employee working hours statistics, the disclosed data for 2022 and 2023 have been adjusted because the calculation of working 
hours did not include or double-counted the number of migrant workers. For details, please refer to the Occupational Safety and 
Health section of this report.
Compilation Guidelines
This report was compiled in accordance with the "Taiwan Stock Exchange Corporation Rules Governing the Preparation and Filing of 
Sustainability Reports by TWSE Listed Companies" and the 2021 version of the GRI Standards with a GRI Content Index provided in the 
appendix. It also discloses sustainability accounting indicators issued by the Sustainability Accounting Standards Board (SASB) for the 
Engineering & Construction Services sector, along with climate-related financial disclosures following the recommendations of the 
Financial Stability Board (FSB)'s Task Force on Climate-related Financial Disclosures (TCFD). In addition, we have followed the disclosure 
requirements of Table 2 under Article 4-1 of the "Taiwan Stock Exchange Corporation Rules Governing the Preparation and Filing of 
Sustainability Reports by TWSE Listed Companies" concerning climate-related information. For details, please refer to the appendix.

▍Responsible Unit and Quality Management for the Report
To enhance the completeness and credibility of BES's sustainability reporting, BES has established a process for preparing sustainability reports and 
conducting internal audits or external verification in accordance with the "Taiwan Stock Exchange Corporation Rules Governing the Preparation and Filing 
of Sustainability Reports by TWSE Listed Companies." These procedures are incorporated into the company's "BES Sustainability Report Preparation and 
Assurance Procedure" and the "BES Engineering Corporation Sustainability Information Management Regulations." Furthermore, the procedures are 
submitted to the Board of Directors for review and approval to ensure their appropriateness.
BES Official Website
Sustainability Development Committee, BES Engineering Corporation

Approach
Responsible Unit (or Position)
Report Compilation
This report is coordinated and planned by the Sustainability Development Committee. All 
data, strategic goals, and performance indicators disclosed in this report are provided by the 
Sustainability Development Implementation Group (each responsible division).
Sustainability Development 
Implementation Group 
(Relevant Divisions)
Internal Review
Upon completion, this report is reviewed for completeness and accuracy by each unit, and 
then approved by the highest-level supervisors of the relevant units.
Sustainability Development

Sustainability Development 
Committee
External Assurance
To enhance this report's accuracy and credibility, BES engaged TÜV NORD Taiwan to 
perform verification based on AA 1000 AS v3 Type 1, moderate assurance level. Financial 
data was audited and confirmed by Deloitte Taiwan, while greenhouse gas inventory was 
verified by SGS Taiwan Ltd. There are no conflicts of interest among these entities, ensuring 
independence and objectivity.
TÜV NORD Taiwan
Deloitte

the Board of Directors for approval before public release.

BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report

2024 BES's Signature Projects
Through its engineering expertise, quality, and extensive experience in both public infrastructure and private construction projects, including bridges, 
tunnels, ports, airports, metro systems, industrial parks, high-tech plants, hospitals, and premium residential buildings, BES has established overseas joint 
ventures in eight countries since 2007 to participate in major public infrastructure projects, completing over 20 projects. Upholding its core values of 
engineering improvement and technical advancement, and leveraging AI-driven real-time construction management technologies, BES has earned a strong 
reputation by winning numerous domestic and international engineering awards. The company aspires to continue setting benchmarks in the construction 
industry through its decades of professional experience. In parallel, BES is dedicated to smart building development, leveraging structures as integrated 
platforms equipped with building installations, office automation, and communication networks into an optimized combination of structure, systems, 
services, and management. Furthermore, BES adheres to sustainable design principles, integrating low-carbon construction techniques and environmentally 
responsible materials. This not only creates livable environments but also affirms its commitment to environmental sustainability.
Looking ahead, BES will continue to center its planning around "smart energy efficiency and green architecture," creating urban corridors rich in greenery, 
expanding green lungs, and promoting environmental integration in living spaces. The company aims to redefine the concept of the "urban jungle."

BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report
On May 31, 2024, the "BES EcoTech Industrial Park" received two Five-Star Top Honors at the 2024 United 
Kingdom International Property Awards in the categories of "Commercial & Manufacturing Architecture" and 
"Sustainable Commercial Development." The project was also selected in the second "Friendly and Outstanding 
Construction Site Selection Campaign" organized by New Taipei City. During construction, a noise sensor-linked 
alert system was implemented to ensure both technologically advanced site management and environmental 
friendliness to surrounding communities.
C. BES EcoTech
With increasing market demand and government 
promotion, the intelligentization of buildings has become 
a modern trend, changing the way people live. How 
to keep up with the times and create intelligent office 
spaces and environments that integrate information 
systems and have human-centric characteristics is an 
important challenge for smart building design.
BES actively incorporates smart and green building 
design. The "BES EcoTech Industrial Park" integrates 
smart buildings and smart logistics into its factory-office 
planning through 5G and AIoT technologies. It further 
aligns with Building Information Modeling (BIM), facility 
management, Digital Twin, 3D visualization monitoring, 
and the future metaverse concept of physical-virtual 
integration, implementing a highly efficient management 
strategy that extends building lifespan, reduces energy 
consumption and manpower needs, and lowers 
operational costs during the building's usage phase.
The "BES EcoTech Industrial Park" provides an advanced, 
intelligent, and green industrial-office environment, 
aiming to attract cutting-edge and competitive 
industries to drive regional industrial transformation. 
It aligns with the government's overarching economic 
and industrial development plans to strengthen Taiwan's 
long-term advantage in high-tech sectors. In addition 
to offering high-quality production, R&D facilities, and 
office spaces, the park addresses urban environmental 
needs and the demand for green, comfortable living 
spaces by incorporating plazas and open areas for 
ecological landscaping. These features help enhance 
the urban aesthetics of the Tucheng Industrial Zone 
and surrounding areas, while promoting harmony and 
convenience between industry and daily life.
Through close collaboration with industries, BES supports local urban development by integrating cutting-edge 
technologies and professional expertise to shape a new paradigm for regional industrial growth. The "EcoTech 
Industrial Park" exemplifies BES's solid architectural capabilities in creating a smart campus that aligns with 
enterprise client needs and green building trends. It incorporates AI intelligence, environmental sustainability, 
resource-sharing and circularity, health and safety, and adherence to ESG standards. The park leverages energy 
management technologies to monitor greenhouse gas emissions and conducts ISO 14067 Carbon Footprint 
Verification, enabling effective management of carbon inventories and seamlessly integrating sustainability 
with innovation.
In terms of environmental sustainability, the project features a low building coverage ratio of 34%, a high green 
coverage ratio of 78%, and nearly 8,400 ping of ecological landscaped park area. It extensively incorporates 
energy-efficient responsible for sustainability and locally sourced building materials to reduce carbon footprint 
and emissions, implementing carbon absorption and climate mitigation strategies. The design includes rooftop 
solar panels, gray water and rainwater recycling systems, smart wastewater monitoring, and intelligent energy-
saving facilities, promoting the use of renewable energy and the recycling of water resources. The project is 
currently undergoing pre-certification application for the U.S. LEED green building label and became the first 
project globally to receive PAS 2080 Carbon Management Certification from BSI (British Standards Institution), as 
well as candidate certification under Taiwan's EEWH Green Building system. It is scheduled to obtain the usage 
license in the second quarter of 2026.

BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report
D. Niaozuitan Artificial Lake
The "Niaozuitan Artificial Lake Project" in which BES participated, is a major water resources infrastructure 
project under the Water Resources Agency. BES commenced construction in 2019, completed the first 
lake zone, and initiated water impoundment in 2021. In 2023, the project played a drought relief role by 
supplying water. By 2024, all six lake zones had been filled, and the project was officially completed in 
January 2025.
Niaozuitan is located beside the Wu River in Caotun Township, Nantou County. It comprises six lake zones 
and resembles a bird's beak when viewed from above. The lake has a water surface area of 110 hectares, 
which is approximately one-seventh the size of Sun Moon Lake. When full, it can store up to 14.5 million 
cubic meters of water, enough to supply one million people for 58 days. This allows for the full utilization 
of the abundant water resources of the Wu River. The lake primarily supplies domestic water to the 
Changhua and Caotun areas. It is expected to provide 210,000 metric tons of water per day to Changhua 
and 40,000 metric tons to Caotun. Previously, Changhua relied heavily on groundwater extraction and 
water transfers from Taichung and Yunlin. Niaozuitan can meet approximately half of Changhua's daily 
water demand. This alleviates coastal land subsidence caused by excessive groundwater extraction and 
enhances regional water supply resilience.
During the construction phase, BES adopted multiple green construction methods. These included the 
use of reclaimed asphalt, system formwork, expanded tree planting, solar-powered monitoring systems, 
and the reuse of resource materials. All machinery deployed during construction was new and certified 
under the "Gold Label for 100% Clean Self-Management, resulting in a successful reduction of carbon 
emissions by 52.68%. In addition, BES also placed strong emphasis on the prevention of water pollution, 
noise control, and air pollution control. Through comprehensive environmental controls, including on-
site air quality monitoring, effluent discharge checks, and an automatic sprinkler system, BES effectively 
ensured environmental protection throughout the construction period.
To ensure ecological sustainability in the Niaozuitan area, BES established an ecological conservation 
team to promote species conservation, removal of invasive species, and ecological assessments. The team 
collaborated with academic institutions and installed 20 camera traps to investigate the potential impact 
of the project on leopard cats. After collecting relevant data, the team implemented various mitigation 
measures, including constructing specialized habitats ("leopard cat apartments")," removing invasive 
species that affect their habitats, establishing wildlife corridors, and establishing supplementary foraging 
zones to reduce the impact on leopard cats. Additionally, the team also developed conservation strategies 
for species such as the black-winged kite and the oriental pratincole, and actively worked to prevent the 
spread of invasive alien plants, aiming to create an eco-friendly habitat in the Niaozuitan area.
After its completion, Niaozuitan continues to integrate ecological values and sustainable development. 
A total of 6,600 trees were planted throughout the lake area, comparable to the total number of trees in 
Daan Forest Park. In the future, the site is expected to become a green and low-carbon recreational area. 
The unique design of six lake zones, combined with an independent water supply and storage system for 
each lake, not only enhances operational flexibility but also allows for individual desilting operations. This 
approach extends the service life of the lake and realizes the goal of sustainable development.
In 2024, the project received the Gold Award at the Ceremony for 
the Enterprise Air Pollution Response and Excellent Construction 
Site Environmental Protection and Management Award organized 
by the Ministry of Environment. It was also honored with the 
Excellence Award in Public Construction Quality at the 24th Public 
Construction Commission Golden Quality Awards – Excellence 
Award. These recognitions demonstrate that the Niaozuitan 
Artificial Lake Project effectively balanced environmental protection 
and construction quality during the construction phase.
Project Length: 5 years (2019-2025)
Effective Storage Capacity: 14.50 million 
cubic meters, sufficient for 1 million people 
for 58 days.
Daily Water Supply: 250,000 tons (210,000 
tons for Changhua, 40,000 tons for Caotun)
Project Benefits: Stabilizes residential 
water supply, mitigates land subsidence, 
and promotes local tourism.

E. Bi Yan Ge
Bi Yan Ge project under BES is part of the "Yanshou Public Housing Section I" urban renewal project. The original buildings in this section were granted a construction in 1992. 
In 2000, it was identified as a concrete structure damaged by salt-contaminated sand by the Taiwan Provincial Association of Structural Engineers and was subsequently 
officially listed by the Taipei City Government. More than 20 years have passed since its completion. In addition to increasing needs for updates in building systems and 
spatial functionality to meet current standards, more than half of the 203 units across the seven residential buildings in the section have long suffered from corrosion caused 
by salt-contaminated concrete.
According to Article 13 of the Taipei City Urban Renewal Self-Governance Ordinance, if a legally constructed building suffers damage due to earthquakes, typhoons, floods, 
fires, explosions, or other force majeure events, or if it is identified as a high-chloride concrete building or a building contaminated by radiation, and is deemed potentially 
hazardous by the competent building authority, the area may apply to be designated as a renewal unit. This is permissible when more than 80 percent of the property owners' 
consent, and the same proportion of the land area and the total floor area of the legally constructed buildings in agreement. Through the "Yanshou Public Housing Section I" 
urban renewal project, BES aims to help address: (1) structural safety concerns associated with high-chloride concrete buildings, and to reconstruct them for improved quality 
of living and public safety; (2) the enhancement of building functionality and the creation of a high-quality living environment, while also strengthening the urban disaster 
prevention and relief system.
Over the years, residents approached multiple construction companies for assistance, yet no consensus 
was reached. In contrast, BES remained committed to supporting the residents of the salt-contaminated 
buildings in the Yanshou area. Through transparent communication and the provision of comprehensive 
regulatory information, BES helped landowners maximize their floor area ratio (FAR) bonus, gaining the 
trust and support of the residents. BES also worked together with public sector agencies to explain the 
goals, benefits, impacts, and means of participation in the urban renewal project. This helped reduce 
misunderstandings and doubts and gradually fostered mutual trust. Bi Yan Ge (Yanshou Public Housing 
Section I), which spans about 1,500 ping and originally housed 203 units, experienced a nearly nine-year 
delay due to three non-consenting households refusing to relocate. In accordance with the principle of 
"sincere negotiation" as set forth in the Urban Renewal Act, BES made numerous personal visits to these 
residents to engage in direct communication and coordination. By demonstrating genuine attentiveness 
to their concerns and working closely with the Taipei City Government, the three non-consenting 
households came to trust the implementer and ultimately agreed to authorize BES to carry out the 
urban renewal. As a result, the project was successfully integrated and is scheduled for completion and 
handover by the end of 2025.
"Bi Yan Ge" was awarded the 2024 Urban Renewal 
and Rebuilding Award for Aging and At-Risk 
Buildings Teams, highlighting the project's 
contribution to improving the quality of living for 
community residents.
During the construction process, BES also considered 
the impact of heat hazards by implementing hazard 
prevention measures, such as installing misting 
devices and providing worker rest areas, to reduce 
the risk of heat exposure for construction workers. 
These measures also contribute to the control of air 
quality indicators during construction.
In terms of occupational safety, BES conducted 
a hazard assessment and subsequently installed 
a safety-enhanced elevator shaft featuring a 
foldable working platform to mitigate fall-related 
risks. This setup effectively reduces risks related to 
open-edge construction during operations.

ESG Governance Structure
1.1 
The Board of Directors of BES serves as the highest decision-making 
and supervisory body for the company's sustainability policies and the 
formulation of development goals. The Sustainability Development 
Committee, chaired by the Chairman of the Board of Directors, oversees 
the Sustainable Development Implementation Group, which is responsible 
for coordinating and implementing sustainability action plans. The Group 
reports on its progress to the Sustainability Development Committee on 
a regular basis.
The Sustainable Development Implementation Group consists of three 
subordinate teams, each focusing on environmental protection, social 
responsibility, and corporate governance. Each team is responsible for 
ESG-related initiatives, including employee training and capacity-building 
programs. The discussion topics covered by each team are illustrated in 
the figure below:

and strategic partners. Implementation is ensured through training and education, 
document signing, internal audits, and institutional evaluations. For example, newly 
registered suppliers must sign the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter" 
before completing the registration process. Most of the policies are disclosed 
on the company's official website under the "Corporate Rules and Regulations" 
section, demonstrating BES's commitment to sustainable governance and proactive 
stakeholder transparency. In addition, the core spirit of these policies is integrated 
into the implementation guidelines for material topics in the annual Sustainability

▍Impact Management Mechanism  GRI 2-13  2-14
The Board of Directors has established a Risk Management Group to manage actual or potential 
risks that affect sustainable development. The Board functions as the highest supervisory and 
decision-making body for enterprise risk management (ERM), approving the company' s risk 
management objectives and policies, and implementing management actions. They continuously 
monitor the risk management mechanism to ensure its effective operation and bear significant 
responsibility for risk management. The Audit Committee also participates in supervising the 
operations of the Risk Management Group, thereby enhancing governance effectiveness and 
transparency.
The Sustainable Development Implementation Group is responsible for identifying non-financial 
impact issues across the ESG spectrum, which are then delegated to functional unit managers for 
response planning and mitigation. These managers propose risk response measures based on 
actual operations, thereby controlling the likelihood of business-related impacts.
To fulfill its corporate social responsibility and implement the philosophy of sustainable operations, 
BES has formulated and publicly disclosed a number of policies and codes of conduct, covering 
areas such as integrity management, human rights protection, gender equality, environmental 
management, anti-corruption, and information security. The key policies include the "Practical 
Guidelines for Sustainable Development", the "Ethical Corporate Management Best Practice 
Principles", the "Human Rights Policy", the "Guidelines for the Promotion of Gender Equality", 
and the "Greenhouse Gas Emission Reduction Management Policy". These policies are guided 
by international human rights conventions such as the "International Covenant on Civil and 
Political Rights", the "UN Global Compact's Ten Principles", and the "ILO Declaration on 
Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work", to ensure that employees work in a safe and secure 
environment, fully reflecting the spirit of respect and protection. All relevant rules and regulations 
are implemented after approval by the Board of Directors, and the Sustainability Development 
Committee conducts annual reviews of these policies and proposes revisions as needed based on 
regulatory or operational requirements.

Material Topics Analysis 
and Management
1.3 
In its 2024 material topic identification process, BES adopted 
the GRI Universal Standards (2021) and SASB Standards, 
and followed the AA1000 Accountability Principles (2018) to 
implement the identification process based on the following 
four core principles:
Inclusivity
Incorporating the views of various stakeholders.
Materiality
Evaluating the degree of impact topics have on the company 
and society.
Responsiveness
Responding to key stakeholder concerns.
Impact
Analyzing the substantive impacts of business operations on 
the environment and society.
In addition, the Company referred to the "European 
Sustainability Reporting Standards (ESRS)" published by the 
"European Financial Reporting Advisory Group (EFRAG)" and 
the "Implementation Guidance on Materiality Assessment", 
introducing the "double materiality" analytical framework.
 Impact Materiality          
	 Financial Materiality
The internal company questionnaire and stakeholder feedback 
were compiled and disclosed in accordance with the GRI 
Standards. The material topics were arranged by order of 
priority, with each topic presenting its corresponding impact 
areas, management strategies, and implementation outcomes. 
This process forms a critical foundation for aligning BES's 
sustainability objectives with strategic planning, thereby 
enhancing stakeholder communication and information 
transparency.

■ Based on evolving policy trends, international disclosure frameworks (e.g., GRI, SASB, 
AA1000), and stakeholder expectations, BES consolidated sustainability issues that are 
highly relevant to its operations.
■ Eight stakeholder groups were identified, and a questionnaire survey was conducted to 
collect their feedback on sustainability issues.
■ Based on the level of concern and the degree of impact, a total of nine material topics 
were identified and prioritized in 2024.
■ External consultants were invited to review the overall process and the appropriateness 
of the applied standards, in order to confirm the completeness and consistency of the 
material topics.
■ The nine material topics were incorporated into the preparation of the sustainability 
report and the formulation of material topic management strategies, serving as the 
basis for subsequent communication and actions.
■ The degree of impact of each sustainability issue on corporate operations was 
assessed by department heads, and combined with the level of concern expressed by 
stakeholders through the questionnaire to conduct a comprehensive analysis.
▍	Roles of the Board of Directors and 
Sustainability Governance Units
	
GRI 2-12  2-13  2-14
The Board of Directors plays the highest decision-making 
and supervisory role in the assessment of Material Topics. 
After identifying material topics and setting indicators 
and goals, respective responsible units develop related 
indicators and objectives for implementation. The results 
of the projects are periodically reported to the Board of 
Directors by the Sustainability Development Committee. 
The Board oversees short, medium, and long-term 
sustainability strategies, including goal-setting, 
implementation planning, and performance evaluation.
To ensure alignment with goals and progress in 
implementation, the Sustainability Development 
Committee holds at least one meeting annually and 
regularly reports the outcomes of its initiatives to the 
Board of Directors. The Committee authorizes the 
Sustainable Development Implementation Group 
(hereinafter referred to as the "Implementation 
Group") to coordinate the progress of sustainability 
issues and data integration, and to track and provide 
recommendations on the management strategies for 
material topics.
In the preparation of the sustainability report, the Board 
of Directors also plays a key role in the management 
process. At the initial phase of report preparation each 
year, the Implementation Group compiles feedback from 
internal and external stakeholders based on predefined 
reporting themes and directions. After the drafting of the 
preliminary version is completed, it is reviewed jointly 
by department heads and external consultants. The final 
version is approved after review by the Sustainability 
Development Committee and the Board of Directors, 
and then publicly released to ensure the transparency, 
consistency, and accuracy of the report content.

1. Identification of Stakeholder Categories
Considering its operational nature and industry profile, BES Engineering 
Corporation, referred to the five key principles of the AA1000 Stakeholder 
Engagement Standard (SES) to conduct an assessment from the following 
five dimensions: "level of dependency," "responsibility," "intensity of concern," 
"influence," and "diversity of perspectives." Through this process, eight key 
stakeholders were identified, including (1) investors/shareholders, (2) clients/
owners, (3) employees, (4) suppliers, (5) community residents, (6) government 
agencies / industry associations, (7) investment institutions and banks, and (8) the 
media. Compared with the 2023 version, BES in 2024 consolidated the previously 
separate categories of "government agencies" and "industry associations" into 
a single stakeholder group to reflect the substantial interactions between policy 
advocacy and industry communication. This adjustment demonstrates BES's 
emphasis on "regulatory promotion," "industry consensus building," and "policy 
feedback," recognizing the high complementarity between the two in regulatory 
advocacy, resource integration, and industry dialogue. As interactions become 
increasingly frequent, incorporating both into an integrated management and 
communication framework enhances BES's efficiency in response to industrial 
policy and sustainability trends.

3. Questionnaire Survey on Stakeholder Concern and Impact Assessment
To enhance the representativeness and objectivity of material topic assessments, BES conducted a simultaneous survey of both external stakeholders 
and internal operational units to collect their views on the level of concern and perceived impact of 21 sustainability issues. The results were subjected to 
standardization and quantitative analysis as the basis for prioritizing the material topics.
	For the same 21 sustainability issues, BES designed two separate assessment questionnaires 
based on the frameworks of the GRI Standards and the European Sustainability Reporting 
Standards (ESRS) to conduct internal impact assessments.
	The response summary is as follows:
■The "Sustainability Impact Assessment Questionnaire" was primarily used to 
evaluate the positive and negative impacts (Impact Materiality) of each issue on the 
external environment and society. A total of 21 responses were collected, covering ESG-
responsible departments and cross-departmental managerial functions.
■The "Organizational Operational Impact Assessment Questionnaire" was primarily 
used to evaluate the potential impacts (Financial Materiality) of each issue on BES's 
operations and finances. A total of 19 responses were collected, covering core business 
and operational departments.
Both assessments utilized a standardized quantitative scoring methodology, and the assessment 
dimensions included:

4. Identification of Material Topics
The results of the "Stakeholder Questionnaire Survey", 
the "Sustainability Impact Assessment Questionnaire", 
and the "Organizational Operational Impact Assessment 
Questionnaire" were subjected to equal-weighted quantitative 
analysis to comprehensively reflect both the external level of 
concern and the internal impact of each material topic. The 
identification logic is as follows:
	 Impact Materiality Assessment: Department heads were 
asked to assess the positive and negative impacts of each 
issue through questionnaires. In accordance with the 
methodologies specified by the GRI and ESRS, impact 
was quantified as "impact materiality × likelihood 
of occurrence." The questionnaire provided concrete 
examples of both positive and negative scenarios to 
support more accurate judgments.
	 Financial Materiality Assessment: Referring to ESRS, the 
definition of financial impact includes potential effects 
on operational performance, access to capital, cash flow, 
and overall financial condition. In this assessment cycle, 
revenue growth was used as the primary metric due to 
its direct correspondence to financial statement items in 
determining financial materiality.
	 To assist the organization in responding to the impacts 
of sustainability and operations, material topics were 
prioritized for inclusion if they met the criterion of 
"ranking among the top seven in financial impact score 
and also among the top seven in either positive or 
negative impact."
	 To incorporate stakeholder perspectives, this cycle's 
concern assessment adopted a cluster analysis approach, 
in which eight key stakeholder groups independently 
scored and ranked each issue. Following the principle 
of "cross-group consensus focus," if an issue appeared 
among the top three in the rankings of three or more 
groups, it was deemed a high-consensus concern and 
included as a strategic material topic.
	 Additionally, based on the opinions of internal and 
external consultants and experts, certain topics identified 
as important issues under regulatory trends were also 
considered for inclusion as material topics.
	 After integrating quantitative and qualitative assessments, 
the Sustainable Development Working Group reviewed 
and finalized the material topic list.
	 Positive Impact Matrix: Potential contributions to environmental improvement, social well-being, and 
innovation value ("Impact Opportunity").
	 Negative Impact Matrix: Risks of negative impacts on resource consumption, social controversies, and 
compliance risks ("Impact Risk").

external environment and society," it is marked with a ★in the corresponding column.
Any issue that ranks among the top seven in at least two of the three dimensions (impact on 
operations/finance, positive external impact, negative external impact) and negative external impact, is 
designated as a priority candidate for material topics.

▍Stakeholder Concern Level Survey Results
A total of 540 responses were collected for this stakeholder questionnaire. The 
respondent groups included: investors/shareholders (15), investment institutions and 
banks (8), clients/owners (106), employees (202), suppliers (110), community residents 
(41), government agencies/industry associations (45), and media (13).
To present the overall concern level of each stakeholder group regarding sustainability 
issues, BES consolidated the questionnaire responses from all groups and conducted 
a statistical analysis of issue concern levels. To avoid biased results caused by an 
excessive number of responses from any single group, the rankings were determined 
based on the average within each group, followed by an overall average, to help 
readers better understand overall trends.
As the number of samples varies across stakeholder groups, 
particularly in categories such as media, banks, and investors 
where the number of questionnaire responses is relatively low, 
directly calculating an overall average ranking may result in 
representational bias and affect the basis for subsequent actions.
Therefore, a two-stage method was adopted in this analysis 
to account for both representativeness and distributional 
differences:
This approach effectively identifies issues with higher levels of 
overlapping concern across stakeholder groups and reveals the 
degree of consensus among different groups regarding specific 
topics. It also ensures breadth, representativeness, and balance, 
while avoiding statistical bias caused by unequal sample sizes or 
the masking of differences through averaging. The results serve 
as a key basis for the selection of material topics.

of overlapping concern for each issue. Issues that are 
of concern to three or more stakeholder groups are 
considered to have a high concern level and are given 
priority for inclusion as material topics.
5. Validation of Material Topics
Following the selection of material topics based on the aforementioned standards, external 
consultants were engaged to jointly review and validate the identified material topics and 
the appropriateness of the applied thresholds. This process ensured that no significant topics 
deserving priority reporting were overlooked or insufficiently addressed, thereby upholding 
completeness, inclusiveness, and comprehensiveness, as well as alignment with BES's 
sustainability development strategy. With the incorporation of expert opinions from external 
consultants, a total of 9 material topics were identified for 2024.
6. Confirmation of Material Topics
A total of 9 material topics were ultimately confirmed for priority reporting. These include 2 
environmental topics, 2 social topics, and 5 governance/economic topics. Compared to the 
previous reporting period (the 2023 Sustainability Report), the list of material topics has been 
adjusted (a comparison table will be provided later). The reporting boundary remains unchanged.
In addition, to ensure effective communication with a broad range of stakeholders through the 
sustainability report, a "Corporate Sustainability Section" has been established on the company's 
official website. A dedicated contact channel for stakeholders is also provided on the site. 
Stakeholders may use this email channel to maintain open and constructive communication 
regarding material topic information or other contents of the report, including any questions, 
suggestions, or complaints.

▍Changes in Material Topics in 2024  GRI 
3-2
In 2024, our assessment of the scope of material topics referred not 
only to sustainability topics defined by the GRI Standards, but also to 
disclosure topics required by the SASB Standards for the industry to 
which BES belongs. This approach helped ensure that the material topics 
are more focused on key and emerging issues.
As a construction company, BES primarily engages in contracting various 
engineering and construction projects. Clients (project owners) include 
government agencies, public and private institutions, and private 
development companies. Since construction projects involve a wide 
range of professional divisions of labor, each project typically involves 
collaborative partners such as construction firms, design units, sales 
channels, and related consultants and supporting vendors.

corporate clients, and individual consumers.

Founded in 1950, BES is guided by a distinguished management team. From the Ten Major Construction Projects and the Six-Year National Development 
Plan to the i-Taiwan 12 Projects, has provided services across public infrastructure, private construction, real estate development, and international 
operations, earning widespread acclaim. In the 2024 Corporate Governance Evaluation, the Company was ranked in the top 6% to 20% of all listed 
companies, and in the top 11% to 20% among non-financial and non-electronics companies with a market capitalization exceeding NTD 10 billion.

▍Board Composition  GRI 
2-9  2-10
The Board of Directors is the highest governing 
body of BES, responsible for overseeing the 
Company's long-term business strategies, risk 
management, executive appointments and 
compensation, ensuring sound operations and 
sustainable growth The Board also oversees the 
Company's economic, environmental, and social 
impacts. 
Between 2017 and 2022, the Company 
progressively established the Audit Committee, 
Compensation Committee, and Sustainable 
Development Committee. These committees 
gather stakeholder feedback through meetings, 
questionnaires, and grievance mechanisms 
to inform strategy adjustments. The Board 
regularly reviews the impact management 
performance of each committee to ensure 
effective implementation of procedures. The 
Board reviews business performance and 
strategic issues monthly, discusses key strategies 
and major events, and examines topics related to 
environmental, social, and governance impacts, 
risks, and opportunities. In 2024, the 27th Board 
of Directors convened 12 meetings, achieving 
a 90% attendance rate. Prior to each meeting, 
the board affairs unit reviews the relevance of 
proposals to any director's interests and reminds 
directors to recuse themselves in accordance 
with the law.
In 2019, BES appointed a Corporate Governance 
Officer responsible for meeting planning, agenda 
setting, director training, and communication, 
to ensure smooth Board operations. Major 
resolutions passed by the Board are disclosed 
on the Company's official website. The BES 
Board deliberates on financial and operational 
decisions, significant institutional adjustments, 
and sustainability-related policies in accordance 
with the "Board Meeting Rules" and the 
"Sustainable Development Best Practice 
Principles."
▍Board Nomination and Selection  GRI 2-10  2-11
According to BES's Articles of Incorporation and the Corporate Governance Best Practice Principles, directors serve a 
three-year term (June 7, 2023, to June 6, 2026). The nomination and selection of board members follow the Articles of 
Incorporation, adopting a candidate nomination system. In addition to evaluating the academic and professional qualifications 
of each candidate, stakeholder opinions are also considered. Candidates' management experience in economic, environmental, 
and social issues are considered, and compliance with the "Director Election Regulations" and the "Corporate Governance Best 
Practice Principles" is ensured to maintain diversity and independence among board members.
As of December 31, 2024, the Board comprises nine members, including four independent directors. Their areas of 
expertise cover finance and accounting, law, engineering and construction, and industry knowledge, and they also 
uphold high ethical standards. This approach ensures both diversity and independence within the board. The Board is 
committed to gender equality, with a target of over 10% female representation. Accordingly, BES held a by-election in 
2024 to appoint one female independent director (1 out of 9, or 11%).
Candidates for independent director meet the requirements of the government's "Regulations Governing Appointment 
of Independent Directors and Compliance Matters for Public Companies." In addition, all independent directors serve on 
BES's functional committees, including the Compensation Committee and the Audit Committee, and are subject to legal 
assessments and evaluations of their independence.
BES's Chairman and President are the same individual. In accordance with the "Guidelines for the Establishment and 
Exercise of Powers of the Board of Directors of Listed Companies" by the Taiwan Stock Exchange Corporation, BES 
appointed an additional independent director in 2024. The Chairman of BES concurrently serves as the President due 
to his extensive operational experience and professional leadership capabilities, which ensure strong alignment between 
strategic decision-making and business execution.  To mitigate potential conflicts of interest, the company has established 
an independent director system to oversee the fairness of Board decisions. In addition, BES has set up an Audit Committee 
and a Compensation Committee, responsible for financial oversight and executive compensation evaluations. Furthermore, 
the Company has implemented internal audit and risk management mechanisms to ensure that business decisions align 
with governance principles and to safeguard shareholder rights and long-term corporate development.
▍Conflicts of Interest   GRI 2-15  
BES has established the "Board Meeting Rules". Regarding board resolutions, directors with personal interests that 
may harm the company' s interests are not allowed to vote on such matters or act as a proxy for other directors. The 
Rules are to prevent directors from using their voting rights for personal gain at the expense of the company or other 
stakeholders.
To prevent insider trading, avoid improper disclosure of information, and ensure the consistency and accuracy of external 
communications, BES has established the "Procedures for Handling Material Internal Information and Preventing Insider 
Trading" and the "Operational Guidelines for Financial and Business Transactions Among Related Parties." 
These regulations specify confidentiality requirements for material information and apply to directors, 
managers, and all employees. For details on directors' shareholdings, please refer to the 2024 Annual Report.
In 2024, all directors completed a written training program on insider trading prevention.
There were three board resolutions in 2024 where directors duly recused themselves due to conflicts of 
interest. For details on these implementations, please refer to the "Corporate Governance Operations" 
section of the 2024 Annual Report.

▍Board's Continuing Education  GRI 2-17  
Board members actively participated in a variety of training programs covering 
areas such as sustainable operations, ethical governance, investment and 
technology applications, and risk management. These efforts aim to promote 
corporate sustainability, keep abreast of global risk trends, and enhance risk 
response capabilities. In 2024, all directors completed at least six hours of 
training, meeting the requirements set by the competent authority, with a 
100% participation rate, demonstrating the Board's outstanding performance.
▍Board Performance Evaluation  GRI 2-18  
In accordance with Article 3 of BES's "Board Performance Evaluation Guidelines," 
the company conducts an internal performance evaluation of the Board of Directors 
annually and engages an external professional independent institution or team of 
academic experts for an external evaluation at least once every three years. The 
evaluation period covers January 1 to December 31, 2024, and includes the overall 
Board, individual directors, and functional committees. The evaluation is carried 
out through internal self-assessment by the Board of Directors, self-assessment 
by individual directors, peer reviews, and evaluations commissioned to external 
professional institutions.
The evaluation process involves directors and functional committee members 
completing relevant self-assessment questionnaires. Evaluation indicators include:
	 Board of Directors and Functional Committees: 
	
Participation in the company operations, enhancement of decision-making 
quality, board composition and structure, director selection and training, and 
internal control effectiveness. 
	 Individual Board Members：
	
Understanding of Company goals and duties, awareness of responsibilities, level 
of engagement, communication skills, professionalism, ongoing training, and 
familiarity with internal control systems. 
The self-assessment results of BES's Board performance evaluation will be submitted 
to the Board of Directors in the first quarter of 2025. BES continues to evaluate 
appropriate and feasible improvement plans to enhance Board communication and 
professional development for aligning with ESG sustainability principles and goals.
In addition to internal self-assessments, the company also commissions external 
institutions to conduct Board performance evaluations every three years. Since the 
company entrusted the Taiwan Association of Board Governance in 2023 to evaluate 
the effectiveness of Board governance, no external evaluation was conducted in 
2024. The evaluation focused on seven major aspects: "Composition and Structure 
of the Board," "Selection and Ongoing Training of Directors," "Board Participation 
in Company Operations," "Improvement of the Quality of Board Decision-Making," 
"Internal Control," "Environment, Social, and Corporate Governance," and "Value 
Creation." Evaluation results indicated that BES's Board governance and operations 
largely meet the standards set by the Taiwan Stock Exchange and Taipei Exchange 
regarding corporate governance practices and Board evaluation criteria. For full 
evaluation results, please refer to the company's official website.

▍Remuneration Policy for Directors and Managers  GRI 2-19  
The remuneration of BES board members is disclosed annually in the annual report. Directors' remuneration includes fixed "compensation" and variable 
"directors' remuneration." The remuneration is based on the degree of participation in BES's operations, contribution value, and the typical level of 
compensation in other listed companies. According to Article 28 of the company's Articles of Incorporation, directors' remuneration shall not exceed 2% of 
the annual pre-tax profit. Beyond this, there are no other retirement benefits, severance pay, or clawback mechanisms for directors.
The policies, systems, standards, and structures governing the compensation and remuneration of directors and senior managers are established and 
reviewed by the Compensation Committee. This committee consists of independent directors, providing diverse external perspectives and opinions. It 
operates at the same level as the Audit Committee, conducting fair and reasonable deliberations regarding the compensation and remuneration of the 
highest governing body and senior management. In 2024, the committee held eight meetings to review and ensure the competitiveness and fairness 
of compensation and remuneration. The current remuneration policy considers corporate governance and business competitiveness and is formulated 
exclusively by internalstakeholders. The annual compensation for BES's directors includes directors' compensation, salaries, and bonuses (the latter two 
applicable only to those concurrently serving as employees). Compensation for senior managers includes salaries, bonuses, and retirement benefits, all 
of which are disclosed annually in the company's annual report. Furthermore, the annual performance evaluation results for the Board of Directors and 
functional committees have been incorporated as important references for the director nomination mechanism and the formulation of compensation 
policies.
Aside from the provisions mentioned above, there are no other significant special benefits for the company's senior managers. The retirement benefit 
system is the same as that for general employees and is implemented in accordance with legal regulations.
▍Clawback Policy for Improper Gains
To enhance the conduct, ethics, and professionalism of 
the company and its employees, BES has established the 
"BES Employee Rewards and Penalties Regulations." Any 
individual who violates the code of conduct must return 
all improperly obtained gains to the affected party or 
the company. Depending on the severity of the violation, 
disciplinary actions such as salary deductions, demerits, 
or even legal actions may be taken. The company 
expects all employees, including managers, to fulfill their 
responsibilities in management and supervision, strictly 
adhere to professional ethics, and ensure the company's 
sustainable growth and development.
2. Functional Committees  GRI 
2-9  
BES is committed to establishing an effective corporate governance structure to strengthen the 
board's functions, emphasize corporate sustainability, and respect the rights of stakeholders, 
thereby enhancing information transparency. BES established the Compensation Committee 
and the Audit Committee in 2011 and 2017, respectively, and the Sustainable Development 
Committee in 2022 to assist the board in fulfilling its supervisory responsibilities.  Functional 
committees conduct due diligence through diverse communication channels (such as internal 
meetings, questionnaires, document signing, and existing grievance mechanisms). They also 
collect recommendations and feedback from stakeholders on significant events that have 
positive or negative impacts on company operations, using this information to develop, 
approve, and update relevant strategies and policies. The Board of Directors is responsible for 
overseeing the impact management procedures and implementation results of these functional 
committees, and it regularly reviews their execution status during monthly board meetings.

▍Shareholders' Meeting
On May 31, 2024, the company held its Annual 
General Shareholders' Meeting and encouraged 
shareholders to actively participate in the 
election of directors and discussions on proposed 
amendments to the Articles of Incorporation. 
Shareholders were given adequate opportunities to

with the Company Act, the meeting minutes were 
publicly disclosed to ensure timely shareholders 
access to relevant company information. Both the 
English and Chinese versions of the shareholders' 
meeting handbook and the meeting minutes were 
available on the Company's official website.
3. Communication of Critical Concerns  GRI 2-16  
BES identifies significant risk issues in line with its risk management policies and procedures and discloses 
major violations, regulatory breaches, or penalties in accordance with the "Taiwan Stock Exchange 
Corporation Procedures for Verification and Disclosure of Material Information of Companies with Listed 
Securities." In addition, the company classifies environmental incidents financial losses over NTD 500,000, and 
personnel casualties as defined under the Occupational Safety and Health Act, as major events that must be 
reported to and disclosed by the Board of Directors. In 2024, one major occupational safety incident occurred 
involving an external contractor a serious occupational injury. BES promptly initiated procedures and root 
cause analysis, followed by corrective and preventive actions in accordance with the ISO 45001 "Occupational 
Safety and Health Corrective Action Management Process." The incident was continuously tracked during 
quarterly Occupational Safety and Health Committee meeting until resolution, whith preventive measures 
were reinforced during monthly coordination meetings. In response, management reviewed and revised 
operating procedures, enhanced hazard identification and risk management in line with occupational safety 
and health regulations and promoted overall awareness of occupational safety.

Remuneration Strategy
2.2 
▍	Remuneration Policy for the Highest Governing 
Body  GRI 2-19  
The remuneration of BES board members is disclosed 
annually in the annual report. Directors' remuneration 
consists of a fixed component (compensation) and a variable 
component (directors' remuneration). Remuneration is based 
on the director’slevel of of involvement in BES operations, 
individual contribution, and prevailing compensation 
benchmarks among listed companies. According to Article 
28 of the company's Articles of Incorporation, directors' 
remuneration shall not exceed 2% of the annual pre-
tax profit. No additional retirement benefits, severance 
payments, or clawback mechanisms are provided to 
directors.
Annual performance evaluation of the Board of Directors 
and functional committees are used askey references in 
director nominations mechanism and compensation policy 
formulation.
▍	Remuneration Determination Process
	
GRI 2-20  
BES has established a Compensation Committee under the 
Board of Directors, functioning at the same hierarchical 
level as the Audit Committee. Composed of independent 
directors, it is responsible for fair and reasonable 
deliberation and decision-making on remuneration of the 
highest governing body and senior executives. The current 
remuneration policy considers both corporate governance 
and business competitiveness, and is determined exclusively 
by internal related parties.
▍Annual Total Compensation Ratio  GRI 2-21  
In 2024, the ratio of the annual total compensation increased for BES's highest-paid 
individual to the median increase in annual total compensation for other employees in 
Taiwan (excluding the highest-paid individual) was 1.97. This marks a notable decrease 
from the 2.56 ratio recorded in 2023, primarily due to an increase in the median total 
compensation for general employees, resulting from annual salary adjustments and the 
issuance of surplus bonuses from construction projects.
▍Link Between Remuneration and ESG
BES refines its remuneration policies for the Board of Directors and senior management 
by considering indicators related to the organization's economic, environmental, and 
social impact goals and performance. To encourage senior managers to work toward 
the company's sustainable development objectives, the Board of Directors and the 
Compensation Committee revised the "BES Employee Performance Evaluation and 
Promotion Regulations" in 2024, formally linking senior managers' compensation to 
sustainability performance. This revision recognizes senior managers' contributions 
to corporate sustainability in areas such as legal compliance, workplace inclusion, risk 
management, employee health and safety, labor relations, and carbon emission reduction.

Impact 
Assessment
Positive Impacts: 	 Providing departments with financial performance analysis, meeting the needs of internal and external parties for reliable information on 
sustainable operations. The stronger a company's financial stability and risk-bearing capacity, the more likely it is to secure funding support.
Negative Impacts: 	Affecting stock prices, reduces external shareholder investment willingness, and makes financing more difficult to obtain.
Policies and 
Commitments
Policies
1.	 Carbon Emissions and Resource Management: As the construction industry 
is a sector with higher carbon emissions, it should report greenhouse gas 
emissions and disclose the financial impacts of energy-saving and emission-
reduction measures.
2.	 Green Building Materials and Supply Chain Management: Monitoring 
suppliers' ESG performance, for example, the use of low-carbon cement, 
recycled construction materials, and reduction of construction waste, and 
ensure that financial budgets support the procurement of sustainable 
materials.
3.	 Establishing rigorous cost control procedures to enhance project profitability.
Commitments
1.	 Promoting diversity and inclusion (D&I) to ensure financial decisions 
do not cause negative social impacts.
2.	 Promoting fair trade within the supply chain, ensuring that contractors 
and suppliers comply with ESG principles.
3.	 Preparing construction budgets in accordance with the company's 
"Construction Budget and Settlement Guidelines" as a basis for cost 
control and performance evaluation during project execution. Monthly 
cost reviews are conducted based on approved budgets, and profit-
and-loss analysis reports are compiled in real time to reflect the current 
financial status of each project.
Responsible 
Unit
The Finance and Accounting Departments are responsible for the accuracy and timeliness of financial data. The Management Department coordinates the 
analysis of operational results, while the Board of Directors, as the highest governance body, oversees and adjusts strategy.
Indicators and 
Goals
Short-Term (2025)

and cost control management system:
1.	Establishing a monthly review process for cash levels and 
financial ratio adequacy, and implement review for 12 times.
2.	100% of submitting and reviewing of monthly performance 
reports on project budget execution (including cost control 
profit and loss analysis, construction expense and work-in-
progress cost variance trends, and value per man-month 
reports).
3.	Reviewing estimated revenue and cost changes monthly 
in response to changes in the construction price index and 
assess their impact on project profitability.
4.	Conducting an annual review report on cost control and 
performance execution, and report related improvement 
measures to operations management.
5.	Maintaining ongoing profitability.
Mid-Term (2030)

risk indicators and finance:
1.	Developing a performance tracking SOP or 
procedural document covering cash level adequacy, 
financial ratios, budget, and financial risks (including 
climate risks).
2.	Disclosing information in accordance with IFRS 
S1/S2 standards, with to third-party review, and 
integrating into the annual report.
3.	Establishing a sustainable capital expenditure 
review mechanism including ESG or low-carbon 
indicators, and conduct one review.

operations system and complete an integrated 
cost process manual.

2024 Annual 
Actions
The "Cash Flow Collection Alert" feature in the communication app provides real-time notifications to relevant personnel on upcoming and overdue accounts 
receivable, including dates and amounts, thereby improving the efficiency and oversight of cash flow management.
Monthly reviews of each project's budget execution performance are conducted, linking cost control profit and loss analyses to an intelligent decision-making 
platform, where the project's financial data is visualized. Modules and reports are generated (including cost management, construction price index, and man-
month productivity analysis). The operations material management system has been improved by adding self-issued material requisition forms and supplier 
codes to facilitate material usage statistics.
Communication 
with Stakeholders
Communication with banks is conducted from time to time via phone, email, or in-person visits. Financial reports are provided quarterly to investors, regulatory 
bodies, and supply chain partners through the company's official website or the Market Observation Post System, and through investor conferences, shareholders' 
meetings, and press releases to ensure stakeholders have timely access to financial information. There is also active communication with the site office employees 
through periodic social media announcements of operational regulations. The company uses a real-time command center and on-site inspections to monitor cost 
control operations at site offices, aiming to manage costs and enhance project profitability.
▍Financial Management Process and Responsible Units
The management of BES's financial performance is primarily divided between the Finance Department and the Accounting 
Department under the Management Department. The Finance Department is responsible for the overall procurement and 
allocation of operating funds, as well as assisting the company's various investment ventures with financial planning and cash 
flow control, ensuring capital efficiency and manageable financial risks. The Accounting Department is responsible for preparing 
financial statements, tax filings, budget control, and providing management accounting information. It also coordinates the 
consolidation of subsidiary financial statements to facilitate operational analysis. Through collaboration between these two 
departments, the company is able to maintain a sound financial status and support its goals of sustainable operation.
▍Cost Control and Resource Allocation Mechanism
To enhance overall financial performance and operational efficiency, BES has each business unit prepare cost budgets and 
monitor execution based on project type, construction progress, and market conditions. The Finance Department and the Cost 
Estimation and Control Department are jointly responsible for overall resource allocation and the review of major expenditures 
to manage financial risk. Rolling adjustments and analyses are carried out based on variances between actual revenue 
and budget. The Management Department also conducts regular reviews of departmental operating results to reinforce a 
performance-oriented management model.
Each month, the Site offices of BES update cost control tables, which are reviewed by the Cost Estimation and Control 
Department. The department also conducts cost reviews and evaluations during each project's execution phase. Close 
communication is maintained with the offices, and operational guidelines are promoted through social media on an ad hoc 
basis. A real-time video command center and on-site inspections are used to manage cost control operations of the Site 
offices, with the goal of controlling costs and improving project profitability.

vision of "creating a sustainable 
environment, building livable housing, 
and establishing a strong presence 
in international markets." We remain 
committed to reform, innovation, and 
sustainable management by establishing 
four major profit centers: "Public Works," 
"Private Projects," "Real Estate Business," 
and "Overseas Business." Through 
vertical integration of related industry 
chains and horizontal collaboration 
across sectors, the company consolidates 
resources to maximize profitability, 
driving continuous growth and progress.

2.4
▍	Tax Policy, Governance, and Risk Management 
BES adheres to principles of tax and financial 
compliance, as well as corportat social responsibility, 
aiming to create corporate value and establish a sound 
tax risk management. The company has built a robust 
financial and tax management system and a culture 
of tax governance, supported by swift and effective 
procedures. BES undertakes construction projects 
across northern, central, and southern Taiwan. In line 
with the government's New Southbound Policy, the 
company is activelyexpanding its overseas operations. 
The company monitors changes in tax policies across 
various countries and assesses the potential tax risks 
associated with local operations.
▍	Tax Governance Structure and Responsibilities
The Board of Directors servers as the highest decision-
making entity for establishing an effective tax risk 
management mechanism at BES. Based on the overall 
business strategy and operating environment, the 
Board reviews and approves the company's tax 
governance on an annual basis as submitted by the 
Finance and Accounting Departments, to ensure the 
effective operation of the tax management system. The 
Finance and Accounting Departments are designated 
as the tax management units responsible for policy 
implementation and oversight.
Finance and Accounting Departments are the designated 
unit responsible for handling and managing tax affairs."
▍Sales Department's Operational Development Overview
Each division, based on the nature of its operations, has a critical impact on BES's financial 
performance. The Civil Engineering Division and Private Engineering Division are the main 
sources of BES's revenue. The Civil Engineering Division continues to pursue major government 
infrastructure projects such as rail, water environments, urban and rural development, and green 
energy engineering. The Private Engineering Division expands a diverse range of building products 
and technologies through both in-house development and external contracting, enhancing project 
quality and brand value. The Real Estate Division is responsible for domestic real estate and industrial 
park development, promoting the activation and acquisition of medium- to large-scale land and 
through methods such as urban renewal, joint construction, public bidding, and industrial park 
planning. Recent strategies have focused on risk diversification and resource sharing by forming 
strategic alliances or joint ventures with industry peers to jointly improve development efficiency 
and revenue stability.
