Environmental Friendliness and Green Engineering
Happy Workplace and Social Impact
3. Commercial Substance
Corporate structures and transactions are based on genuine commercial substance. BES does not engage in tax 
arrangements intended solely to avoid tax liabilities, nor does it shift profits to low-tax jurisdictions for the purpose of 
tax avoidance.
Related-party transactions follow the arm's length principle, and BES is committed to complying with transfer pricing 
regulations in all jurisdictions where it operates, fulfilling tax obligations in jurisdictions where value is created.
Based on trust, transparency, and legal compliance, BES maintains relationships with tax authorities in an honest, 
respectful, fair, and ethical manner, proactively disclosing significant tax matters and contributing to the improvement 
of the tax environment and regulatory framework.
4. Open Communication
Transactions between related parties comply with the transfer pricing principles published by the Organization for 
Economic Co-operation and Development (OECD), as well as the regulations outlined in the Base Erosion and Profit 
Shifting (BEPS) Action Plan.
BES published by relationships of mutual trust and open communication with tax authorities in all jurisdictions 
where it operates, providing industry perspectives and professional insights to support the enhancement ofthe tax 
environment and system.
5.  Risk Management
BES has established a robust tax risk control framework and organizational culture. It considers the overall optimization 
of the company's tax burden, risk control, and sustainable value. Tax risks and corresponding measures are carefully 
assessed. In line with BES's internal control and Risk management processes, tax-related risks are identified, evaluated, 
and managed, and appropriate measurement, management, and control measures are proposed. These matters are 
submitted by the Finance and Accounting Departments to the Audit Committee, or discussed by the Risk Management 
Committee, and subsequently reported to the Board of Directors.
▍	Communication Guidelines with Tax-Related Stakeholders
BES's primary tax-related stakeholders are governmental tax authorities. All tax filings and payments are conducted 
in full compliance with the laws and regulations of each jurisdiction. When uncertainties arise in the application of 
tax laws during daily operations, the company either communicates directly with the relevant authorities or consults 
through Deloitte Taiwan to determine appropriate solutions.
In the event of a tax audit, BES promptly prepares the required documentation and fully cooperates with the 
authorities.
To ensure transparency in its tax governance policies, BES also discloses relevant tax information to 
other stakeholders—such as shareholders and investors—via the stakeholder section of its official 
website, the annual report, and the general shareholders' meeting. Furthermore, BES has established 
reporting and whistleblowing channels for issues related to ethics and anti-corruption, which also 
accept tax-related concerns. For more details, please refer to the section on Integrity Management 
and Anti-Corruption.
▍	Tax Governance Policy, Controls, 
and Risk Management
BES's tax governance is grounded in transparency 
and legal compliance. The followingoutlines the 
tax policies and code of conduct uphold by BES:
1.  Legal Compliance
BES is committed to complying with local 
tax laws and legislative intent at all of its 
operating locations, as well as adhering to 
international tax standards. In response to 
changes in tax legislation and sustainability-
related regulations, BES promptly evaluates their 
impact on the company and adopts appropriate 
countermeasures, while considering the 
company's sustainability development goals.
Taxes are calculated accurately, declared, and 
paid within statutory deadlines, fulfilling the 
company's tax obligations. 
BES continuously gathers and monitors updates 
to tax regulations across various countries and 
jurisdictions. All tax filings are handled by local, 
reputable accounting firms. Annually, financial 
data is submitted to Deloitte Taiwan for tax return 
filing, and tax-related information is disclosed 
in financial statements and the annual report in 
accordance with financial reporting standards 
and regulatory requirements.
2.  Information Transparency
BES ensures the transparency in its tax reporting, 
including country-by-country reports, master 
files, and transfer pricing reports.
BES uses legal and transparent tax incentives and 
does not exploit tax benefits in ways that violate 
the spirit of the law.

SDGs
SDG 8 Decent Work & Economic Growth
SDG 12 Responsible Consumption and Production
SDG 16 Peace Justice and Strong Institutions
Impact 
Assessment
Positive Impacts:	
Establishing a robust compliance mechanism helps mitigate legal risks, enhances the company's sustainable image, attract investor and 
stakeholder support, and foster long-term stable development.
Negative Impacts:	
1.	Increased Compliance Costs: Establishing and maintaining a robust compliance mechanism requires substantial resource investment (e.g., system setup, personnel 
training), which may increase operational costs and impact short-term financial performance.
2.	Regulatory Interpretation and Implementation Challenges: Failure to interpret relevant regulations accurately or in a timely manner might lead to delays in 
adjusting internal policies, increasing the risk of non-compliance or regulatory penalties.
3.	Employee Adaptation Pressure: Frequent regulatory updates and training sessions may place additional pressure on employees, especially during peak periods, 
potentially reducing work efficiency or leading to internal resistance.
4.	Amplified Reputational Risk: Failure to meet promised sustainability image or committed performance targets (e.g., failure to achieve ESG goals) may lead to 
stakeholder skepticism and harm corporate trust.
Policies and 
Commitments
1.	Monitor and track the progress and direction of policy and regulatory changes related to the company's operations. Identify relevant changes and assess their 
potential impact to ensure all business activities comply with the latest regulatory requirements. 
2.	Implement the company's compliance system, regularly update and assist departments in promoting integrity management and anti-corruption policies. 
Strengthen occupational safety and health measures, ensure strong protection of labor rights, and support the development of a friendly workplace environment. 
3.	Assist all departments in reducing significant non-compliance in their business activities, identify and manage key risks, and ensure the timely and accuracy 
disclosure of relevant information to safeguard the company's reputation. 
Responsible Unit
The Legal Department monitors legal developments, assists with contract reviews, manages legal disputes and litigation, collaborates with various departments on 
regulatory audits and compliance reviews, and provides legal analysis, opinions, and recommendations on potential risks or disputes.
Indicators and 
Goals
Short-Term (2025)
1.	 Continuously monitor legal developments and 
provide monthly updates via the company's internal 
system to raise employee awareness or notify relevant 
departments for their attention and assessment.
2.	 Regularly conduct internal legal training to enhance 
employees' legal awareness and support departments 
in strengthening communication with suppliers and 
stakeholders.
3.	 Optimize the risk assessment management 
framework by continuously supporting departments 
in identifying relevant regulations for their operations, 
conducting compliance reviews, and developing and 
updating internal policies. These efforts aim to reduce 
major instances of non-compliance and legal risk, and 
to ensures timely disclosure of significant lawsuits 
and disputes for accurate information reporting.
Mid-Term (2030)
1.	 Continuously monitor and update legal developments 
and issue monthly updates through the company's 
internal system for employee awareness or notify 
relevant departments for their attention and assessment.
2.	 Regularly conduct internal legal training to enhance 
employees' legal awareness and supportt departments 
in strengthening communication with suppliers and 
stakeholders. Participation compliance-related courses 
at headquarters continues annually.
3.	 Optimize the risk assessment management framework 
by continuously supporting departments in identifying 
applicable regulations for their operations, conducting 
compliance reviews, and developing and updating internal 
policies. These efforts aim to reduce major non-compliance 
and legal risk incidents, and ensures timely and accurate 
disclosure of significant lawsuits and disputes.
Long-Term (2030-)
1.	 Continuously enhance the monitoring and updating of 
legal changes, publishing updates via the company's 
internal system to raise employee awareness or notify 
relevant departments for timely evaluation. 
2.	 Condduct internal training at least once a year 
to support departments in enhancing internal 
communication and system implementation. These 
efforts improve compliance with relevant legal 
requirements among employees and suppliers, 
strengthen the company's compliance management 
capacity, and reduce operational risks. 
3.	 Continuously refine the assessment framework to 
anticipate legal risks. Support departments in identifying 
applicable regulations, conducting compliance reviews, 
and updating internal policies to reduce major non-
compliance and safety incidents. Ensure timely and 
accurate disclosure of significant lawsuits and disputes.

▍	Explanation of Violations and Subsequent Improvements 
	
GRI 2-27   SASB
 IF-EN-160a.1  IF-EN-250a.2   
BES defines as major incidests any environmental violations that result in fines exceeding NTD 500,000, or 
occuptational accidents as "major" under Article 37, Paragraph 2 of Occupational Safety and Health Act. This 
also includes case where fines exceeding 50% of the maximum statutory amount, or a single fine surpasses 
NTD 1,000,000 -whichever is greater. We also analyze all cases of fines and penalties, any case determined to have a 
significant impact on the company's business or finances is classified as a major incident. BES Engineering will place 
these cases under enhanced tracking until improvements are completed, and will simultaneously improve related 
operational procedures to prevent recurrence.
In 2024, BES incurred a total of 24 fines related to environmental violations, covering areas such as air pollution, 
water pollution, waste management, and noise control. The total fine amount reached NTD 606,400, marking an 
increase compared to NTD 597,350 in 2022 and NTD 138,500 in 2023. BES has taken active for improvement, such 
as enhancing site patrols and acquiring equipment for dust suppression. Over the past three years, BES has not 
been subject to any major environmental violations or significant penalties for pollution.
In 2024, BES incurred 25 penalties to social issue (e.g., violations of the Labor Standards Act or the Occupational 
Safety and Health Act), with total amount of fines exceeding those of the previous two years. This increase is 
attributed to several projects entering the construction phase, during which BES strengthened relevant training and 
improvement measures. In addition, one major occupational injury was reported. The total amount of social-related 
fines reached NTD 3,500,000.
▍Overview of BES Legal Compliance Training Over Past Three Years
In 2024, BES commissioned an external attorney to conduct an Integrity Management Seminar, attended by 145 participants. In addition, 
22 sessions of the "Basic Legal Concepts and Case Analysis for Engineering" course were conducted.

Risk Management (Material Topic)
2.6
The construction industry faces significantly higher risks than other sectors, and companies often encounter various uncertainties during operations. To 
prevent losses caused by such risks, BES has established an integrated risk management policy and procedures that address economic, environmental, 
social, and climate change factors. Depending on the level of crisis, emergency response meetings are promptly convened following the risk management 
process to formulate appropriate strategies and action plans. These measures effectively address and review risk events, prevent recurrence, and mitigate 
potential impacts.
Material Topic Management Approach
SDGs
SDG 16 Peace Justice and Strong Institutions
Impact 
Assessment
Positive Impacts: 	 Proper management and prevention of operational risks help achieve optimal benefits within acceptable risk levels.
Negative Impacts:	 Unidentified emerging risks or uncontrollable factors, such as supply chain disruptions caused by wars/pandemics, leading to financial or 
reputational losses for the company.
Policies and 
Commitments
Policy
BES's risk management policies and procedures, approved during the 26th meeting of the 4th Board of Directors, are based on the company's overall 
operational guidelines. They establish a risk management mechanism that identifies early, measures accurately, supervises effectively, and strictly controls risks 
to prevent potential losses within acceptable risk levels. This mechanism is continuously refined in response to internal and external changes to safeguard the 
interests of employees, shareholders, customers, and stakeholders, enhance company value, and ensure optimal resource allocation. To prevent various risks 
that may arise during operations, BES formulates corresponding risk response strategies and mitigation measures according to different crisis levels. When a 
risk occurs, the responsible unit promptly reports it through the chain of command and initiates mitigation measures to minimize its impact on the company. In 
Post-incident review stage, a review plan is proposed as a reference for future risk response.
Responsible 
Unit
The board of directors is the highest management unit for the company's risk management. The Audit Committee also serves as the supervisory unit for the 
company's risk management.
Indicators and 
Goals
Management 
Review 
Mechanism
The Risk Management Group is primarily responsible for the execution-level tasks of monitoring, measuring, and assessing company risks. It exercises its duties 
independently from business units and operational activities and reports to the Audit Committee and the Board of Directors annually.
Evaluations of the implementation of risk management are conducted by internal audit personnel to assess whether risk management is effectively executed, 
ensuring proper enforcement and compliance with the system.
2024 Annual 
Actions
The risk management strategy identifies risks across three dimensions: economic, environmental, and social, as key indicators. A total of 30 risks have been 
identified for strategic planning and management.
Communication 
with 
Stakeholders
Relevant stakeholders include investors/shareholders, clients/owners, employees, suppliers, community, government agencies, investment institutions/banks, 
and media. Communication is conducted regularly/on an ad hoc basis in various forms.
Short-Term (2025)
Continue conducting regular annual risk 
identification, with the Risk Management Group 
convening meetings and reporting to the Audit 
Committee and the Board of Directors.
Mid-Term (2030)
Continue conducting regular annual risk 
identification, with the Risk Management Group 
convening meetings and reporting to the Audit

Continue conducting regular annual risk

convening meetings and reporting to the Audit

▍Risk Management Policy   GRI 2-23  
The "BES Risk Management Policy and Procedures" were approved at 
the fourth meeting of the 26th Board of Directors and underwent a 
strategic update in 2024. Based on the company's overall operational 
strategy, the policy systematically defines various types of risks 
and establishes a management mechanism for early identification, 
accurate assessment, effective supervision, and strict control, aiming 
to prevent potential losses within an acceptable risk range. The 
company will continue to refine its risk management practices in 
response to internal and external environmental changes, striving 
to protect the rights and interests of employees, shareholders, 
customers, and all stakeholders, enhance corporate value, and 
achieve optimal resource allocation.
▍Risk Management Organizational Structure
The Board of Directors serves as the highest authority in the 
company's risk management organizational structure. Its 
responsibilities include ensuring regulatory compliance, promoting 
and implementing comprehensive risk management, identifying 
operational risks, ensuring risk control effectiveness, and assuming 
ultimate responsibility. 
The Board of Directors supervises the Risk Management Group, which 
is led by the most senior manager of the Management Department. 
Managers from other departments serve as core members and 
actively identify and manage risks throughout the company's 
operations. The Risk Management Group conducts quantitative 
analysis of business risks to assist in formulating risk management 
policies and response strategies, which are then submitted to the 
Board of Directors. A risk management report is presented to the 
Audit Committee and the Board at least once a year.
Each manager of the functional unit is responsible for risk 
management within their respective operations. This includes 
regularly analyzing and monitoring relevant risks, and ensuring the 
effective implementation of risk control mechanisms and procedures.
On November 26, 2024, BES held a risk management meeting 
and identified 30 high-risk issues, along with ongoing mitigation 
measures. These were reported to the Audit Committee on December 
24, 2024, and to the Board of Directors on December 26, 2024, to 
ensure thorough implementation.
▍Risk Management Process
Risk management at BES involves the following steps: risk identification, risk measurement, risk 
monitoring, and risk response. The company's risk management process includes identifying risk 
issues, analyzing risks, assessing risks, responding to risks, and preparing risk reports and disclosures.
BES identifies risks across three dimensions—economic, environmental, and social—while also 
factoring in the company's size, industry and business characteristics, operational activities, and overall 
sustainability strategy. These assessments are categorized according to the following risk types.

▍Risk Matrix
Based on the identified risk issues, BES analyzes and assesses the likelihood (low, medium, high) and severity (minor to very severe) of their impact. 
According to the quantitative results, a risk matrix is developed, and high-risk issues (indicated in red in the diagram) are identified. Appropriate response 
measures are then implemented to mitigate potential losses resulting from these risks.

The bidding team conducts detailed schedule evaluation and planning for construction periods. For projects that cannot meet the unfeasible 
schedules, a no-bid strategy is adopted, accompanied by a clarification statement. Bids are submitted only after the contracting authority 
adjusts the project duration to ensure the feasibility of the timeline and further reduce schedule risks.

Surging prices and increasing 
procurement/ contracting costs
1. 	Conduct rolling monthly reviews of rebar demand for each construction project. Weekly rebar meetings analyze domestic and

facilitate cost reductions.

and price negotiation.
5. 	In addition to executing monthly cost control for project orders and enhancing profit-and-loss reporting, a real-time cost variance 
statistical function has been added to the existing operations management system to boost cost control efficiency and facilitate 
immediate detection of anomalies.

carbon emissions.

Integrity Management and Anti‑Corruption Prevention (Material Topic)
2.7
Material Topic Management Approach
SDGs
SDG 16 Peace Justice and Strong Institutions
Impact 
Assessment
Positive Impacts：	 Corporate governance is the foundation of corporate management. BES operates under the principles of steady business, honesty, and integrity, 
while establishing a sound governance framework and promoting related initiatives to safeguard the rights and interests of all stakeholders.
Negative Impacts：	Poor corporate governance can lead to internal corruption and misconduct, erode investor trust and shareholder rights, and damage corporate 
image and reputation. In the event of serious legal violations, brand reputation and value may suffer, potentially affecting market value and 
incurring fines.
Policies and 
Commitments
Policy
To establish a corporate culture of integrity and effective management mechanisms, BES has 
formulated the "Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice of BES Engineering Corporation" 
and the "Procedures and Behavior Guidelines for Integrity Management" by referring to the "Ethical 
Corporate Management Best Practice Principles for TWSE/GTSM Listed Companies." These have 
been approved by the Board of Directors. These codes and guidelines clearly outline precautions 
to be taken by BES's employees during business execution to actively prevent dishonest behavior, 
including corruption, bribery, and fraud. They explicitly prohibit giving or receiving bribes, making 
illegal political donations, improper charitable donations or sponsorships, offering unreasonable gifts 
or hospitality, infringing intellectual property rights, or engaging in unfair competition. The company 
also educates employees on preventive measures, complaint channels, and internal disciplinary 
procedures to protect employees from illegal conduct, prevent corporate asset loss and damage to 
the company's reputation, and safeguard customer interests. Moreover, these integrity management 
policies are published in internal regulations, the annual report, and the company's website so that 
managers, employees, suppliers, customers, and other business-related entities and individuals can 
understand BES's integrity principles and standards.
Commitment
In accordance with the "Ethical Corporate Management 
Code of Practice of BES Engineering Corporation" and 
"Procedures and Behavior Guidelines for Integrity 
Management," if any employee commits any of the 
following actions and is found to be true, the company 
will, depending on the severity, impose administrative 
penalties, recover improper gains, or pursue legal 
responsibility in order to protect the company's reputation 
and rights:
 Engaging in private gain or fraud, embezzling public 
property, or accepting bribes.
 Abusing their position to seek personal or others' 
benefits.
 Operating outside businesses that seriously affect the 
company's interests.
Responsible 
Unit
The core members of the BES Integrity Management Group are from the Chairman President Office, Audit Office, Human Resources Department, Strategic 
Development Office, and Legal Department. They are responsible for revising the Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice of BES Engineering Corporation 
and Procedures and Behavior Guidelines for Ethical Corporate Management, conducting internal awareness campaigns, and providing training. They also report 
regularly to the Board of Directors. The Audit Office is in charge of supervising and assisting the Board of Directors and management departments in auditing and 
assessing whether the preventive measures established for integrity management are effectively implemented.
Indicators and 
Goals
BES has identified the signing of integrity declarations, educational promotions on the Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice of BES Engineering 
Corporation, and the signing of commitment letters by key suppliers to comply with BES's Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice as key management 
indicators and objectives for this material topic.
Short-Term (2025)
1.	100% of directors, appointed managers, and 
employees sign the integrity declaration.
2.	80% participation rate in educational promotions on 
the Integrity Management Code of Practice.
3.	75% of key suppliers sign the "Supplier Code of 
Conduct Commitment Letter" of BES (including 
integrity management requirements).
Mid-Term (2030)
1.	100% of directors, appointed managers, and 
employees sign the integrity declaration.
2.	90% participation rate in educational promotions on 
the Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice.
3.	95% of key suppliers sign the "Supplier Code of 
Conduct Commitment Letter" of BES.
Long-Term (2030-)
1.	100% of directors, appointed managers, and 
employees sign the integrity declaration.
2.	100% participation rate in educational promotions on 
the Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice.
3.	95% of key suppliers sign the "Supplier Code of 
Conduct Commitment Letter" of BES.

1.BES's Internal Control and Audit Mechanism
▍Internal Audit Organization
BES has established a dedicated internal audit unit that reports 
directly to the Board of Directors and is supervised by independent 
directors on the Audit Committee. The head of the Audit Department 
is responsible for planning and executing audit activities. In addition 
to reporting monthly audit findings to each independent director, 
the audit head also attends and presents reports at meetings of 
Audit Committee and Board of Directors meetings. The audit unit 
assists the Board of Directors and management in inspecting and 
reviewing deficiencies in the internal control system and evaluating 
the effectiveness and efficiency of operations. They provide timely 
recommendations for improvements to ensure the ongoing 
effectiveness of the internal control system, which also serves as the 
basis for periodic review and revision.

▍Internal audit operations
The audit unit assists the Board of Directors and management in 
identifying and addressing deficiencies in the internal control system, 
evaluating the effectiveness and efficiency of operations, ensuring 
the reliability, timeliness, transparency, and compliance of reports 
with relevant regulations and laws. The audit unit provides timely 
improvement suggestions to ensure the continuous and effective 
implementation of the internal control system and to serve as the basis 
for reviewing and revising the internal control system.
The audit unit considers the characteristics of the business, 
organizational size, and potential risks to draft an annual audit plan 
approved by the Board of Directors. This plan is used to inspect the 
internal control systems of the company's various units and subsidiaries, 
with work papers and related materials attached to create audit reports. 
For deficiencies and abnormalities found in the internal control system 
during inspections, they are disclosed in the audit report, tracked after this 
report is submitted, and follow-up reports are prepared at least quarterly 
until improvements are completed. This ensures that relevant units have 
taken appropriate improvement measures in a timely manner and includes 
these measures as key performance evaluation items for each unit.
After the audit report and follow-up report are submitted, they should 
be delivered to the Audit Committee's independent directors for review 
by the end of the month following the completion of the audit item. If 
significant violations or major harm to the company are discovered, a 
report should be immediately submitted and the Audit Committee's 
independent directors notified.
	Self-Assessment Operations: 
	
To implement the company's self-monitoring mechanism and 
promptly respond to environmental changes by adjusting the 
design and implementation of the internal control system, as well 
as to enhance the quality and efficiency of audits, each unit and 
subsidiary of BES must conduct a self-assessment operation at least 
once a year. The audit unit reviews the self-assessment reports and 
the improvements of internal control deficiencies and abnormalities 
found by the audit unit. These serve as the primary basis for 
the Board of Directors and the President to evaluate the overall 
effectiveness of the internal control system and to issue the internal 
control statement.
	Operational Basis: 
	
BES's internal control system, internal audit system, and internal 
control system self-assessment operation management measures.
2. 	BES's Risk Assessment for Integrity Management
	
GRI 205-1   SASB  IF-EN-510a.1
To establish corporate ethics and strengthen corporate governance, BES has formulated the 
"Ethical Corporate Management Code of Practice of BES Engineering Corporation" and the 
"Procedures and Behavior Guidelines for Ethical Corporate Management" in reference to the 
"Ethical Corporate Management Best Practice Principles for TWSE/GTSM Listed Companies." 
These were approved by the board of directors. These regulations specify the matters that 
employees should pay attention to when performing their duties, actively preventing dishonest 
behaviors including corruption, bribery, and fraud. BES promotes prevention measures, complaint 
channels, and relevant internal disciplinary measures to protect employees from illegal activities, 
avoid asset losses and damage to the company's reputation, and safeguard customer rights. BES 
has established an Integrity Management Group, primarily composed of representatives from 
the Board of Directors Office, Audit Office, Human Resources Department, Strategy Development 
Office, and Legal Department. This Group is responsible for revising the procedures and behavior 
guidelines for ethical corporate management, conducting internal promotion activities, providing 
education and training, overseeing the signing of integrity management declarations, and 
regularly reporting to the board of directors on the implementation of integrity management.
BES has completed a comprehensive assessment of corruption-related risks at all operating 
locations. According to BES's internal control system and the self-assessment operation 
management guidelines, self-assessments are conducted annually in January. Each first- and 
second-level unit must perform at least one self-assessment annually in accordance with the audit 
procedures outlined in the "Internal Audit Implementation Rules of BES," evaluating their respective 
responsibilities and internal control systems. These assessments are subsequently reviewed by the 
Audit Office serve as the basis for evaluating the overall effectiveness of the company's internal 
control system. These self-assessments must be documented and retained, along with the reports 
and related materials, for a minimum of five years. Supervisors of primary units, financial and 
accounting supervisors, internal audit supervisors, and directors should complete the "Internal 
Control Component Assessment Form." All self-assessment operations should comply with the 
five components of internal control stipulated by the Financial Supervisory Commission: "Control 
Environment, Risk Assessment, Control Activities, Information and Communication, Monitoring 
Activities and their Judgment Items," and rigorously review the related internal control systems, 
including whether the system design is appropriate and whether the actual implementation results are 
effective. 
According to the evaluation results of the above process, BES's corruption risk has been 
adequately controlled, and no significant risks were found. The company conducts risk assessments 
for the annual audit plan (including internal control items for anti-corruption prevention audits). 
In 2024, BES conducted a comprehensive corruption risk assessment covering all operating 
locations, including headquarters and all active site offices, achieving 100% coverage.
In addition, according to the 2024 overall operational risk items and the risk management report 
from the Risk Assessment Team, a total of 129 operational risk items were assessed, of which 49 
were identified as potential high-risk, accounting for 38%. These high-risk items will be prioritized 
in the 2025 audit plan as key subjects for mandatory annual review.

3. BES Integrity Management Anti‑Corruption 
Communication and Education and Training  GRI 205-2
BES upholds integrity management in all business activities, 
adhering to high ethical standards and maintaining a zero-tolerance 
stance against corruption and bribery. In addition to establishing 
integrity-related policies with clear anti‑corruption and anti‑bribery 
guidelines, BES provides communication channels and training 
to employees and business partners to help prevent bribery and 
corruption.
Estimated Distribution of Risk Levels in Operational Items for 
2025 Based on the 2024 Risk Assessment
▍Anti-Corruption Communication Mechanisms
In 2024, BES informed its board members and managers each quarter based on 
notifications from the Taiwan Stock Exchange, about common issues related to 
insider shareholding change disclosures that violated securities regulations. This 
communication drove the 9 directors and 19 appointed managers (100% of the 
governance-level group) to properly file shareholding change reports as required. 
BES also regularly emailed all employees to promote the concept that "anti-corruption 
is everyone's responsibility," and 100% of directors and employees signed the 
integrity management declarations.
BES continues to require suppliers to sign the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment 
Letter" when entering into procurement contracts, in order to implement responsible 
business practices. The Letter explicitly includes integrity-related requirements, 
prohibiting suppliers from directly or in18directly providing, receiving, promising, 
or requesting improper benefits to obtain or maintain personal gain, and requiring 
compliance with government laws and regulations. In 2024, 99% of key suppliers 
signed the Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter. BES also uses an 
assessment system to continuously manage and evaluate suppliers, for detailed 
procedures please see the "Supplier Sustainability Management" section.
▍Anti‑Corruption Education and Training
BES regularly conducts educational training on integrity management topics, 
delivering in-house or commissioned governance and anti‑corruption courses each 
year to employees at headquarters and all construction sites.
The integrity-related courses are updated annually and promoted to directors, 
managers, and employees as follows:
	In 2024, orientation for new employees included training on integrity policies and 
whistleblowing channels, totaling 372 participants.
	Headquarters hosted an on-site seminar, recorded the session as an online course, 
and produced an AI promotional video titled "The Path of Integrity" to reinforce 
integrity principles and strengthen corporate governance and risk management 
mechanisms. In 2024, a total of 2,986 participants completed the training, 
including: 1,468 from headquarters and site offices; 795 Thai employees; 709 from 
subsidiaries (CKSGuard, Coreasia, CMK Theatres); and 14 from the Vietnam office. 
The training participation rate for all BES employees reached 100%.
None of the BES's disclosed operating locations in 2024 were 
found to be located in any of the 20 lowest-ranked countries on 
the 2024 Transparency International's Corruption Perception Index.

4. 	BES Integrity Management and 
Anti‑Corruption Complaint Mechanism 
GRI 2-26
▍	Guidelines for Reporting Violations of 
Integrity Management
Integrity and responsible business conduct are the foundation 
of the Company's sustainable operations. To implement its 
integrity policies, BES provides a comprehensive complaints 
mechanism. If a complaint regarding improper business 
conduct is received, the Audit Office handles it confidentially 
and commits to protecting the whistleblower from dismissal, 
demotion, salary reduction, deprivation of legal, contractual, 
or customary rights, or other adverse actions related to the 
reported matter.
BES has issued the "Guidelines for Reporting Violations of 
Integrity Management." The designated office for handling 
reports is the Audit Office, and the guidelines specify 
dedicated hotlines, email, and fax. According to BES's 
reporting system, anonymous reports are generally not 
acted upon; however, if the complaint is clear and warrants 
investigation, it may still be processed. Named reports are 
immediately investigated by the responsible office. The 
whistleblower must provide detailed evidence and contact 
information. If the accused person is found to have violated 
laws or company policies, BES will take necessary actions, 
including ordering the accused person to cease the conduct, 
applying appropriate disciplinary measures, and pursuing 
legal liability. The retention period for complaint records is 
five years for general cases and seven years for major cases, 
with extended retention when legal proceedings are involved. 
Summary of Complaints and Appeals in 2024: One case was 
received in 2024. After investigation by the Internal Audit 
Office, no formal case was established.
▍Whistleblower Reward and Protection Policy
To further promote a corporate culture of "anti-corruption as everyone's responsibility," BES formally adopted the 
"Whistleblower Reward and Protection Policy" during the 13th meeting of the 27th Board of Directors in March 2024. This 
policy aims to encourage and safeguard whistleblowers by establishing a three-tier protection framework: First Tier: 
Emphasizes that anti-corruption is a shared responsibility in all professional duties, empowering whistleblowers to take 
actions. Second Tier: Designated contact points in relevant departments are assigned responsibility for handling reports 
involving potential legal violations in their respective areas. Third Tier: Enhances the authority and role of the Audit Office 
to strengthen BES's whistleblower system. This three-tier protection mechanism provides a secure environment for reporting 
misconduct, fosters a positive perception of whistleblowers, and effectively implements a zero-tolerance policy towards 
corruption in the corporate culture. As of 2024, BES has not received any whistleblower reports under this mechanism.
▍	Occurrence of Anti-Corruption and Anti-Competitive Behavior 
	
 GRI 205-3  206-1   SASB IF-EN-510a.2
In 2024, BES reported no confirmed incidents of corruption, nor any public legal cases against the company or its 
employees involving corrupt practices. No employees were dismissed or disciplined for corruption-related incidents. 
Furthermore, there were no cases of anti-competitive behavior (such as price manipulation or unfair competition), 
antitrust violations, or breaches of monopoly regulations, and the company was not involved in any related legal 
proceedings or subject to fines or sanctions.
▍Special Investigation Procedures
Note: 	This policy serves as a specific regulation for reporting illegal acts and misconduct within BES. Matters not covered by this policy shall 
be governed by other relevant internal regulations of BES.
Note: During the year, BES received reports through the hotline and email, including both anonymous and named complaints. Upon verification, these reports 
were found to be unrelated to corruption and lacked supporting evidence. After thorough evaluation, they did not meet the case filing criteria under the 
"Guidelines for Reporting Violations of Integrity Management," and thus were not filed as cases.

Customer Privacy and Information Security (Material Topic)
2.8
Material Topic Management Approach
SDGs
SDG 9 Industry, Innovation and Infrastructure
SDG 17 Partnerships for the Goals
Impact 
Assessment
Positive Impacts: 	 Enhancing cybersecurity credibility ensures business continuity, reduces the risk of personal data breaches, elevates the company's 
image, demonstrates responsible management, and strengthens competitive advantage.
Negative Impacts: 	Operational risks and threats may arise both internally and externally, such as malicious intrusions or cyberattacks by external 
attackers, or unauthorized access and system vulnerabilities from within the company. These incidents can lead to shutdowns of 
critical business systems, leaks of sensitive data, financial losses, and damage to corporate reputation.
Policies and 
Commitments
To safeguard customer privacy and information security, BES has established a range of internal management systems and operating procedures to 
ensure compliance and risk control throughout the information handling process. Relevant guidelines include:
 "Guidelines for Computer-Related Operations and Information Security Management", which regulate areas such as equipment and network 
connectivity usage, system development and programming, information file and operational processing, and information security audits;
 "Operational Guidelines for the Management of Financial and Non-Financial Information" and other internal control systems outline personal data 
protection standards to strengthen privacy safeguards during data processing;
The company has also established an Audit Committee, in accordance with Article 14-1 of the Securities and Exchange Act, responsible for reviewing 
and revising internal control systems and regularly assessing their effectiveness to ensure the proper implementation of information security and 
personal data protection policies.
BES is committed to continuously enhancing its information security management and customer privacy protection mechanisms in line with legal 
requirements and industry practices, thereby reducing potential risks and strengthening stakeholder trust.
Responsible 
Unit
The Information Security Office is responsible for implementing information operations security management plans;
The Information Security Promotion Group is led by the President, who concurrently serves as the Chief Information Security Officer;
Department heads serve as members of the group, dedicated to promoting the company's information security and handling related audit matters.
Indicators and 
Goals
Management 
Review 
Mechanism
BES's information security management policy is based on the ISO 27001 framework, with a focus on risk control across four key aspects: personnel, 
processes, systems, and internal controls. Through training, anomaly monitoring, access control, and audit mechanisms, the company strengthens 
cybersecurity awareness and operational resilience, ensuring that corporate data, customer privacy, and trade secrets are well protected.
Short-Term (2025)
1.	 At least one individual to obtain an information security 
professional certification (ISO 27001 Lead Auditor) in 
2025.
2.	 Zero information security incidents reported for the year.
3.	 A minimum of 4 information security promotion sessions 
held annually.
4.	 Preparing and submiting an application for ISO 27001 
certification.
Mid-Term (2030)
1.	 Maintain at least one certified information 
security professional within the company.
2.	 Zero information security incidents reported 
for the year.
3.	 Conduct at least 4 information security promotion 
sessions each year.
4.	 Obtain ISO 27001 Risk Assessment Certification.
Long-Term (2030-)
Ensure that information security and 
personal data protection systems 
comply with legal requirements, 
strengthen information security 
management, and enhance customer 
privacy protection mechanisms to 
maintain customer trust.

Communication

Through internal communications and promotion sessions, employees are reminded to comply with information security and personal data protection policies;
Via the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter," suppliers of equipment are required to fulfill responsibilities related to data leakage 
prevention and personal data protection.
▍Organizational Structure and Units
BES established the Information Security Office at the 
end of 2022. The Office is responsible for implementing 
information security management plans, establishing 
and maintaining the information security management 
system, and overseeing the formulation, execution, risk 
control, and compliance auditing of information security 
and protection policies. Moreover, an Information 
Security Promotion Group was formed, with the 
President concurrently serving as the Chief Information 
Security Officer. The head of the Audio/Video Command 
Center serves as both the supervisor and the Information 
Security Officer. Two dedicated information security 
managers are also assigned. Managers of each 
department from across the company, including Legal, 
Audit, IT, and Engineering, are members of the group, 
responsible for promoting the company's information 
security and conducting related audits.
Information Security 
Managers
Head of Each Department
Information Security Office
The Information Security Promotion Group
▍Information Security Management Policy
BES's information security management policy is aligned with the ISO/IEC 27001 framework and 
is designed to fulfill the control requirements set forth in international standards. This serves as 
the fundamental control mechanism for the daily operations to protect company data：
In addition, BES also promotes the implementation of the relevant policies through the 
following aspects:
1.	 Personnel Management: Deliver ongoing training to enhance employees' cybersecurity awareness and 
integrate it into various operational processes to reducehuman-related risks.
2.	 Cybersecurity Monitoring: Regular updates to firewall firmware and blocking rules, along with 
monitoring internal and external abnormal activities through the cybersecurity monitoring center, 
establishing a robust cybersecurity barrier.
3.	 Process Management: Define responsibilities for software development and program modification 
processes, system document management, and access control for programs and data within the 
information system cycle to ensure data security and proper information security management.
4.	 Internal Control Management: Conduct annual audits of information cycles and cybersecurity by the 
internal audit unit to ensure the implementation of internal cybersecurity management measures and 
the continuous improvement of control measures.
1.	 Protect the company's information from unauthorized access, modification, disclosure, or 
destruction; 
2.	 Maintain the integrity and availability of the company's systems and data;
3.	 Establish information security risk assessment and management procedures;
4.	 Enforce a secure password management policy;
5.	 Ensure that employees, consultants, and contractors understand and comply with the company's 
information security policies;
6.	 Regularly monitor and test the company's information security measures and address any 
identified vulnerabilities;
7.	 Regularly review and update the information security policy.

▍	Information Security Incident 
Management and Response
In accordance with BES's information security policy, 
BES will implement an information security incident 
management procedure to swiftly respond to 
and recover from security incidents, including the 
following measures:
 Establishing a contact list for information systems 
and clear reporting procedures.
 Ensuring backups and restoration processes for 
critical systems or data.
 Documenting, reporting, escalating, and analyzing 
information security incidents.
 Taking necessary actions to restore affected 
systems and data in order to minimize loss and 
impact.
During the development of its security management 
system, BES will strengthen relevant security 
controls and monitoring mechanisms. BES will 
conduct targeted drills and awareness training to 
enhance endpoint protection, regularly disseminate 
information security policies to all staff, and carry out 
related education and training to ensure effective 
incident response time reduction and safeguard 
company data and system for reducing potential 
corporate losses. According to BES's "Personal 
Data File Security Maintenance Plan," BES conducts 
personal data file security audits at least once 
annually to verify compliance with its provisions. For 
identified non-compliance or potential risk, BES must 
plan remedial measures and ensure their execution. 
When implementing corrective and preventive 
actions, it should follow the following procedures:
 Identifying the nature and root cause of the non-
compliance.
 Proposing corrective and preventive action plans.
 Documenting the audit findings and outcomes.
The audit findings and results must be included in the 
audit report and signed off by the company's internal 
audit supervisor and responsible parties.
▍Personal Data Management Policy
To ensure the company's confidential information, related trade secrets and personal data are properly protected, BES continues 
to strengthen its information security capabilities. In addition to complying with international information security standards, BES's 
information operations must also comply with relevant domestic and foreign laws and regulations, and promote the protection 
of confidential information. In accordance with the Personal Information Protection Act and BES's Personal Data Protection 
Management Guidelines, BES has established a personal information management control system, which describes the following 
operational procedures and control points:
▍Reporting and Response
In accordance with BES's "Personal Data Protection Management 
Guidelines" and "Personal Data File Security Maintenance Plan," 
the following measures are to be taken in the event of a personal 
data incident:
▍	2024 Information Security 
and Personal Data Protection 
Achievements   GRI 418-1
	 In 2024, BES did not receive any confirmed complaints 
regarding customer privacy breaches or data loss, nor were 
there any penalties imposed by regulatory authorities.
	 Conducted five internal cybersecurity promotion sessions 
covering topics such as construction site information security, 
asset management, email account usage, and system usage 
guidelines.
	 Assisted at least one employee in obtaining the ISO 
27001:2022 Lead Auditor qualification for Information 
Security Management Systems.
	 Continued preparations for ISO 27001 Information Security 
Management System certification.
	 Joined the Taiwan Computer Emergency Response Team / 
Coordination Center (TWCERT/CC) initiative.
Individuals whose personal data has been stolen must be 
notified in writing and informed of the response measures 
that the company has taken.
Improvement measures must be developed based on the 
cause of the incident.
When personal data is found to be stolen, altered, 
damaged, lost, or leaked, the incident must be immediately 
reported to the department supervisor and designated 
responsible person. The cause and accountability must be 
promptly investigated, and appropriate measures should be 
taken based on the circumstances.

II.  Key Controls
1.	The use of personal data must comply with 
BES's personal data management guidelines 
and relevant laws and regulations.
2.	If a data security incident occurs involving 
personal data files, the affected individual 
must be notified, and the incident must 
be documented and archived for future 
reference.
3.	The maintenance of personal data file 
security must comply with the laws, 
regulations of competent authorities, and 
BES's internal standards.
Employee and customer-related personal 
information is regularly inspected by 
the personnel of BES's IT department to 
determine whether they have been attacked 
or compromised, or data theft. Access to 
the server room is also strictly controlled to 
prevent the leakage of sensitive personal data.
I.  Operational Procedures
1.	The unit responsible for personal data management must comply with the 
regulations of the Personal Data Protection Act when collecting, using, and 
processing personal data and must not exceed its authorized scope.
2.	Each unit must clearly inform individuals of their rights when collecting personal data.
3.	Each unit is responsible for managing and maintaining the accuracy of personal data 
related to its business functions.
4.	If any errors or omissions are identified in the personal data, the individual must be 
notified to make corrections or provide additional information.
5.	In case of a personal data accuracy dispute, the data processing or use must be 
suspended either proactively or at the request of the individual.
6.	When the specific purpose of using or processing personal data has been fulfilled, 
the retention period has expired, or the individual request for deletion, suspension 
of use, or disposal, all use of the data must be ceased, and the data deleted.
7.	All stages of data collection, processing, use, correction, supplementation, and 
deletion must be properly recorded and preserved.
8.	Data on decommissioned computers must be thoroughly deleted.
9.	For outsourced operations involving personal data, the external party must be 
required to implement data protection measures in compliance with the Personal 
Data Protection Act, and such operations must be properly monitored.

1.Supply Chain Management Policy
Procurement and 
Contracting Manager
President
Suppliers are key partners for BES; after launching a 
construction project, BES has established management 
systems from the selection of design teams and suppliers 
before contracting, to the inspection and evaluation of 
suppliers during the project. Over the years, BES completed 
numerous high-profileand high-quality projects both 
domestically and internationally. BES not only emphasizes 
the quality of construction and materials from suppliers 
but also pays attention to the ESG aspects of suppliers. 
BES incorporates the use of green building materials and 
corporate sustainability considerations into the supplier 
selection and evaluation system, aiming for mutual 
growth and sustainable operations with suppliers.
▍Sustainable Value Chain
BES's construction projects cover residential and industrial 
buildings, subways, MRT, tunnels, bridges, roads, airports, 
and power plants. Major clients include project owners and 
self-built project customers. Engineering Projects involve 
collaboration with numerous professional suppliers, 
and BES expects collaborative suppliers to adhere to 
the principles of corporate sustainability, integrating 
sustainable supply chain management into procurement 
processes. Before contracting, suppliers' finances and 
project performance are screened to ensure suitable 
suppliers; after contract signing, progress, quality, safety, 
and health management capabilities are assessed and 
evaluated. Environmental and corporate sustainability 
assessments of suppliers are incorporated as key criteria 
in supplier selection during procurement, as well as in 
performance evaluations after contract signing.

▍BES Supplier Management Process
To strengthen sustainable management 
of the supply chain, BES has established 
the "Supplier Registration and Screening 
Guidelines" for new suppliers and the 
"Supplier Assessment and Evaluation 
Procedures" for contractors. Based on 
these guidelines and procedures, new 
suppliers are screened, and contracted 
suppliers are assessed and evaluated. 
At each BES site office, contractors 
with contract amounts of NTD 300,000 
or more are evaluated on their 
performance in areas such as project 
progress, quality, and occupational 
health and safety. Scores are assigned 
during pricing and payment processes. 
T h e  P ro c u re m e n t  a n d  D e l i v e r y 
Department aggregates these regular 
assessments and conducts annual 
evaluations for contractors whose billed 
amounts exceed NTD 1 million.
If a BES site office identifies deficiencies 
in a contractor's performance regarding 
progress, quality, or health and safety, 
the contractor is instructed to correct 
the issues within a specified deadline. 
If corrections are not made promptly, 
the site office may employ alternative 
resources to address the deficiencies, 
and the company may designate the 
contractor as "Under Evaluation" to 
manage risk. In 2024, 3 contractors were 
classified as "Under Evaluation" and 
were not invited to quote any projects.
Selection of 
New Suppliers/ 
Contractors
New Supplier Registration Review
•	Supplier/Contractor registration forms (company registration business items, financial governance, project performance, 
green building materials, and suppliers with ESG and CSR reports) are submitted, reviewed, and graded.
•	From January 1, 2025, supplier/contractors with total environmental pollution fines of NTD 300,000 or more, or those involved in one 
or more major occupational incidents within the year prior to registration or review, will be disqualified from becoming new suppliers.
Invitation to bid for the selection of supplier/contractors
•	Supplier/Contractors are evaluated based on their business scope, financial capability, project track record, and statistical 
performance.
•	Corporate Sustainability Review: During the quotation process, supplier must complete a "Corporate Sustainability" self-assessment 
questionnaire covering areas such as integrity management, compliance with labor laws, prohibition of forced labor and child labor, 
environmental protection, energy and water conservation, and social impact assessment. 
•	Financial Credit Review: Before being invited to bid, companies must be checked on the Government e-Procurement System and the 
China Credit Information Service website for any records of dishonored checks or violations of the Government Procurement Act 
before they can be nominated. When submitting a quote, the company must also provide its "Business Tax Sales and Tax Declaration 
Form (401)" and proof of tax payment.
•	Suppliers with ESG, green building materials, and recyclable construction methods are preferred.
•	The assessment and evaluation of C and other factory dealers are eliminated, and factory dealers are excluded from the bidding process.
Supplier/ 
Contractor 
Maintenance 
and 
Assessment
Supplier/Contractor Contracts are signed
•	Signed the "Closing Letter on Matters to be Complied with in Third-Party Safety, Health and Environmental Protection Operations".
•	Sign the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter".
Supplier/Contractor Assessment
•	Frequency: Supplier/Contractor assessments are conducted during each estimate and pricing cycle, with an annual evaluation held 
every January.
•	Assessment: Supplier/Contractors with contracts worth NTD 300,000 or more are included in the assessment list. During each 
estimate and pricing cycle's verification and pricing phase, they are evaluated on progress, quality, and occupational health and 
safety. Supplier/Contractors with ESG credentials or green procurement practices would receive bonus points. Supplier/Contractors 
who violate the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment" are subject to deductions and placed under monitoring for improvement.
•	Evaluation: Supplier/Contractors whose pricing amount exceeds NTD 1 million in a given year are included in the annual evaluation 
list. In January of the following year, vendor grading is conducted based on assessment scores.
ESG promotion and advocacy
•	 From 2025 onward, BES plans to promote ESG among supplier/contractors, encouraging them to disclose their sustainability practices.

2. Sustainable Procurement   GRI 204-1
At our primary operating locations (including the operational 
boundaries defined in this report), we prioritize local sourcing to reduce 
carbon emissions from long‑distance transportation and support local 
business development. Based on new contracts worth over NTD 300,000, 
procurement statistics are categorized by the registered business address 
of the supplier as follows: In 2024, local procurement in Taiwan (including 
Penghu, Kinmen, and Matsu islands) totaled NTD 23,461,632,462. Green 
procurement amounted to NTD 559,592,367, accounting for 2.39% 
of total procurement. No procurement was made outside Taiwan. The 
amounts of both local and non-local procurement in other countries 
were also NTD 0. Therefore, Taiwan's local procurement ratio was 100%.
In recent years, BES has continued to promote environmentally friendly and 
energy-saving policies while also encouraging all departments to use eco-
friendly products, such as energy-efficient equipment (e.g., LED lighting, energy-
saving air conditioning systems, and products with eco-friendly, energy-saving, 
or water-saving labels). BES plans to gradually increase the adoption rate of 
energy-efficient and eco-friendly building materials in private sector projects 
and self-developed cases, with such materials already being used in most 
construction sites for enhancing overall green procurement efforts. Since 2022, 
BES has actively participated in the "Green Procurement Declaration Platform for 
Private Enterprises and Organizations" launched by the Ministry of Environment, 
Executive Yuan, which has significantly increased its green procurement 
amount and performance. BES was awarded a certificate of appreciation by 
the Department of Environmental Protection, Taipei City Government for this 
achievement. BES continues to develop the green supply chain and plans to 
launch a supplier sustainability advocacy program starting in 2025 to strengthen 
suppliers' sustainable operations and enhance their sustainability performance.

▍BES Supplier Sustainability Management Regulations  GRI 407-1  408-1  409-1
To enhance corporate sustainability, reduce impacts on the natural environment and society, and establish sound ethical standards, BES has formulated 
the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter" (hereafter "the Commitment Letter"). In 2025, the Commitment Letter will undergo its revision to 
incorporate provisions on no deforestation, land conservation, and biodiversity protection. BES will continue to adopt a risk-based approach, dynamically 
reviewing the structure of its supply chain and the suitability of its management measures.
This Commitment Letter also requires that suppliers 
do not employ child labor, do not impose forced 
or compulsory labor, and must respect workers' 
freedom of association and collective bargaining 
rights. These requirements are prerequisites for 
cooperation with suppliers on new contracts worth 
exceeding NTD 300,000 or more. In addition, BES 
requires all newly invited suppliers to complete 
a Sustainable Development Self-Assessment 
Questionnaire to confirm their commitment to 
prohibiting child labor, forced labor, and complying 
with labor regulations.
A dual-process assessment mechanism is 
implemented for existing suppliers to ensure 
consistent periodic performance checks and an 
annual evaluation. This also includes a review of 
compliance with the Commitment Letter. If serious 
violations are identified, suppliers are penalized 
with point deductions and placed on a monitoring 
list, required to make improvements, or have their 
qualifications suspended. In 2024, this applied to 
a total of 470 suppliers. Based on self-assessments 
and evaluations, BES did not identify any suppliers 
violating freedom of association, employing child 
labor, or using forced labor. In the future, BES 
will expand the coverage of signed Commitment 
Letters and update risk assessments immediately in 
response to changes in procurement or workforce 
structures.
Employee Health and Safety
•	 Provide a safe working environment and 
protective equipment
•	 Establish mechanisms for occupational injury 
prevention and emergency response
•	 Arrange appropriate rest and activity 
alternation opportunities
•	 Plan proper safety operation procedures and 
conduct training
Labor and Human Rights Protection
•	 No discrimination, no forced labor, 
and prohibition of sexual harassment
•	 No child labor; protect underage and 
female workers
•	 Comply with labor law requirements, 
including statutory wages, working 
hours, holidays, and benefits
•	 Respect freedom of association and 
the right to collective bargaining
Environmental Protection
•	 Classify and dispose of waste in 
compliance with regulations
•	 Adopt green practices and recycling 
mechanisms to reduce pollution
•	 Reduce the generation of volatile 
toxic substances and ozone-
depleting substances
•	 Improve work processes, use green 
building materials, promote waste 
sorting, recycling, and implement 
wastewater management and other 
environmental protection measures
Integrity Management
•	 Prohibit any form of improper 
exchange of interests
•	 Respect intellectual property 
rights and prevent the leakage of 
technical information
•	 Protect personal data and prevent 
unauthorized disclosure
•	 Comply with legal and regulatory 
requirements

3. Supplier Risk Assessment  GRI 308-1  308-2  414-1  414-2
Since 2022, BES has incorporated ESG, CSR, and green building material 
certifications as part of the new supplier registration and screening 
process. During the bidding stage, invited suppliers are asked to 
complete the Corporate Sustainability Self-Assessment Questionnaire. 
Preference is given to suppliers with ESG, CSR, green building material 
certification, or reusable construction methods. During the supplier/
contractor assessment phase, evaluation items include their performance 
on progress, quality, occupational health and safety, and daily 
environmental protection management. This is intended to reduce the 
environmental impact caused by the construction industry. According to 
BES's Supplier Registration and Screening Guidelines, 110 new suppliers 
were onboarded in 2024, all of whom signed the "Supplier Code of 
Conduct Commitment Letter", achieving a 100% signing rate.
Starting from January 1, 2025, the selection of new suppliers will 
be revised. Suppliers listed on the on the Ministry of Environment's 
regulated pollution source database (including penalty information) 
website (https://prtr.moenv.gov.tw/deal.html) with cumulative fines for 
environmental pollution totaling NTD 300,000 or more within one year 
prior to the registration review date will not be eligible as new suppliers. 
Moreover, beginning January 1, 2025, social criteria for screening new 
suppliers will be based on the Ministry of Labor's Occupational Safety 
and Health Administration's major occupational safety incident public 
website (https://pacs.osha.gov.tw/2875/). Suppliers involved in a major 
occupational safety incident within one year prior to their registration 
application review date will not be eligible as new suppliers.

For suppliers that seriously violate occupational safety and health regulations and fail to actively undertake corrective 
actions, BES will impose suspension or termination of cooperation. During the reporting period, one supplier was

standards for corporate social responsibility.

assessments are conducted every January based on BES's environmental and social management standards. As of the end 
of the reporting period, 470 suppliers were evaluated in 2024. Suppliers identified with environmental management risks 
are placed under monitoring to ensure the supply chain meets sustainable development requirements. Assessments 
also cover safety records, labor rights, and working conditions to mitigate potential social risks.

Social
Environmental
Potential Negative Impacts
Inadequate construction site safety management, 
workers' improper use to properly use personal 
protective equipment (PPE), and lack of 
enforcement of safety regulations for high-risk 
operations (such as working at heights or operating 
heavy machinery) may lead to industrial accidents 
and occupational injuries.
Non-compliant wastewater discharge can affect water quality 
around construction sites. Excessive dust and noise pollution 
generated during construction may harm the surrounding 
environment. Failure to effectively suppress dust or control 
emissions during construction may lead to air pollution. 
Violations of waste disposal regulations may compromise 
environmental hygiene.
Corrective Measures Following 
Identification of Negative 
Impacts
•	Suppliers are notified to make improvements 
within a specified timeframe and may be fined. If 
improvements are not completed by the deadline, 
BES will either assign other laborers to implement 
the necessary improvements or prohibit the 
supplier's workers from entering the site.
•	The BES's Occupational Safety and Health 
Management Department periodically organizes 
6-hour general occupational safety and health 
training to strengthen employee safety, and 
conducts occasional on-site safety audits to ensure 
compliance and reduce future risks.
•	For suppliers that seriously violate occupational 
safety and health regulations and fail to undertake 
corrective actions, BES will impose suspension or 
termination of cooperation.
•	Suppliers with confirmed environmental pollution fines 
or work stoppages, posing significant actual or potential 
environmental impacts, will be notified by BES to improve 
within a specified timeframe. If they fail to comply, BES will 
assign other laborers to carry out the improvements.
•	For suppliers involved in serious environmental pollution, 
BES may terminate cooperation following evaluation if any 
of the following conditions are identified:
1.	Rated as "Under Evaluation" or downgraded due to 
pollution for two consecutive years. 
2.	Repeated violations of environmental protection 
regulations with five or more instances and total 
fines exceeding NTD 300,000 or had at least one work 
stoppage. 
3.	Failure to provide proof of compliant waste disposal and 
confirmed environmental violations upon audit.

4. Supplier/Contractor Anti‑Corruption  GRI 2-25  2-26  205-2  205-3  206-1   SASB
IF-EN-510a.3
BES's primary business partners are suppliers. According to BES's internal "BES Domestic Procurement Guidelines," established in 2014 and amended for 
the fifth time in 2020, anti‑corruption policies and procedures are clearly stated in procurement contracts (excluding supplementary agreements). Suppliers 
are requested to sign the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter" to pledge adherence to integrity in business and compliance with BES's policies. 
Suppliers in serious violation of BES's anti‑corruption policy may face suspension or disqualification from future collaboration.
To enforce its integrity policy, BES handles any submitted appeals or identified 
improper commercial behaviors that conducted confidentially through 
the Audit Office. BES commits to protecting whistleblowers from dismissal, 
demotion, salary reduction, or any violation of their legal, contractual, or 
customary rights due to reporting. In 2024, 470 suppliers were evaluated and 
found no incidents of corruption, anti‑competitive behavior, antitrust issues, 
or violations of social or economic laws. BES will continue to require the 
signing of the "Supplier Code of Conduct Commitment Letter" in procurement 
contracts to progressively ensure responsible business conduct with suppliers.
(1)	 Suppliers, during bidding or contract execution, if they encounter 
bid‑rigging, coercion, bribery, threats, injury, or other irregularities, may 
directly report or lodge a complaint to BES.
(2)	 Suppliers and their subcontractors must not offer expectations, bribes, 
commissions, rebates, or other improper benefits to BES personnel or 
agents. Violators not only bear legal responsibility but also lose bidding 
or award qualifications. If BES suffers losses as a result, they are liable for 
compensation.
BES's unit for handling reports and complaints: Audit Office
Email: report@bes.com.tw 
Phone: (02) 8787‑7735 / (02) 8787‑6522
Fax: (02) 8787‑6250

Policies and 
Commitments
Committed to taking concrete actions to support the goal of the Paris Agreement to limit global warming to within 1.5 ℃, BES demonstrates its ambition 
toward achieving net-zero carbon emissions.
To fulfill the 2050 Net Zero Emissions commitment, BES's Sustainable Development Implementation Group actively studies regulations from the Financial 
Supervisory Commission and the Ministry of Environment, while referencing international Science-Based Targets initiatives (SBTi) to formulate BES's own 
science-based emission reduction targets. These targets are intended to meet greenhouse gas reduction goals and outline an annual decarbonization pathway.
Responsible 
Unit
The company has designated the Sustainable Development Implementation Group as the core executing unit, coordinated and supervised by the Sustainable 
Development Committee, which regularly reports progress to the Board of Directors, thereby fulfilling its oversight responsibilities.
Indicators and 
Goals
Management 
Review 
Mechanism
BES' greenhouse gas inventory and verification timeline has been reported to the Board of Directors, and going forward, the progress will be submitted 
quarterly to enable the Board's supervision and oversight, with verification and disclosure carried out in accordance with regulatory timelines. The Plan-Do-
Check-Act (PDCA) approach will be used to record monthly data on water and electricity usage for continuous review of opportunities for improvement.
2024 Annual 
Actions
1. A net-zero emission goal has been established, aligned with the SBTi's 1.5 ℃ carbon reduction targets and pathway requirements.
2.	100% of site offices have adopted solar-powered warning lights, and 3.01% of vehicles used by site offices are hybrid electric. 
3.	Greenhouse gas emissions increased by 24.27%, while greenhouse gas intensity (CO2 equivalent per revenue) decreased by 3.19% compared to the previous year.

with

emissions by 2050.

Robust Operations and Corporate Governance
Environmental Friendliness and Green Engineering
Happy Workplace and Social Impact
In recent years, due to the increasing frequency of disasters caused by climate change, BES proactively responded in 2024 by having the Risk Management 
Group conduct an initial identification of related climate risks. They developed corresponding policies and preventive measures, which were then submitted 
to and approved by the Board of Directors. In the same year, BES also proposed a net‑zero emissions strategy and carbon‑reduction targets to establish a 
greenhouse gas reduction management policy. BES referenced the TCFD framework, combining risk identification, stakeholder interviews, and workshops, 
to identify climate-related risks and opportunities, and appropriately disclose the financial impacts caused by climate change and related actions. After 
implementing adequate climate adaptation and disaster recovery measures, BES seeks to seize opportunities to ensure profitability and strengthen its climate 
resilience in order to cope with subsequent climate disasters.
1. Climate Governance
BES will follow the 1.5° C emission‑reduction targets and pathways defined by 
the Science Based Targets initiative (SBTi), and commits to setting short‑term 
goals to reduce Scope 1 and Scope 2 greenhouse gas emissions by 42% and 
Scope 3 emissions by 25% by 2030; the long‑term goal is to achieve net‑zero 
carbon emissions by 2050.
The Board of Directors is the company's highest risk‑management entity, 
responsible for clearly understanding the risks faced by operations, ensuring 
the effectiveness of risk management, and bearing ultimate responsibility 
for risk management; the Risk Management Group conducts quantitative 
analysis of operational risks, proposes response strategies, and submits these 
to the Audit Committee and the Board of Directors. On November 26, 2024, 
BES convened a risk management meeting and identified 30 high-risk issues, 
along with ongoing mitigation measures. These were reported to the Audit 
Committee on December 24, 2024, and to the Board of Directors on December 
26, 2024, to ensure thorough implementation. Since the establishment of the 
Sustainable Development Committee in 2022, BES has regularly discussed 
potential internal and external impacts of various issues, including the 
identification and assessment of climate‑change risks and responses to climate 
impacts, and has formulated adaptation and mitigation strategies based on 
advice of experts.
The Sustainable Development Implementation Group serves as the core unit 
executing net‑zero emissions targets; all promoting managers had signed 
a net‑zero commitment in July 2024, voluntarily pledging practical actions 
to support the Paris Agreement's goal of limiting global warming to within 
1.5° C, demonstrating the company's strong intention toward net‑zero carbon 
reduction.
2.Risk Management
To identify and assess significant impacts or risks associated with 
operations, BES has established the following under its Board of Directors:
 Risk Management Group
The group is responsible for managing all actual or potential risks 
affecting sustainable development. The Board serves as the highest 
supervisor and decision-making entity for risk management, approves 
the company's risk management objectives and policies, ensures 
implementation of management measures, continuously monitors the 
risk management mechanism for effectiveness, and bears the major 
responsibility for risk management.
 Sustainable Development Committee
The committee assists the Board in evaluating risks and response 
strategies across environmental, social, and governance aspects to 
achieve sustainable operational goals, and convenes at least once 
annually.
▍Climate-Related Risk Management Process
In 2024, the Risk Management Group followed a structured risk 
management process from risk identification, analysis, evaluation, 
response, report, and disclosure, BES assessed the level of consensus 
across departments on various risks, identified high-risk issues, and 
established corresponding measures. Moreover, the Sustainable 
Development Committee approved a greenhouse gas reduction 
management policy and formalized BES's net-zero targets.
