BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report
3. Climate Strategy
In 2024, BES incorporated the potential impacts of climate 
change into overall operational considerations through risk 
assessment, evaluating the likelihood and severity of risks, and 
formulating risk response and mitigation plans. Subsequently, 
based on business type, risk strategy, and financial planning 
status, BES identified and planned for both physical risks and 
transition risks and opportunities, using scenario analysis to 
simulate potential future climate-related financial impacts, 
which serve as the foundation for future action plans.
Regarding physical risks, BES identified that climate change 
could restrict water and electricity supply in construction sites, 
directly affecting project schedules and construction timeline. 
It also noted that data centers might face system failures and 
equipment damage due to extreme weather events, potentially 
causing operational disruptions. The increasing frequency and 
severity of extreme climate events could lead to project delays 
and physical damage to facilities, raising project costs and 
insurance expenses.
Regarding transition risks, as Taiwan legislates its 2050 net-
zero emissions target, policy and regulatory changes are highly 
likely, including strengthened carbon emissions reporting 
requirements and the implementation of carbon pricing. 
These developments may increase operating costs and affect 
profitability. Additionally, the transition to new technologies 
poses challenges, particularly in the effective adoption 
of greenhouse gas emissions accounting and reduction 
technologies. In response to these challenges, BES has been 
actively seizing on market opportunities brought by climate 
change in recent years, adopting innovative technologies 
in line with green building standards to improve energy 
efficiency, such as replacing lighting with LEDs and purchasing 
low-energy-consumption inverter air conditioners. BES will 
continue to invest in energy-efficient building design and 
the development of carbon estimation tools. The carbon 
management data from the BES EcoTech Industrial Park 
will serve as a basis for low-carbon planning in future new 
construction projects, enhancing overall competitiveness.
4. Identification and Assessment of Climate Risks
▍Actual Scenarios
BES initially used the Representative Concentration Pathways (RCP) scenarios 
proposed by the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC), considering 
three scenarios: RCP2.6, RCP4.5, and RCP8.5. It also referred to simulations from the 
Taiwan Climate Change Projection Information and Adaptation Knowledge Platform 
(https://tccip.ncdr.nat.gov.tw/) for RCP2.6–RCP8.5 scenarios to estimate Taiwan's 
temperature and rainfall percentage changes and assess the potential impacts.

6. Indicators and Goals
The Sustainable Development Implementation Group serves as the core unit executing net‑zero emissions targets; all promoting managers had signed a net‑zero commitment in July 
2024, voluntarily pledging practical actions to support the Paris Agreement's goal of limiting global warming to within 1.5 ℃, demonstrating the company's strong intention toward 
net‑zero carbon reduction.
Using 2023 as the base year, achieve an absolute reduction of 42% in Scope 1 and Scope 2 greenhouse gas emissions by 2030 (equivalent to an annual reduction of 6%), and a 25% 
reduction in Scope 3 emissions (equivalent to an annual reduction of 3.6%).
In accordance with the Taiwan Stock Exchange's directive No. 1110004505 issued on March 21, 2022, BES is classified as a listed company with paid-in capital exceeding NTD 10 
billion. Therefore, BES must complete its greenhouse gas (GHG) inventory by 2023 and third-party verification by 2024. In addition, subsidiaries included in the consolidated financial 
statements must complete their GHG inventory by 2025 and verification by 2027. The parent company's board of directors must complete the planning of the GHG inventory and 
verification timeline for the entire group (including subsidiaries) in the first quarter of 2023, and supervise the progress on a quarterly basis.
BES has already reported its GHG inventory and verification timeline planning to the 17th meeting of the 26th Board of Directors. Moving forward, the company will report quarterly 
progress on its phased targets to the Board to facilitate its oversight and supervision.

7. Energy Usage and Greenhouse Gas Emissions
▍Energy Usage  GRI 302-1  302-3
BES's energy consumption mainly consists of indirect energy emissions (accounting for 81.81% of total energy consumption) and direct emissions (accounting 
for 18.19% of total energy consumption), with externally purchased renewable energy (electricity) accounting for 0% of total energy usage. In 2024, total energy 
consumption was 76,641.75 MJ, an increase of 25.31% year-on-year. The main reason was that most construction sites entered their peak working phase and the 
reporting scope expanded. However, energy intensity decreased by 2.3% compared to 2023. In 2024, BES increased usage for some energy sources, with electricity 
consumption increasing most significantly. To improve energy efficiency, BES will continue to require each site office to take energy-saving measures and strictly 
control energy usage.
Note 1: 	For 2024, the assurance scope covers BES's headquarters and 41 site offices, along with eight subsidiaries and sub-subsidiaries: Chung-Hua City Co., Ltd., Chung-Hua City Development Co., Ltd., Chung-Hua City International 
Investment Co., Ltd., BES Investment Co., Ltd., BESM Holding Co., Ltd., BES Logistics International Co., Ltd., Huading Enterprise Co., Ltd., and BES Construction Corporation. 
Note 2: 	The 2023 boundary included BES's headquarters and 32 site offices.

▍	Greenhouse Gas Emissions  	 	
GRI 305-1  305-2  305-4
In terms of greenhouse gas management, in 2022, 
BES EcoTech Industrial Park became the world's 
first asset owner to obtain PAS 2080 certification 
for carbon management in buildings and 
infrastructure. Through this project, greenhouse 
gas emissions from materials and construction 
methods used during the construction phase 
each month were calculated, providing more 
data to support carbon reduction efforts in 
construction projects. In 2024, BES expanded 
the boundary of its greenhouse gas inventory 
to include BES's headquarters and 41 site offices, 
as well as subsidiaries and sub- subsidiaries 
such as Chung-Hua City Co., Ltd., Chung-Hua 
City Development Co., Ltd., Chung-Hua City 
International Investment Co., Ltd., BES Investment 
Co., Ltd., BESM Holding Co., Ltd., BES Logistics 
International Co., Ltd., Huading Enterprise Co., 
Ltd., and BES Construction Corporation. The 
greenhouse gas inventory was also verified by a 
third party in June 2025, currently not including 
Scope 3. The results of this greenhouse gas 
inventory will support the company in complying 
with regulatory requirements and provide data for 
setting strategies of the net-zero target. BES will 
use the results of the greenhouse gas inventory 
to formulate a corporate transition plan, adopting 
energy-saving and carbon-reduction measures 
such as conserving electricity, fuel, water, and 
paper consumption.

▍Energy-Saving and Efficiency Improvement Measures and Plans for Headquarters and Site offices
BES continuously collects and reviews energy 
consumption data, replacing high-energy 
equipment and including high-efficiency 
device usage benchmarks in standardized and 
rolling management. This establishes effective 
operational control methods and processes to 
improve energy efficiency.
•	 Replacement of energy-saving lamps and 
elimination of unnecessary lamps and 
other energy-consuming equipment in the 
headquarters.
•	 Installing LED energy-saving lighting 
fixtures in newly established site offices.
•	 Strengthening online collaboration 
and paperless operations, consolidate 
photocopying devices across units, and 
reducing needs for printing and copying.
•	 Promoting electronic official documents 
and paperless construction budgeting to 
reduce paper usage.
•	 Installing timers on air-conditioning 
units. Replacing with energy-efficient air 
conditioners, setting temperature at 26° C 
plus fans, and turning off air-conditioning 
from November to February in winter.
The energy intensity of the headquarters and 
site offices (measured in gigajoules per million 
NTD of revenue) decreased by approximately 
2.32% compared to the previous year.
	 Results
	 Management and Assessment Mechanism
Establishing management guidelines for water 
and electricity use, regulating employee behaviors, 
and inventory whether the headquarters and 
construction site offices have energy- and water-
saving equipment or outdated high-energy 
devices. Managers of each unit then oversee 
employee actions and equipment replacement, 
and use a PDCA cycle to record monthly water 
and electricity consumption data, continuously 
reviewing any possibility for improvement.
	 Improvement Actions
	 Improving the overall efficiency of energy and resource usage.
	
Specific measures include formulating relevant action plans through 
energy resource management policies to promote energy and carbon 
reduction, as well as water conservation, and to minimize the negative 
impacts of overuse of energy resources and environmental pollution. 
In addition, by enhancing resource efficiency, sustainable value is then 
created.
	 Implementing energy and carbon reduction, 
and conserve water to reduce societal 
impact.

Policies and 
Commitments
Policies
1.	Being a pioneer in smart eco‑friendly products.
2.	Promoting clean environments and reducing environmental pollution.
3.	Supporting circular economy by implementing resource recycling and reuse 
policies.
4.	Protecting natural ecosystems and minimizing disturbance to wildlife habitats.
Commitments
1.	 During project planning and design, adapting to natural conditions and regional characteristics by creating 
green buildings and integrating smart monitoring equipment to build livable homes.
2.	 Improving energy and resource consumption from an operational perspective and actively implement 
environmentally friendly technologies, thereby balancing environmental sustainability and market economic 
development, reducing negative environmental and social impact, and creating sustainable value.
Responsible 
Unit
Green and Smart Buildings: 
Private Engineering Division, Real Estate Division
Indicators and 
Goals
Short-Term (2025)
1.	For a project that has been listed as the candidate for 
green‑building label, applying for the green‑building 
certification once construction is completed.
2.	For at least one new private construction project, using 
aluminum formwork or circular‑economy alternative 
methods on at least 70% of the site to reduce construction 
waste.
3.	Introducing smart and AI technologies, such as integrating 
real‑time monitoring, risk alerts, access control, anomaly 
notifications, and dashboards combining environmental and 
site personnel data; ensuring that 60% of site offices achieve 
at least three of these cores smart‑management functions.
4.	In accordance with construction noise‑control standards, 
implementing noise-mitigation measures; reducing public 
complaints by 5% compared to the previous year.
5.	Beyond owner's requirements, ensuring that for site 
offices with new construction projects, material usage with 
environmental labels or low‑carbon certified green building 
materials (as defined by the Architecture and Building 
Research Institute, Ministry of the Interior) accounts for more 
than 3% of interior finish surface area.
6.	Strengthening separation management of construction 
waste, managing all on‑site construction waste by type—
from generation to reuse or transfer to treatment agencies—
in compliance with the types of reuse and management 
methods for construction and demolition waste as stipulated 
by the National Land Management Agency, Ministry of the 
Interior.
Mid-Term (2030)
1.	Obtaining two Green Building Labels.
2.	For at least one new private construction project, using 
aluminum formwork or circular‑economy alternative 
methods on at least 80% of the site to reduce 
construction waste.
3.	Introducing smart and AI technologies with 
80% implementation rate, such as integrating 
real‑time monitoring, risk alerts, access control, 
anomaly notifications, and dashboards combining 
environmental and site personnel data; ensuring that 
65% of site offices achieve at least three of these cores 
smart‑management functions.
4.	Ensuring construction projects comply with 
construction noise-control standards and implement 
noise-mitigation measures; reduce public complaints 
by 5% compared to the previous year.
5.	Beyond owner's requirements, ensuring that for new 
construction field offices, environmentally labeled or 
low-carbon certified green building materials account 
for over 5% of materials used.
6.	Strengthening separation management of construction 
waste, managing all on‑site construction waste 
by type—from generation to reuse or transfer to 
treatment agencies—in compliance with the types of 
reuse and management methods for construction and 
demolition waste as stipulated by the National Land 
Management Agency, Ministry of the Interior.
Long-Term (2030-)
1.	Obtaining two Green Building Labels.
2.	For at least one new private reinforced concrete (RC)-
structure construction project, implement aluminum 
formwork or circular-economy alternative methods 
covering more than 80% of the site to reduce 
construction waste.
3.	Introducing smart and AI technologies with 
100% implementation rate, such as integrating 
real‑time monitoring, risk alerts, access control, 
anomaly notifications, and dashboards combining 
environmental and site personnel data; ensuring 
that 70% of site offices achieve at least three of these 
cores smart‑management functions.
4.	Ensuring construction projects comply with 
construction noise-control standards and implement 
noise-mitigation measures; reducing public 
complaints by 5% compared to the previous year.
5.	Beyond owner's requirements, ensuring that for new 
construction site offices, environmentally labeled or 
low-carbon certified green building materials account 
for over 10% of materials used.
6.	Strengthening separation management of 
construction waste, managing all on‑site construction 
waste by type—from generation to reuse or transfer 
to treatment agencies—in compliance with the types 
of reuse and management methods for construction 
and demolition waste as stipulated by the National 
Land Management Agency, Ministry of the Interior.

Management 
Review 
Mechanism
1. 	Application of Smart Technology
	
The Command Center assists each site office in the introduction and application of relevant AI technologies. The heads of each site offices are responsible for 
coordination, control, and execution. The Command Center conducts follow-up audits and integrates data to evaluate the degree of implementation by each unit.
2. 	Establishment of Environmental Protection Work Guidelines for Construction Sites
	
Using the PDCA cycle and the 6S principles (Sort, Set in Order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, Security), ensuring implementation of related operational procedures. 
The head of each site office supervises the implementation status of environmental protection operations.
2024 Annual 
Actions
1.	 Obtained one Gold-level Candidate Green Building Certificate.
2.	 100% of construction site safety facilities used solar-powered warning lights; 3.01% of site offices adopted electric motorcycles; 1% of site offices used low-noise 
machinery; 1% of site offices used green building materials; 100% of construction waste was sorted at sites.
3.	 All site offices are now fully equipped with monitoring systems and have established facial recognition and access control systems.
4.	 In line with the company's paperless policy and ESG initiatives, the bidding preparation process has been digitized to reduce paper consumption.
5.	 The application of smart platform modules visualizes construction progress, owner billing, financial revenue, dispute cases, design changes, budgeting, and 
project execution, making weekly engineering meetings more efficient for review and control.
6.	 Self-developed LINEbot technology has been introduced, effectively integrating group communication and enforcing a real-name registration system for 
personnel, thereby enhancing team management efficiency.
Communication 
with 
Stakeholders
1.	 The Board of Directors convenes monthly.
2.	 The General Shareholders' Meeting is held annually.
3.	 The Audit Committee convenes occasionally.
4.	 The site offices are visited quarterly to engage with owners and supervisory units.
5.	 Occasional exchanges are held with various government agencies, consulting firms, and vendors.
6.	 Monthly progress meetings, construction coordination meetings, and interface coordination meetings are held in cooperation with owners.
In recent years, in response to labor shortages and a lack of management talent in Taiwan, it has become essential not only to continue developing new 
construction methods that reduce manpower requirements, but also to integrate smart systems during construction to enhance management efficiency and 
deploy migrant workers as needed. The overall pace of internalizing new construction methods and advancing digital transformation will directly impact 
competitiveness. In addition, in line with the trend toward net-zero buildings, BES emphasizes carbon footprint assessments for projects and incorporates 
the PAS 2080 standard from the planning and design phases. BES also incorporates the selection of low-carbon building materials and green material 
procurement into its management practices. Furthermore, BES strengthens cost management and control, reduces carbon emissions during construction, 
and enhances differentiation through new materials, construction methods, and technologies. Therefore, BES continues to adopt smart building as a core 
design principle, leveraging government urban renewal projects to enhance its brand reputation while accumulating experience in planning, interface 
integration, and construction management. Notably, the "BES EcoTech Industrial Park" is the prime example where smart building designs have been 
actively implemented.

BES Engineering 
Department
To enhance transparency and efficiency in construction site management, BES 
launched the first phase of smart construction site implementation at the Dunbei 
Engineering Department in 2024. This phase introduced of smart technologies such 
as real-name registration management, environmental monitoring, access control, 
mobile surveillance systems, and digital forms. Simultaneously, feasibility tests were 
conducted to integrate project management platforms with on-site equipment data.
A key innovation is the independently developed LINE group management robot 
(BES@bot), which integrates engineering information flow and digital governance 
features:
	Real-name registration and chat records: Personnel identity verification and full 
logging of chat timestamps and content enhance accountability and traceability 
communication.
	Automated archiving and full-text search: Support multiple file formats such as 
PDF, Word, PowerPoint, and Excel, with the capability to search within compressed 
files and support for multilingual queries in Chinese, English, and Vietnamese.
	Real-time notifications and cloud storage: Managing messages, file auto-
archiving, with LINE push notifications for permission changes or task assignments 
to improve response efficiency.
	Occupational safety management application: Combining with digital form tools 
to enable online completion and submission of safety documents such as "Hazard 
Notification Forms" and "Simplified Safety Forms," effectively strengthening 
safety records and real-time monitoring on-site, bringing practical results to 
digital occupational safety management. Relevant forms are being developed 
progressively in line with project schedules, and a document coding system is 
currently under development.
Furthermore, LINE Bot-related technologies have been included in BES's intellectual 
property management program, covering trademark, patent, and copyright 
registrations. Progress is periodically compiled and reported annually to the board 
of directors, demonstrating BES's investment and achievements in smart governance 
and technology autonomy.

Robust Operations and Corporate Governance
Environmental Friendliness and Green Engineering
Happy Workplace and Social Impact
The nearly zero-carbon building responds to sustainability through "green energy, renewable energy, and water resources" design, integrating 
sustainability and environmental coexistence into building practices. In 2024, BES has implemented the following measures in the EcoTech Industrial 
Park project, and it is expected to be completed in 2026:
BES Nearly Zero-Carbon Building Example – EcoTech Industrial Park
•	 By designing habitat areas and open landscape spaces, biodiversity is 
enhanced.
•	 The site is designed for water retention to reduce stormwater runoff.
•	 Multi‑layered and vertical greenery design helps mitigate the urban heat 
island effect.
•	 Green transportation provisions include bicycle parking, shared mobility 
shuttle bus, and low‑emission vehicle parking.
Sustainable Site Design
Water-saving Design
•	 Water-saving devices are used throughout to reduce water consumption.
•	 A rooftop rainwater harvesting system is used for landscape irrigation.
•	 Drought-tolerant native plant species are selected to minimize irrigation 
water usage.
•	 Adopting a central water recycling and reuse system to reduce water 
consumption.
Passive Building Carbon Reduction Design
•	 Building orientation and shading are focused on optimizing sunlight 
exposure, ventilation, and shading.
•	 The building envelope is energy‑saving: featuring natural daylighting and 
external sun shading to reduce direct solar gain.
•	 High‑insulation roofing and Low‑E energy‑saving glass are used.
•	 Steel structure is used to reduce cement consumption.
•	 High‑performance concrete is adopted to improve structural durability.
•	 Lightweight partition construction reduces waste and structural load.
•	 Open‑plan piping design minimizes consumables during maintenance.
Low-carbon Green Building Materials
•	 Green building materials are used, and more than 65% of indoor area 
materials (including ceilings, flooring, and walls) are green materials.
•	 Locally sourced building materials are preferred, focusing on low 
processing, low energy consumption with low carbon emissions.
•	 Recycled building materials are used wherever possible, in compliance 
with the 3R principles: Reduce, Reuse, and Recycle.
2. Introduction to Green Building Design
In recent years, with rising environmental awareness, self‑developed projects and urban renewal cases have incorporated nine green building indicators 
(green coverage, site water retention, water resources, daily energy savings, CO2 reduction, waste reduction, wastewater/garbage improvement, biodiversity, 
and indoor environment) as design estimation items. Through the evaluation of these nine indicators, the buildings are adapted to local climatic 
conditions to achieve energy efficiency and reduced environmental pollution for carbon reduction. In addition to utilizing native and multi-layered plant 
landscaping designs, when selecting construction materials and equipment, BES not only choose green building materials that meet standards but also 
adopt lightweight designs to reduce waste after the building's life cycle. The thermal insulation properties of materials are also considered, and rainwater 
harvesting facilities are installed to increase water resource recycling.

•	 The total planned electricity use for the Park is approximately 20,000 kW. According to the energy 
planning analysis, the top three energy-consuming systems are the air conditioning (42%), lighting 
(12%), and elevator (7%), collectively accounting for 61% of total consumption. These have been 
designated as the project's “priority energy-saving targets."
•	 All systems are integrated into a smart energy management platform to enable real-time energy 
consumption monitoring, electricity recovery tracking, and carbon emission calculating.
•	 Solar panels are planned to cover over 40% of 
the rooftop area, with a total installed capacity of 
1,152 kW.
•	 The estimated annual electricity generation is 1 
million kWh, effectively offsetting power from 
the public grid and supporting the Park's energy 
self-sufficiency and carbon reduction goals.
Air Conditioning System
•	 A centralized energy center supplies 
air conditioning on demand to reduce 
idle energy consumption.
•	 Using high-efficiency variable 
frequency centrifugal chillers, paired 
with low-load DC inverter magnetic 
bearing chillers, minimizing energy 
waste during nighttime and 
	 off-peak hours.
Lighting System
•	 The entire building is 
planned to use high-
efficiency LED lighting 
systems.
•	 Lighting schedules are 
controlled by zones and 
paired with sensors to 
enhance usage efficiency.
Elevator Energy  Recovery System
•	 Passenger and freight elevators are installed throughout 
the entire area, all equipped with regenerative systems 
that convert kinetic energy into electricity.
•	 Recovered energy is monitored, recorded, and analyzed 
in real time via smart meters.
•	 An energy management platform is used to track 
regenerative electricity, energy savings, and carbon 
reduction contributions.

3. Recycled Materials and Circular Economy
▍Materials Used  GRI 301-1  301-2
The raw materials BES primarily used are construction engineering 
materials. In 2024, BES used a total of 2,074,676.4 metric tons 
of non-renewable materials, with no renewable materials were 
utilized. To reduce environmental impact and achieve waste 
reduction goals, we will further consider increasing the use ratio 
of eco-friendly green building materials (renewable materials) 
such as bio-concrete and green asphalt in our construction 
projects. BES's main products are construction structures, and 
because waste disposal is handled by third-party professional 
contractors, we are unable to provide data on packaging material 
recycling.
▍	Proportion of Recycled and Reused Materials Used 
by BES  GRI 301-2
In 2024, BES used a total of 2,074,676.4 metric tons of materials, 
of which 65,714.5 metric tons were recycled and reused 
materials, accounting for 3.17% of the total.

Most of BES's private construction projects have already adopted the aluminum 
formwork method, effectively reducing waste and enhancing construction quality. 
However, in new construction projects, the use of timber formwork still accounts 
for a significant proportion. Timber formwork typically becomes unusable and 
non-recyclable after using for 4 to 8 times, 
often ending up as waste. In response to the 
need for wood conservation and energy-
saving environmental protection, "aluminum 
formwork," made of aluminum material in 
place of wood, has been gradually and widely 
adopted in ongoing construction projects.

4. User Health and Safety Assurance  GRI 416-1  416-2
To ensure BES provides construction quality and safeguards users' health and safety, no incidents of non-compliance with health and safety laws related to 
products and services occurred in 2024. In construction design, construction planning and execution, BES ensures the following steps are taken to assess 
and mitigate related risks:
To prevent indoor air quality issues arising during construction or renovation and to maintain the comfort and health of construction 
workers, building materials, and users, BES plans an indoor air quality control program before construction begins. This includes detailing the 
installation sequence of materials and protecting or storing absorbent materials, such as panels, insulation, mineral fiber ceilings, and gypsum 
boards, to avoid moisture or contamination. It also requires on-site photo documentation for EEWH certification, including the following items 
in the records:
(1)	 No smoking indoors during construction period.
(2)	 Dust protective equipment worn by indoor 
construction workers.
(3)	 Dust covers installed on all existing HVAC systems.
(4)	 Ventilation and exhaust equipment added in poorly 
ventilated or dusty areas.
(5)	 Photo records of dust protection measures for absorbent building materials.
(6)	 Photos of dust isolation and ventilation measures in wood-cutting zones.
(7)	 Photos of clean indoor environments after construction completion.
(8)	 Monthly EEWH consultant reviews, with dated supporting photos and 
necessary documentation.
(1)	 For all BES's new building projects, during the design phase we review each clause of Chapter 10 ("Accessible Buildings") of the 
Construction Technical Regulations and the related commentary manual on accessible building facilities, and prepare submission drawings 
accordingly.
(2)	 To reduce noise pollution, all BES's new projects design impact sound–insulating structures during the design phase, in accordance with 
Section 9 ("Soundproofing") of Chapter 2 ("General Design Principles") of the Construction Technical Regulations. We also review drainage 
pipe layouts to eliminate impact noise and incorporate vibration-dampening and sound insulation around equipment such as generators.
(3)	 For basic landscaping design in all BES's new projects, we set greenery requirements that exceed regulatory minimums. Layered planting 
landscapes and ecological grass slopes are installed in public areas, terraces, rooftops, gardens, and sidewalk setbacks, with vertical 
greening applied to facades and balconies.
(1)	 BES has built a "Low-Carbon Building Design Technology Database" and a "Carbon Value Database Index" to support the selection of 
building materials and the evaluation of low-carbon building applications during the design phase for the company's various projects.
(2)	 Green building materials used have relevant certification labels.

5. Construction Industry's "Five Standardizations" of Construction
As a pioneer in the construction industry, BES continues to advance the "Five Standardizations of Construction." Moving forward, the company will 
deepen these initiatives to strengthen operational efficiency and achieve sustainable development.
A. Design Standardization  GRI 416-1
BES adheres to the three core principles of "on‑time, on‑quality, and on‑truth" to properly manage the quality of every project. To ensure project quality, BES 
has implemented the ISO 9001:2015 Quality Management System. The headquarters also has a dedicated Quality Department that manages all construction 
phases through a three-tiered quality control system. Additionally, BES regularly conducts random inspections and audits at various phase of construction to 
guarantee quality assurance.

 Quality Control Organization and Division of Responsibilities
Quality control personnel include: professional engineering staff, site managers, quality control managers, and 
quality control engineers, each with clearly defined roles and responsibilities (as shown in the diagram above). 
They are respectively responsible for supervising construction quality, guiding technical and safety measures, 
inspecting materials and construction processes, as well as tracking improvements and conducting quality audits.
 Standardization of Construction Quality Management
Meanwhile, in order to effectively enhance quality management and improve construction quality, BES has 
established a "Seven-in-One Integrated Management System" based on its Site office Management Manual. 
This system tightly integrates multiple key operational processes to ensure that every aspect of quality control 
is comprehensively addressed and implemented. The integrated components include the followings: detailed 
construction planning and precise drawing preparation to ensure construction procedures and details meet 
design specifications; rigorous vendor qualification reviews, material and equipment submissions, mock-up 
production, and approvals to strictly control quality from the source; and integration of construction scheduling, 
public administration, and procurement processes to align all resources and timelines with quality requirements, 
reducing defects caused by management oversight. This systematic Seven-in-One Integrated Management 
approach strengthens the quality management process from planning through execution, thereby significantly 
improving overall construction quality.
B.	Prefabrication of Structural 
Components 
In BES's construction projects, some or all structural 
components are prefabricated in advance at casting 
yards or factories, and then transported to the 
construction site for hoisting and assembly. This 
approach reduces on-site construction processes, 
effectively enhances construction speed, ensures 
quality stability, and minimizes the impact of weather. 
Components such as curbstones and drainage culverts 
have already adopted prefabrication measures.
C. Mechanization of Construction
During the construction process, BES extensively 
utilizes modern construction machinery and 
automated equipment, including hydraulic breakers, 
cutters, excavators, backhoe loader and cranes. 
This helps improve construction efficiency, reduce 
labor intensity, improve working environments, and 
enhance construction accuracy.

BES formulates quality management standards for 
each major work item (such as rebar, formwork, 
concrete, waterproofing, curtain walls, etc.) based 
on contracts, drawings, and regulations.
During construction, BES convenes monthly 
"Construction Meetings" composed of managers 
of each department, with meeting records 
kept as a basis for departments to follow up on 
improvements. Internal audits are conducted every 
six months in accordance with ISO standards, 
and joint quality audits are performed with the 
supervision unit. Audit results are documented, 
and audited units are required to complete 
improvements within a set timeframe. The quality 
control team tracks the issues until closure.
The procedures for identifying, 
reporting, isolating, and removing 
nonconforming items are clearly 
defined. A corrective and preventive 
mechanism is in place to trace, 
analyze, and rectify the root causes of 
anomalies to prevent recurrence.

Environmental Management
3.3 
1.	Environmental Management Policy
	
SASB
IF-EN-160a.2
BES's environmental policy is aligned with the environmental, safety, 
and health policy approved by the Board of Directors. Its objective is 
to prevent pollution caused by construction sites to the surrounding 
environment, such as air, water, and waste. To protect both local 
community and site environments, BES promotes environmentally 
friendly technologies and practices. These include adopting 
community roads; engaging waste disposal services through EPA-
approved and certified contractors; enhancing site environmental 
inspections during construction; increasing the use of water trucks, 
vehicle washing stations, dust suppression, noise barriers, and 
installing automatic sprinkling systems to mitigate dust and noise 
impacts on surrounding communities. Moreover, BES promotes 
on-site greening, strict implementation of runoff wastewater 
control plans, cooperation in ecological surveys, protecting natural 
ecosystems, and promoting the 6S clean-site initiative to reduce 
environmental impact.
In terms of environmental management systems, BES has adopted the 
ISO 14001 Environmental Management System and obtained third-
party certification. The company takes environmental maintenance 
and safety and health of each project very seriously. It formulates 
suitable plans for environmental protection, waste management, 
and construction site runoff control based on each project's specific 
characteristics, aiming to prevent and mitigate any potential 
environmental impacts during construction.
▍Environmental Impact Details
BES mainly works as a contractor for public/private construction projects 
as well as self-developed projects, all of which have direct and actual 
impacts on the environment. Therefore, when determining project 
specifications, the project owner must consider potential environmental 
impacts and conduct environment/ecology assessment. During 
construction, BES actively seeks to prevent and minimize its environmental 
impacts, the protection and preservation of biodiversity also relies on the 
management measures requested by the project owners.

▍Environmental Cost
The environmental cost is for the prevention of various types of 
environmental pollution. For example, air pollution prevention 
includes water trucks, sediment control nets, and vegetation. 
The costs cover the installation of car wash bays, procurement 
of car washing equipment, wastewater treatment equipment, 
waste management, environmental monitoring instruments, 
ecological conservation monitoring, equipment procurement/
update and other fees (inspection and verification). Costs 
vary depending on the size of each project. For example. BES 
invested a total of NTD 24.1 million for the water recovery 
equipment at its EcoTech Industrial Park.
▍	Environmental Management Measures and Actual 
Actions
BES's environmental management measures encompass at 
minimum the following during the construction phase: air 
quality monitoring, water pollution prevention and runoff 
control, waste management, ecological conservation, and 
environmental education and training. For projects aiming 
to obtain LEED certifications and ensure sustainable site 
development, BES submits a "Construction Site Runoff 
Wastewater Pollution Reduction Plan" or a "Construction 
Activity Pollution Prevention Plan" prior to construction and 
ensures strict implementation throughout the construction 
period. To mitigate the heat island effect and its impact on the 
microclimate, human beings, and wildlife, BES plans to install 
green roofs or use roofing and hardscape materials with high 
Solar Reflectance Index (SRI) or Solar Reflectance (SR) values. 
To reduce excessive external lighting and light pollution, BES 
minimizes site lighting and adopts mitigation technologies, 
such as fixtures angled below 90 degrees, low-reflectivity 
surfaces, and spotlights with narrow beam angles. In order 
to lower building water consumption, BES also installs water 
fixtures that meet LEED standards, thereby reducing tap water 
demand and easing the load on wastewater treatment systems.
2. Air Pollution Prevention
To prevent air pollution, BES follows ISO 14001 environmental management system and 
follows the PDCA principle. The company also implements legally required pollution 
control measures to prevent environmental contamination.
▍Dust Control Measures for Construction
Among all sources of air pollution, the largest source is the dust from construction. To 
ensure the quality of life of nearby residents, BES, installs overflow protection bases) and 
dust-control mesh or tarp, assigns staff to patrol the construction site regularly, replaces 
outdated machinery and sprays water on the ground before work begins to protect the air 
quality of the construction site and minimize impacts.

bases around the construction 
site perimeter.

to prevent exhaust emissions from

be included in the daily automatic 
checks and recorded.

3. Water Resource Management
▍Water Conservation Measures  
At different phases of operation, BES adopts various approaches to conserve water. Prior to 
construction, BES evaluates strategies to reduce runoff wastewater pollution. During construction, 
BES actively engages in the recycling and reuse of wastewater generated from the construction 
process. BES approaches water conservation through comprehensive strategies, including water 
usage management, water reduction, rainwater harvesting and reuse, and wastewater recycling. 
These strategies are developed by considering water sourcing, water-saving technologies, and 
conservation practices. BES also integrates experience from individual projects and practical 
implementation efforts to establish effective water resource management. The methods include 
the following:
▍Daily Inspection and Maintenance
	Personnel will be assigned to perform daily 
sweeping and maintenance of the roads around 
the entrance and exit areas. They will conduct 
inspections of the road conditions around the 
construction site in the morning and afternoon 
and document the daily cleaning status by taking 
photographs for record-keeping. Electronic 
display boards are also installed to provide daily 
air quality information.
	The project will set up digital signage to display 
daily air quality information. The personnel 
will monitor the Air Quality Index (AQI) from 
nearby monitoring stations daily and adjust 
construction activities within the work area based 
on the displayed AQI values and strengthen dust 
suppression measures as needed.
	Daily construction activities will be recorded in the 
construction log and the staff will continuously 
observe the air quality at monitoring stations and 
adjust work processes accordingly to prevent 
deterioration of air quality in local areas.
▍ODS Emissions Status   GRI 305-6
Through various air pollution control measures, 
BES conducts regular equipment monitoring 
by assigned personnel and reports air pollutant 
emissions quarterly in accordance with the Air 
Pollution Control Act. In 2024, no ozone-depleting 
substances (ODS) emitted.
Wastewater Recycling
A reservoir is set up next 
to the construction site' s 
car wash area to store and 
recycle the dirty water 
used for vehicle washing. 
After sedimentation and 
purification, the water can 
be reused.
Rainwater Recovery
The water required for the 
concrete curing process is 
the rainwater collected from 
using water- stopping piers/
thresholds or reduced using 
curing agents. The collected 
rainwater, after passing through 
sedimentation, can also be 
reused for road cleaning to 
suppress dust.
Installation of Equipment 
with Water Efficiency 
Label
BES follows the policies 
of the Water Resources 
Agency under the Ministry of 
Economic Affairs to encourage 
consumers to choose water-
efficient products. Water-
saving equipment with water 
efficiency labels is installed 
in both the Company' s 
headquarters and site offices.
Installation of Wastewater 
Treatment Facilities
Wastewater treatment facilities 
are installed at discharge 
points to ensure that the 
discharged wastewater meets 
the discharge standards.

▍Water Pollution Prevention and Runoff Wastewater Management
During the construction period, the main sources of water pollution include wastewater from various construction activities, domestic sewage, equipment 
wastewater, etc. To reduce pollution, BES has implemented the following water pollution prevention measures:
•	 Installation of complete barrier fences and foundations within the construction 
site to effectively prevent wastewater from overflowing outside the work area.
•	 Each construction site will implement a runoff wastewater pollution reduction 
plan as approved. Suitable measures such as intercepting ditches, settling 
tanks, sedimentation tanks, or wash bays will be set up according to the site' 
s scope. These measures will collect wastewater from the work area through 
intercepting ditches to control the discharge of sediments and pollutants. After 
natural gravitational settling, regular sampling and testing will be conducted 
to ensure that the discharged wastewater complies with the Effluent Standards.
•	 Regularly dispatch personnel to clean the drainage systems around the 
construction site and maintain equipment such as drainage covers and 
sediment control nets.
•	 Cover building materials and excavated soil or earthwork stored 
within the site to prevent runoff caused by rainfall.
•	 Implement waste management practices to prevent waste from 
polluting surface runoff.
•	 Maintain and clean roads. Install sediment control nets above public 
drainage covers on roads surrounding each construction site to 
prevent soil and debris from entering the drainage system.
•	 Office area and dormitory domestic wastewater is treated using 
environmentally certified FRP sewage treatment tanks. After 
treatment to meet discharge water standards, it is discharged. 
Portable toilets set up on the work site are professionally serviced and 
handled to meet discharge water standards before being discharged.
▍	Water Resource Management and Water Pollution Prevention 
GRI 303-3
All water consumption at BES's headquarters is domestic water. According to 
the invoices from the water company, all water sources for the site offices are 
the temporary water supplies that sourced by the water company (third-party 
water). All water consumed by BES is domestic water consumed for site offices, 
offices, construction and cleaning. In 2024, BES expanded the boundary for water 
consumption calculation and yet the overall water withdrawal was still on the low 
side, testament to the company's water management.
▍Water Withdrawal  GRI 303-3
In 2024, BES's total water withdrawal amounted to 269.072 million liters (ML), 
with third-party supply (tap water) as the sole source, accounting for the full 
269.072 ML. All construction sites prioritize the use of tap water to ensure 
water quality stability and to minimize the impact on natural water sources. 
The company also conducts routine inspections of pipes and valves to reduce 
leakage and waste, and implements water optimization measures to lower water 
consumption during construction. Water withdrawal data is primarily derived 
from water bills and on-site meter readings. The compiled figures are based on 
the assumption that all construction-related water usage is supplied by tap water, 
excluding temporary rainwater collection and any unrecorded reused water.

4. Waste Management   GRI 306-3
The waste generated by BES are mainly construction wastes. Improper handling of construction wastes may also cause pollution or environmental burden. To 
minimize waste generation, BES has implemented the ISO 14001 Environmental Management System and applies the PDCA cycle and the 6S procedures—
Sort, Set in Order, Shine, Standardize, Sustain, and Security—to ensure the effective execution of all related operations, including waste management.
Each site office is responsible for overseeing the implementation of environmental protection measures. Additionally, external verification is conducted by 
the third-party certification institute, SGS Taiwan Ltd.
Suppliers are required, through a signedCommitment Letter, to comply with the Waste Disposal Act and other relevant 
laws and regulations when handling waste. They must also follow BES's waste sorting and are encouraged to engage in 
material recycling.
◆ Proper Sorting
-	 Under the "Domestic Procurement Operating Guidelines," suppliers must manage waste in accordance with 
environmental regulations. Contract clauses stipulate that suppliers must comply with environmental protection and 
labor safety laws, as well as BES's "Contractor Safety, Health, and Environmental Protection Guidelines," which include 
provisions for handling construction waste. Violations may result in contract termination or deductions in payment, 
depending on severity.
-	 Certified waste transporters deliver waste to approved recycling facilities. BES requires contractors to submit related 
proof documents, which are reviewed by site offices or engineering departments before payment estimation and 
approval.
◆ Data Tracking
All waste is weighed and recorded by the Occupational Safety and Health Department using a digital platform for 
regular review and tracking.
◆	Certified contractors determine whether waste should be recycled or disposed of.
◆	Auditing and Improvement: Site offices or engineering departments audit the process, with 
the Cost Estimation and Control Department performing further checks in accordance with 
regulations. Payment is made only after all verification steps are completed. Any discrepancies 
found must be rectified.

suppliers of disposal, employing a three-tiered approach to reduce potential impacts:

5.  Environmental Violations in 2024  GRI 2-27   SASB  IF-EN-160a.1
In 2024, a total of 24 environmental violations resulted in fines issued by the 
Ministry of Environment, amounting to NTD 606,400. The violations were 
categorized as "environmental-related incidents," involving breaches of the Air 
Pollution Control Act, the Regulations Governing Air Pollution Control Equipment 
for Construction Projects, the Waste Disposal Act, and the Noise Control Act. 
BES has completed corrective actions and implemented several improvement 
measures as required by the relevant authorities. These include the installation of 
wastewater recycling systems, updates to building equipment maintenance SOPs, 
enhanced waste sorting and audit mechanisms during construction, staff training, 
and follow-up audits. Improvement reports were submitted to the relevant 
authorities. In addition, BES did not incur any "major violations" during the year 
(defined as a single fine amounting to NTD 500,000 or more).
▍Waste Generation and Disposal
As a company in the construction industry, BES primarily generates construction waste. All such waste is handled in accordance with the Waste Disposal Act and 
is transported by waste removal contractors approved by the Department of Environmental Protection to qualified waste treatment or recycling facilities. Prior 
to construction, BES prepares a construction waste management plan that includes setting recycling targets and clearly listing at least five recyclable materials. 
The plan also estimates the percentage of total waste these materials represent. BES immediately sorts waste upon generation, and the waste is promptly loaded 
onto vehicles for centralized management. The vehicles are tightly covered with tarpaulins and only permitted to leave the site after being thoroughly washed.
For contracted projects, BES adheres to the specifications set by owners. The largest category of waste is excavated soil, which is transported directly to soil 
treatment sites as required by regulations. BES also enforces controls on vehicles transporting loose construction materials (such as sand and gravel), waste, or 
excavated soil and rock. These vehicles must be fully covered with tightly secured tarpaulins and cleaned at designated washing stations before leaving the site. 
Additionally, machinery maintenance is conducted off-site at designated facilities, and used oil is collected and handled by authorized recycling vendors.
In accordance with the "Regulations for the Reporting and Management of Industrial Waste," BES assigns its Occupational Safety and Health Department to 
compile and periodically review data. A digital management platform is used to track the volume and destination of various waste types. Total waste volume 
is calculated based on billing statements from third-party treatment providers, ensuring transparency and regulatory compliance. In 2024, according to third-
party billing records, BES generated a total of 11,196.25 metric tons of construction waste. All waste is classified as general industrial waste under the Waste 
Disposal Act, including materials such as concrete, bricks, metals, and wood. Since waste treatment is outsourced to third-party providers, BES only maintains 
data on waste generation. As qualified recycling or disposal facilities typically sort and process waste only after accumulating sufficient quantities, BES is unable 
to confirm the actual volume of recycled materials or provide statistical data on final treatment methods such as incineration or landfill.

6. Biodiversity  GRI 304-1  304-4
▍	Biodiversity and Ecological Conservation – Wu River Niaozuitan Artificial 
Lake Project
▍Biodiversity Impact and Management  GRI 304-2
BES places great importance on biodiversity and, in accordance with owner requirements, commissions third-
party institutions to conduct ecological assessments. As stipulated in owner contracts, 12 site offices are required 
to conduct outsourced ecological assessments. However, due to variations in project start dates and the frequency 
of assessments required by contract, only one site office needed to carry out assessments in 2024. Following 
contractual obligations, BES evaluates the environmental and ecological impacts and completes the corresponding 
ecological surveys and reporting procedures. Although construction in the lake area has been completed, the 
professional contractor engaged by BES continues to conduct regular ecological assessments at the site through 
November 2024. As the lake area is a hotspot for leopard cat activity, an indicator 
species for conservation in Taiwan that is highly sensitive to habitat quality and 
human disturbance, it serves as an effective measure of the ecological health of 
the construction zone. Leopard cats are active during dawn, dusk, and nighttime, 
which overlaps with the time of human activity. Moreover, the construction of 
local service roads and the artificial lake attracting more visitors has increased 
the risk of roadkill. To minimize these impacts, BES pays special attention to 
the conservation status of the leopard cat. To prevent and mitigate roadkill 
incidents or other ecological impacts, BES adopts four key principles in handling 
protected wildlife near construction sites: avoidance, minimization, mitigation, 
and compensation, aiming to reduce ecological disturbance.
The Niaozuitan Site office is located in Caotun Township, Nantou County, and is 
responsible for carrying out the Wu River Niaozuitan Artificial Lake Project (Lake Area 
Project) of the Central Region Water Resources Branch, Water Resources Agency, Ministry 
of Economic Affairs (hereinafter referred to as the Central Region Water Resources 
Branch). The project covers an area of 283.03 hectares and involves the construction of 
an artificial lake with a storage capacity of about 14.5 million cubic meters. The scope 
of work includes embankment construction, earthwork moving and transportation, 
waterway systems, hydraulic structures, road construction, bridge construction, 
landscaping, and more. The terrestrial animal species in this area include Class I protected 
species in Taiwan (such as leopard cat), 14 species of Class II protected birds (such as 
crested goshawk) and 4 species of Class III protected birds (such as oriental pratincole). 
The fish species found in the aquatic ecosystem are commonly seen in streams of western 
Taiwan, including the critically endangered and endemic species Squalidus banarescui.

▍Environmental Monitoring
BES has installed infrared automated cameras in 
the project area and surrounding areas to monitor 
multiple cohabiting species simultaneously. This 
will provide a comprehensive understanding of the 
status of biodiversity, particularly large mammals and 
migratory birds, in the monitored area. To protect the 
local ecosystem, BES prohibits its workers from hunting, 
trading, possessing, or consuming wild animals. BES 
assigns personnel to patrol the construction site daily 
to conduct inspections and maintain records on the 
ecosystem. If injured animals are discovered, BES will 
apply first aid and then determine whether or not to 
transport them to conservation authorities for care. 
▍Ecological Conservation Collaboration
Furthermore, in collaboration with the Central Region Water Resources Branch, the Biodiversity 
Research Center at the Academia Sinica, National Pingtung University of Science and 
Technology, National Chung Hsing University, National Tsing Hua University, the Endemic 
Species Research Institute, the Society for Wildlife And Nature (SWAN), and the Taiwan Water 
Resources Conservation Alliance, we have jointly established the Ecological Conservation Task 
Force for the Wu River Niaozuitan Artificial Lake Project. This task force provides decision-
making consultations and recommendations on matters related to ecological conservation for 
the Wu River Niaozuitan Artificial Lake Project.
To enhance the management of the progress and effectiveness of various ecological 
conservation measures, we provide weekly reports based on the tasks, content, and progress 
of the project commissioned by the Central Region Water Resources Branch. These reports 
include details on the implementation content and methods of each task, as well as reviews and 
recommendations for future actions, enabling the Central Region Water Resources Branch to 
have real-time insights into the status of each task.
 Environmental Monitoring
 Infrared Automated Cameras Installed
 Personnel Patrol
▍Reduce Environmental Impact
Preventive measures against noise and air pollution from 
various sources (e.g., machinery) are implemented, including 
the installation of dust screens, construction fences, 
construction pathways, intercepting ditches, sedimentation 
tanks, car washing facilities, and tree transplantation. 
Additionally, infrared cameras support monitoring, 
ecological protection awareness campaigns are conducted, 
and waste is managed centrally. Within the project area, 
sweet potatoes and other crops are grown on fertile soil 
piles for consumption by local large mammals and avian 
species. This helps guide them away from the construction 
area, reducing the impact on the environment and avoiding 
disruptions to local wildlife. BES uses infrared cameras for 
identification and dynamic data archiving to monitor the 
conservation outcomes of leopard cats. Since 2017, a total 
of 22 individuals have been identified, with three confirmed as stable resident individuals. This 
indicates potential for the continued survival and reproduction of this native species. These three 
individuals have consistently appeared since 2021. Their movement patterns show established 
territorial behavior, suggesting they can be regarded as a stable resident population. As of 
June 2024, monitoring data indicate no significant disturbances to the activities of these three 
individuals due to construction.

into the leopard cat apartment.

During the construction period, BES promoted ecological 
conservation awareness among construction personnel. In 
accordance with owner requirements, BES conducted ecological 
assessment training for the workers of Niaozuitan Artificial Lake 
Project. Before the lake area project in 2024, 13 required owner-
funded training sessions were completed between 2019 and 
2023. However, BES continues to prioritize ecological protection, 
therefore, BES also held an additional 3-hour training session 
attended by 15 participants in 2024.
▍Ecological Conservation  GRI 304-3
The vitality of alien species must not be underestimated. BES assigns personnel 
to remove alien species in the project area regularly, such as mikania, mimosa, 
parthenium weed, Amazon sailfin catfish, cane toad and apple snail to protect 
Taiwan's native biodiversity. 
In response to the reporting of cane toads at the end of 2021, the project team 
launched a monitoring and removal program targeting this alien species. Through 
community collaboration, volunteer participation, and patrol actions, the initiative 
aimed to reduce the potential threat posed by alien species to the local ecosystem. 
The results of removal were as follows: In 2022: 63 patrols were conducted, with 
ongoing accumulation of removed individuals. In 2023: 94 patrols were carried 
out, and approximately 1,500 cane toads were removed. In 2024: 35 patrols were 
conducted, with the number of removed cane toads surpassing 30,000.

▍Eco-friendly Measures
BES understands the habits of the animals in the project area. To 
protect these creatures, BES has implemented many conservation 
measures to co-exist and co-prosper with them.
Additionally, BES strictly prohibits the use of pesticides, herbicides, 
chemicals and any other animal-harming substances in the 
protected area to ensure food sources for the wildlife. The company 
follows its monitoring plan to track changes in the terrestrial 
ecosystems in the construction areas to understand their changes 
during the construction period.
In terms of controlling stray animals at the construction site, BES 
have taken various measures. These include posting relevant 
warning signs and notices in the construction area, covering 
food waste containers, implementing food waste recycling, and 
collaborating with animal protection organizations to carry out 
Trap-Neuter-Vaccinate-Return (TNVR) programs. These efforts aim 
to enhance the effectiveness of stray animal control.

1. Workforce Overview
BES is dedicated to fostering a diverse, equitable, and friendly 
workplace culture, firmly opposing all forms of discrimination, 
and respecting the diverse values of all ethnic groups, genders, 
ages, nationalities, political stances, and religious beliefs. In 
all aspects of human resource management, including talent 
acquisition, employment, development, promotion, and 
retention, BES adheres to principles of fairness, ensuring no 
differential treatment based on personal background. We are 
committed to providing employees with equal opportunities 
and an environment for growth. Simultaneously, we prioritize 
professional development and competitive compensation and 
benefits, aspiring for every employee to fully leverage their 
talents, continuously grow within the company, and collectively 
advance towards the goals of sustainable development and 
long-term value creation with the enterprise.
▍Company Workforce Overview  GRI 
2-7  
2-8  
As of the end of 2024, BES employed a total of 2,138 
employees, including both headquarter and site offices 
personnel. This represents an increase of 375 individuals 
compared to the previous year, primarily due to a significant 
rise in engineering staff as projects entered their peak phase. 
Of the total workforce, 1,680 were male and 458 were female. 
In terms of employee composition, there were 2,131 full-time 
employees and 7 part-time employees. Additionally, in 2024, 
there were 240 non-employees, including cleaning staff and 
security personnel. The total workforce increased by 21.7% in 
2024 compared to 2023.
BES is also committed to fostering a diverse and rich talent 
pool. This includes safeguarding employment opportunities 
for individuals with disabilities and increasing the proportion 
of local residents serving as senior executives at overseas 
locations, all aimed at promoting diversity, mutual prosperity, 
and enhancing the company's overall competitiveness.

▍Diverse Employee Composition  GRI 405-1
BES aligns with SDG 8: "Decent Work and Economic Growth" by providing equal employment 
opportunities to individuals of different genders and ages, and by safeguarding job opportunities for 
other minority groups in accordance with government regulations, ensuring a diverse workforce.
BES is gradually increasing the proportion of female managers and employees. According to employee 
data statistics at the end of 2024, non-managerial female employees accounted for approximately 19.6% 
of the total workforce, while female managers constituted about 1.9%. The total proportion of all female 
employees was approximately 21.4%. The company will continue to increase the representation of female 
employees and managers in the future, while effectively protecting women's employment rights.
The proportion of middle-aged and older workers (over 50 years old) at BES is 30.4%. In 2024, the 
company employed 17 individuals with disabilities (including 5 women) and 18 Indigenous people 
(including 7 women) as part of its commitment to supporting vulnerable and minority groups. 
Additionally, apart from local employees, BES had 908 foreign employees in 2024, a 46.9% increase 
compared to 2023.

▍	Proportion of Senior Management Hired from 
the Local Community GRI 202-2
To foster local prosperity and talent development, BES employed 
a total of 21 senior management personnel working and residing 
in Taiwan in 2024. This includes positions such as General 
Manager, Deputy General Manager, Manager, and various 
departmental sub-management roles. All of these individuals are 
local residents of Taiwan, accounting for 100% of these positions. 
This demonstrates the company's continued commitment to 
implementing local talent cultivation and promotion systems, 
thereby supporting local economic and social sustainable 
development.
▍Employee Turnover and Changes  GRI 401-1
New Employee
BES utilizes diverse and open recruitment channels to select 
suitable talent, with a steady growth in the new hire rate over 
the past three years. Recruitment channels include publishing 
job advertisements, collaborating with recruitment agencies, 
employee referrals, and campus recruitment. In 2024, BES hired 
442 new employees to meet the company's continuous growth 
in talent demand. Of these, 305 were male and 137 were female, 
with employees aged 31-50 (inclusive) accounting for the largest 
proportion at 48.42%.
Employee Turnover and Retention
Regarding employee retention, BES's rate of employee turnover was approximately 26.3% in 2022 
and 24.2% in 2023. In 2024, a total of 328 employees departed, comprising 230 males and 98 females, 
resulting in an overall turnover rate of approximately 26.3%. Although this represents a slight increase 
of 2%, BES will continue to strengthen work-life balance, enhance management capabilities, and offer 
career development opportunities to promote employee retention.

Parental Leave  GRI 401-3
BES complies with the Act of Gender Equality in Employment and champions SDG 5: "Gender Equality," supporting employees' rights to raise children and 
safeguarding their right to parental leave. Any BES employee who has been employed for at least six months can apply for parental leave without pay before 
their child reaches three years of age. The leave can extend until the child turns three, but not exceeding two years. Employees can continue to participate in 
their existing social insurance during parental leave.
In 2024, 52 BES employees were eligible for and applied for parental leave, resulting in an application rate of 11.54%. The return-to-work rate for eligible 
employees in the same year was 75%, and the retention rate after one year was 33.33%. Recognizing the nature of the engineering industry, BES will 
strengthen its efforts to develop a more supportive work environment and safeguards to better care for employees and their families.

2. Company Human Rights and Labor Rights Protection  GRI 2-23  201-3  402-1  406-1  407-1  408-1  409-1  410-1  411-1
BES strictly adheres to international standards and labor employment laws across all its operating locations. We prohibit the employment of child labor under 
16 years of age, forced labor, and any improper employment discrimination. We also require our suppliers to comply with these same regulations. The company 
is committed to safeguarding labor rights, including minimum wage, working hours (including overtime), insurance, leave, retirement pension schemes, 
notice periods for contract termination, freedom of association, and collective bargaining rights. We provide equal employment opportunities and treatment, 
without differentiation based on race, gender, religion, political or social origin, or other factors. In 2024, neither the company nor its suppliers experienced any 
significant risks or incidents of discrimination, child labor, forced labor, indigenous rights infringements, or other violations of labor human rights.
BES refers to international human rights norms, including the International Covenant on Civil and Political 
Rights, the United Nations Global Compact's Ten Principles, and the International Labour Organization's 
Declaration on Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work, to formulate its human rights policy. This policy, 
signed and approved by the Board of Directors, fully embodies the company's spirit of respecting and 
protecting human rights. Key highlights of BES's human rights policy include:
BES actively promotes human rights 
education and training to enhance 
all employees' understanding and 
appreciation of human rights issues. 
In 2024, human rights-related 
courses were conducted, with a total 
of 2,480 participants and 2,659 hours 
of training. BES also ensures that 
security personnel receive human 
rights education training; in 2024, 
a total of 208 security personnel 
participated, each receiving 3 
hours of training, achieving a 100% 
participation rate.
To safeguard employee rights, 
BES has also established a 
Workplace Violence Prevention 
Statement, which clearly stipulates 
that company supervisors 
must not engage in workplace 
bullying or violence, including 
physical, psychological, verbal, 
sexual harassment, or stalking 
harassment.
Prohibition of Child Labor / 
Illegal Migrant Workers
BES complies with labor, health, 
safety, and environmental 
regulations in its operating 
locations, as well as relevant 
international standards. We prohibit 
the employment of child labor and 
illegal migrant workers and do not 
accept any suppliers who engage in 
child labor or forced labor.
Non-Discrimination
We do not discriminate based on race, class, 
language, ideology, religion, political affiliation, 
origin, birthplace, gender, sexual orientation, 
age, marital status, pregnancy, appearance, facial 
features, or disability. We are jointly committed to 
creating a dignified, safe, equal, and harassment-
free work environment.
Healthy and Safe Workplace
 In addition to strictly complying 
with all labor laws and regulations, 
BES is dedicated to building a 
healthy, safe, and comfortable 
workplace environment. We 
regularly arrange in-service health 
examinations for all employees, 
with workplace nurses proactively 
providing care to safeguard 
employee health. We regularly 
assign employees to participate in 
first-aid training and retraining to 
to ensure effective response in the 
event of an incident.
Prohibition of Forced Labor
While considering each 
employee's career development 
and employment rights, BES 
strictly prohibits forcing or 
coercing any unwilling individual 
into labor.
Prohibition of Sexual Harassment
BES promotes gender equality and has established mechanisms 
for preventing, reporting, and disciplining sexual harassment. 
Awareness campaigns are conducted regularly. A Sexual 
Harassment Complaint Handling Committee has also been 
established to promptly address incidents when they occur.

▍Company Human Rights Grievance Mechanism  GRI 2-25
BES is committed to respecting and protecting the human rights of all employees and stakeholders. Adhering to the Universal Declaration of Human Rights, the 
UN Guiding Principles on Business and Human Rights (UNGPs), and domestic labor laws, we have established clear grievance and remediation mechanisms to 
ensure that human rights-related concerns are properly addressed.
2. Processing Procedure
3. Implementation Effectiveness and 
Improvement Directions
BES will conduct regular reviews every three 
years, analyzing and evaluating different 
types of workplace violence to provide 
feedback and revision suggestions for the 
organization's prevention policies and 
measures. In 2024, one sexual harassment 
case was reported. The investigation 
confirmed the incident, and the sexual 
harassment was established. BES notified 
the Taipei City Government Department 
of Labor in accordance with Article 13, 
Paragraph 4 of the Sexual Harassment 
Prevention Act. Concurrently, BES has 
revised its "Unlawful Infringement 
Operating Procedures" to provide more 
timely assistance to victims and prevent the 
recurrence of sexual harassment cases.
BES will continue to review and optimize its 
complaints procedure and integrate human 
rights risks into its operational management 
and training system to mitigate potential 
human rights impact risks.
01
02
03
04
BES's Human Resources unit is responsible for receiving complaints. It must complete 
the confirmation of receipt within 7 days of receiving a complaint and designate 
dedicated personnel to initiate an investigation.
(1)	 Upon confirmation of receipt, the dedicated personnel will initiate an 
investigation according to relevant procedures, simultaneously notifying the unit 
supervisor or security personnel of the case to jointly assist and cooperate with 
the investigation.
(2)	 If necessary, arrangements will be made for the affected employee to seek 
medical attention or be accompanied to file a police report, or to escalate the 
report.
(3)	 An incident report/complaint form will be completed, and counseling referrals (or 
psychiatric consultation) will be arranged based on the employee's needs.
(4)	 All relevant handling measures will be fully documented and properly preserved 
in a confidential manner.
During the investigation, the Human Resources unit should provide immediate, 
continuous, and supportive protective measures to the affected employee as 
needed. These immediate protective measures may include work adjustments or 
changes, arranging appropriate leave or flexible adjustments to job duties, legal 
assistance, and psychological counseling resources.
Complaint cases should be investigated within two months, but this period may be 
extended by one month if necessary.

▍BES Labor Rights Measures  GRI 2-30  201-3  402-1
Working 
Hours
Termination 
and 
Retirement 
Policy
Collective 
Bargaining 
Agreements
Major 
Operational 
Changes
For full-time employees, normal working hours are 8 hours per day and 40 hours per week.
If overtime is required due to special circumstances, the total daily working hours must not exceed 12 hours, and the monthly 
overtime limit is 46 hours.
In accordance with the Labor Standards Act, overtime pay is provided for work exceeding 8 hours per day, and employees cannot 
be forced to work overtime.
Major operational changes that impact employee rights and the corresponding response measures are implemented after 
discussion in labor-management meetings.
If the company needs to lay off employees due to major operational changes, it strictly adheres to the Labor Standards Act and the 
Act for Worker Protection of Mass Layoffs by providing advance notice:
• 10 days prior for employees with service seniority of three months to less than one year；
• 20 days prior for employees with service seniority of one year to less than three years；
•	 30 days prior for employees with service seniority of three years or more.
No major operational changes occurred in 2024.
If there's a need to terminate an employment relationship with an employee, the company adheres to Article 16 of the Labor 
Standards Act, providing advance notice of contract termination, severance pay, and job-search leave.
BES contributes to the new labor pension system for employees monthly, in accordance with the Labor Standards Act, at 6% of 
their total salary. The total contribution for 2024 amounted to NTD 47,723,025. For employees with seniority under the old labor 
pension system, an additional 7% of their total salary is deposited monthly into a dedicated retirement reserve account at the Bank 
of Taiwan. The total contribution for the old system in 2024 was NTD 7,028,279. These retirement reserves are deposited monthly 
and calculated based on the annual closing balance. (The retirement system is not covered migrant workers.)
BES employees have formed a labor union, which operates under the "BES Trade Union Articles of Association" and "BES Trade 
Union Operating Rules," which are established in accordance with the "Labor Union Act" and its enforcement rules. BES follows 
the "BES Trade Union Member Representative Assembly Organization Rules" to elect union member representatives. These 
representatives then attend meetings and elect directors, alternate directors, supervisors, and alternate supervisors by secret ballot 
and proportional representation, according to the "BES Trade Union Board of Directors and Supervisors Election Regulations." The 
union holds regular monthly board meetings and member representative assemblies.
In 2024, a total of four labor-management conferences were held, with relevant business managers from the company attending 
each one. Both labor and management sides engaged in full coordination and communication to jointly safeguard employee 
rights. Union members constitute 94.6% of the entire company's workforce, with those not joining the union being department 
supervisors. BES has not yet signed a collective bargaining agreement with the union as it is still in the coordination phase. 
However, BES highly values all matters raised by the union and is committed to striving for their achievement or improvement, 
fostering a harmonious labor-management working environment.

3. Remuneration and Benefits
▍Company Wage Levels  GRI 202-1  405-2  
BES offers a fair and competitive remuneration policy, ensuring that employees are not subject to wage discrimination based on differences in gender, race, 
or religion. The salary standards for new employees are determined based on the educational background and work experience required for their positions. 
After employment, annual salary adjustments and promotions are made based on work performance, with corresponding remuneration provided. Each 
year, based on the company's operational goals and profitability, employees' professional knowledge and skills, job responsibilities, and performance are 
comprehensively evaluated to provide them with reasonable remuneration, benefits, and rewards, enabling them to grow alongside the company.
In 2024, all BES employees' salaries were above the local minimum wage standard. The average annual total remuneration for non-managerial men was 
NTD 1,019,980, and for non-managerial women was NTD 792,916, both exceeding the local average wage. The ratio of average annual total remuneration 
for non-managerial men to non-managerial women was 1.29:1.

▍Company Benefits Program  GRI 401-2  
BES offers a comprehensive benefits program to all full-time employees (excluding 
temporary or part-time staff). In addition to statutory entitlements such as labor insurance, 
health insurance, annual leave, maternity leave, and parental leave, we provide a wide range 
of employee benefits. Our goal is to enhance employee well-being and create a positive and 
happy workplace environment.
To motivate employees and strengthen their sense of belonging to the company, BES has 
established an Employee Welfare Committee in accordance with the Employee Welfare Fund 
Act. This committee is responsible for administering various employee benefits, organizing 
welfare and recreational activities, and distributing gifts and bonuses to BES employees.
