▍Employee Training and Development System   GRI 404-1  
BES provides a comprehensive employee training system, offering diverse internal and external learning resources to current employees based on annual 
training plans, thereby supporting their career development. Our training curriculum coversnew hire orientation, core competencies, management skills, 
general knowledge, professional expertise, and foreign language training. This caters to the developmental needs of employees at different levels, ensuring 
they possess fundamental work abilities, a positive work attitude, and knowledge for self-career planning. Additionally, the company regularly organizes 
specialized courses and in-person seminars focusing on new technologies, core skills, and market trends. These initiatives help employees continuously 
refine their expertise, broaden their interdisciplinary perspectives, and strengthen their diverse competitiveness.

In 2024, BES organized and commissioned 253 in-house training 
courses and arranged 355 external training courses. The total 
expenditure on training was NTD 5,821,939, marking a 23.15% 
increase compared to the previous year. This investment provided 
employees with more intensive education and training across 
various professional competencies, with a particular focus on 
employee professional development, ultimately assisting in their 
growth.
▍Performance and Career Development   GRI 404-3  
BES regularly conducts performance and career development reviews for its employees. Through 
initial goal setting, periodic performance evaluations, and interviews, we assess work performance 
to provide appropriate rewards and promotion opportunities. This process aims to comprehensively 
improve work efficiency, maintain BES's competitiveness within the industry, and assist employees 
in their career development. By implementing the setting of key performance indicators, BES fosters 
employees' core expertise and fully supports communication regarding performance between 
employees and management, thereby strengthening the effectiveness of performance management.
▍Employee Assistance Programs   GRI 404-2  
BES is committed to providing diverse support measures to foster employees' professional 
development and work adaptation. For professional training, we offer necessary internal and 
external educational resources to current employees based on annual training plans, enhancing their 
professional skills and competitiveness. Additionally, we promote a succession talent development 
program, which identifies high-potential individuals and provides management competency training 
to elevate the capabilities of key talent. This is integrated with a compensation and reward system 
to strengthen talent development and retention. Simultaneously, BES actively cultivates a friendly 
workplace environment, regularly sharing mental and physical well-being information and organizing 
lectures. We also implement relevant policies and programs to care for and support employees. If 
an employee is laid off due to business adjustments, BES also notifies employment service centers in 
accordance with the law to assist them with career transition or re-employment.
Note: Employees not included in the performance review are part-time employees, employees who have been with the company for 
less than 3 months, and employees currently on leave without pay.

Occupational Safety and Health (Material Topic)
4.2 
Material Topic Management Approach
SDGs
SDG 3 Good Health and Well-being
SDG 8 Decent Work and Economic Growth
Impact 
Assessment
Positive Impact: 	 Effective occupational hygiene and safety management can reduce occupational disaster risks, enhance employee health and job 
satisfaction, thereby increasing productivity and corporate image.
Negative Impact: 	Poor occupational health and safety management may lead to occupational injuries, health problems and legal liabilities, affecting 
enterprise operations and damaging brand reputation.
Policies and 
Commitments
BES's Environmental, Safety, and Health (ESH) policy prioritizes "Safety First." We are committed to continuous improvement across all aspects, 
including personnel health and well-being, environmental protection, risk management, regulatory compliance, contractual requirements, and full 
employee participation, to provide a safe and secure workplace for our colleagues. This ESH policy has been signed by the Chairman and promulgated 
throughout the company for strict implementation.
The policy content includes: 
• Creating a high-quality, healthy, and safe environment；
• Strengthening autonomous workplace safety and health management；
• Safeguarding lives and ensuring safety in the workplace；
• All employees adhering to rules and continuously striving for improvement；
•	 Fostering a safety culture through full employee participation.
Responsible 
Unit
Occupational Safety and Health Management Department（Policy formulation and promotion）
Engineering Units（Execution）

Goals

Mechanism
BES adhere to all management procedures of the ISO 45001:2018 Occupational Safety and Health Management System, continuously passing 
certifications and maintaining the system's effectiveness to achieve zero major occupational accidents.

zero fatalities.

Actions
1.	 The number of major occupational safety incidents decreased compared to the previous year (from 3 incidents to 1).
2.	 100% acquisition rate of Taiwan Occupational Safety Card for all company employees.
3.	 Self-inspection rate of 83%, with an average of 1.7 non-conformities found per site office.
4.	 5 health lecture sessions conducted.
5.	 BES organized 4 health-related activities after health examinations, which included:
•	 Smoking Cessation Program: 9 groups with 18 participants.
•	 Weight Loss Challenge: 193 participants, resulting in a total reduction of 305 kg.
•	 Walking Challenge: 254 participants, collectively walking 150 million steps (each person walked 200,000 steps per month for 3 consecutive months).
•	 Health and Fitness Program: 480 participants (implemented across all site offices).
Communication 
with 
Stakeholders
1.	 Quarterly Occupational Safety and Health Committee meetings will continue to be chaired by the Chairman (chief committee member) in 
accordance with occupational safety and health management regulations, aiming for continuous improvement of the work environment and 
prevention of occupational accidents and diseases.
2.	 BES implemented the "2024 Construction Site Safety, Quality, and Environmental Management Implementation Plan," conducting occupational 
safety and health education and training at various site offices.
3.	 BES promoted a Workplace Safety and Health Week, led by top management and first-tier supervisors, to launch activities and foster a friendly and 
healthy workplace.

of "Taiwan Occupational Safety Card" training courses for new employees in 2024.

Department of Labor Inspection), the National Construction Industry Occupational Safety and Health Promotion Association (under the Ministry 
of Labor's Occupational Safety and Health Agency), and the Industrial Safety and Health Association of the R.O.C (a non-profit organization). BES 
actively participated in various meetings and activities held by these associations.
1. Occupational Safety and Health Management
▍Occupational Safety and Health Management System  GRI 403-1  403-8
To ensure employee safety and prevent occupational hazards, in accordance with the Occupational Safety and Health Act and relevant regulations, BES has 
implemented the ISO 45001:2018 & CNS 45001 Occupational Safety and Health Management System. This system has been successfully certified by SGS 
Taiwan Ltd. In accordance with legal requirements, BES has appointed occupational safety and health management personnel, established an occupational 
safety and health reward and punishment system, and strengthened its post-incident learning and improvement processes.
BES integrates data for all applicable personnel based on ISO 45001 and categorizes and compiles statistics by referencing local occupational safety 
regulations. Data sources include the HR system, construction site personnel attendance records, contractor management platforms, and internal and 
external audit reports. The accuracy of this data is ensured through internal and third-party audits. The scope of workplaces covered by the Occupational 
Safety and Health Management System includes all BES construction sites, covering relevant workers (all internal employees and controlled contractor 
personnel), with no specific worker exclusions. This includes a total of 2,138 official employees (including migrant workers). Contractors and subcontractors 
are also covered; however, their exact numbers are not tracked within the system, only their work hours are recorded. The estimated number of these 
personnel, based on work hours, is approximately 2,146 individuals (calculated as 4,291,506 total hours divided by 2,000 working hours per person per year).

▍Occupational Safety and Health Committee  GRI 403-4  
BES's Occupational Safety and Health Committee is chaired by the Chairman or their proxy, who oversees all committee affairs. The committee consists of

personnel, medical and nursing staff engaged in employee health services, and engineering technical personnel related to occupational safety and health. 
The 6 employee representatives are elected by the BES Industrial Union.

2. Occupational Safety Risk Assessment and Control
▍Occupational Safety Hazard Risk Assessment and Control GRI 403-2  403-7
The assessment of occupational safety risks and opportunities at BES is spearheaded by the 
BES Occupational Safety and Health Management Department. This department is responsible 
for training and assisting with risk assessment procedures, approving risk assessment 
results and improvement measures, helping propose corrective suggestions, and tracking 
their effectiveness. The concrete execution of these tasks falls to the individual units and 
engineering project teams.
▍Occupational Hazard Identification and Risk Assessment
BES conducts hazard identification to pinpoint potential sources, situations, or behaviors 
that could cause injury or harm to personnel, as well as the characteristics of related 
hazards. We consider the potential severity and likelihood of combinations of hazard events 
and exposures that could lead to risk. Simultaneously, we evaluate the effectiveness of 
existing control measures to determine the acceptability of risks and decide on appropriate 
countermeasures. BES also performs hazard identification analysis and sets risk levels based 
on occupational accident records. Common types of occupational safety hazards include 
falls/rolling, entanglement/crushing injuries, slips, and being struck. Employees conduct 
daily self-inspections, and site managers lead on-site walkthroughs. During these activities, 
non-compliant machinery, equipment, facilities, and unsafe behaviors are documented as 
deficiencies, and improvements are then implemented.
▍Identification Process

Happy Workplace and Social Impact
BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report
▍Establishing Assessment Methods
BES clearly defines the methodology and standards for occupational 
safety and health risk assessment, specifying its scope, nature, and 
timing to ensure its proactive and systematic application. BES adheres 
to the principle of "Safety First" when conducting risk assessments 
for construction projects. If the owner has stricter regulations or 
requirements, the Engineering Project Department will comply with 
the owner's specified content for risk assessment.
▍Background Establishment
The Occupational Safety and Health Management Department 
assists Engineering Projects and responsible units in establishing 
a Risk and Opportunity Assessment Form (hereinafter referred to 
as "Assessment Form") based on risk and opportunity assessment 
procedures. This form covers aspects such as operational procedures 
and their personnel, materials, machinery and equipment, operational 
methods, and working environment, serving as the foundation for 
identifying occupational safety and health risks and opportunities.
▍	Occupational Safety and Health Risk and Opportunity 
Identification
The Occupational Safety and Health Management Department, 
in conjunction with engineering projects and responsible units, 
performs environmental impact considerations as part of the risk and 
opportunity assessment process, covering aspects like air pollution, 
water pollution, waste, toxic substances, and noise. After identifying 
high-risk operations such as falls, electric shocks, slips, and burns, 
the results are recorded in the Assessment Form, serving as the basis 
for ESH (Environmental, Safety, and Health) risk and opportunity 
assessment. If necessary, workers and stakeholders will be consulted 
or invited to participate.
The identification process also includes the identification of other ESH 
opportunities to enhance ESH performance. This involves considering 
planning, changing the organization, policies, processes, or activities, 
and adapting work, work organization, and the work environment to 
suit worker opportunities, eliminate hazards, and reduce ESH risks.
▍Risk and Opportunity Assessment
The Occupational Safety and Health Management Department, in collaboration with 
engineering projects and the Human Resources Department (consulting or inviting 
workers or worker representatives and stakeholders to participate when necessary), 
conducts risk and opportunity assessments in accordance with regulations. This 
involves evaluating the probability and severity of occupational safety and health 
risks and opportunities, as well as environmental impacts and opportunities, to 
determine unacceptable risks and significant environmental impacts. The results are 
recorded in the Assessment Form.
The Human Resources Department is responsible for conducting occupational safety 
and health risk and opportunity assessments for offices and warehouses under 
the headquarter's jurisdiction. These assessments should be reviewed annually or 
whenever there are changes.
Upon the establishment of a new project, the engineering project team performs 
an ESH risk and opportunity assessment according to the second edition of the 
Risk Assessment Technical Guidelines and submits it to the Occupational Safety and 
Health Management Department for record. This process may adopt a phased risk 
assessment approach depending on the characteristics of the construction project.
Engineering projects review the ESH risk and opportunity assessment form at 
least every three months based on operational conditions and submit it to the 
Occupational Safety and Health Management Department for record.
The Occupational Safety and Health Management Department regularly collects 
and updates the latest occupational safety and health knowledge and information, 
such as information or reports from government safety and health authorities, labor 
inspection agencies, safety and health consulting firms, and other organizations, to 
serve as a basis for determining risk and opportunity control measures.
▍Risk and Opportunity Control
Engineering projects and the Enterprise Resources Department, based on the risk 
and opportunity assessment, formulate feasible risk control countermeasures for 
identified unacceptable risks and significant environmental impacts, including 
opportunities for improvement.
If the risk assessment level is deemed unacceptable or represents a significant 
environmental impact, and it cannot be effectively reduced to an acceptable risk or a 
non-significant environmental impact, it should be managed as an ESH objective in 
accordance with system management procedures.

▍Response and Management
At BES, environmental factors, materials, behaviors, and operations 
within our scope are all considered potential hazards. These 
aspects are fed back into the assessment form for risk evaluation, 
identification, and tiered control. BES engineering projects conduct 
hazard identification and assessment following the safety and 
health risk assessment process to determine the probability and 
severity of occupational safety and health risks, thereby deciding if a 
particular hazard is an unacceptable risk or a significant impact. When 
a risk is deemed unacceptable (R=4), risk control measures must 
be implemented within a specified timeframe. Operations cannot 
commence until the risk is reduced to an acceptable level. Risks at 
level 2 or lower are considered low risk, requiring no immediate 
mitigation measures, but the effectiveness of existing protective 
measures must be ensured.
▍	BES Occupational Safety and Health Management: 
	
Hazard Identification, Analysis, and Improvement Measures
In 2024, BES identified a total of 39 high-risk hazards, based on the specific 
characteristics of each site office and the nature of the work. All new project sites 
undergo a hazard risk identification process. The identified high-risk hazards 
included 19 cases of fall/rolling hazards, 3 cases of falling objects, 8 cases of 
collapse/caving-in, 5 cases of collision/being struck, and 4 cases of drowning/
oxygen deficiency hazards. Improvement measures for these identified hazards 
have been fully implemented (see table below for details).
In the event of changes, we will reassess risks and opportunities 
related to temporary or permanent modifications in engineering 
projects. If necessary, we will revise plans and implement measures to 
mitigate negative impacts and enhance improvement opportunities. 
Simultaneously, we will develop change risk control plans as required 
by the owner and notify relevant units via email about new products, 
services, processes, or changes to existing ones concerning workplace 
location, surrounding environment, work organization, working 
conditions, equipment, and other related matters. When necessary, 
the Occupational Safety and Health Department will review the 
need for relevant updates, manage document revisions according to 
established procedures, communicate them appropriately to affected 
personnel, and retain records.

Fall/Rolling 
Hazard
Uninstalled/
unused safety 
facilities, 
insufficient 
protective 
measures, and 
other unsafe 
behaviors and 
environments.
1.	 For operations at locations with a height difference exceeding 1.5 
meters, install compliant safety access equipment.
2.	 For edges and openings of workplaces with a height difference of 
2 meters or more, install fall protection facilities such as compliant 
guardrails, covers, safety nets, or full-body harnesses. 
3.	 For operations at locations with a height difference of 2 meters 
or more where aerial work platforms, scaffolding, or other work 
platforms are difficult to set up or are not used, implement measures 
such as installing safety nets or wearing safety harnesses.
4.	 Use compliant mobile ladders and stepladders, and use them 
according to regulations/requirements. 
5.	 For steel structures exceeding two stories or 7.5 meters in height, 
erect safety nets with clear space underneath, ensuring no obstacles 
between the work surface and the safety net. 
6.	 Provide sufficient lighting and ensure clear passages. 
7.	 Conduct legally required education and training, and implement 
education and training and hazard notification for personnel 
entering the site. 
8.	 Conduct self-inspections of facilities/equipment.
Falling 
Object 
Hazard
Lack of facilities 
to prevent 
falling objects, 
insufficient 
protective 
measures, 
absence 
of control 
measures, and 
other unsafe 
behaviors and 
environments.
1.	 Remove loose stones, install facilities to prevent falling objects, and 
provide protective measures such as safety helmets.
2.	 Objects at risk of falling should be secured; protective nets should 
be installed at the edges of openings where falling objects are a risk.
3.	 Long objects should generally be hoisted with two slings at two 
points, and large-area objects with four slings at four points. When 
necessary, a tagline should be used to control the object's direction.
4.	 Control the area beneath hoisted objects, and assign dedicated 
monitoring personnel to strictly prohibit unauthorized entry into the 
warning line area.
5.	 Conduct legally required education and training, and implement 
education and training and hazard notification for personnel 
entering the site.
6.	 Conduct self-inspections of facilities/equipment.

Hazard 
Identification
Hazard Analysis
Improvement Measures
Collapse 
Hazard
Lack of facilities/measures to 
prevent collapse/toppling, 
absence of control measures, 
and other unsafe behaviors 
and environments.
1.	 Earth retaining supports, formwork supports, and scaffolding, etc., must be designed and calculated by a dedicated 
professional engineer for installation, and supporting ties or pins must not be arbitrarily replaced.
2.	 Material stacking height must not exceed 1.8 meters, and avoid placing materials in areas susceptible to external impact.
3.	 Concrete formwork supports or other temporary structures must not be connected to scaffolding; scaffolding should use 
bracing for appropriate auxiliary support.
4.	 The ground for setting up scaffolding and construction platforms must be level and tightly compacted, and, if necessary, 
suitable padding material should be used to prevent sliding or uneven settlement.
5.	 Scaffolding must have wall ties installed at vertical intervals not exceeding 5.5 meters and horizontal intervals not exceeding 
7.5 meters, securely connected to the structure.
6.	 Scaffolding and wall ties used must comply with CNS4750 regulations.
7.	 For steel column/beam assembly, lifting hooks may only be released after all installation bolts are fully inserted and secured.
8.	 Demolition work must not be carried out at different heights simultaneously; demolition should proceed sequentially from 
top to bottom. Demolished materials must not be excessively accumulated or stacked against walls. Structures at risk of 
falling or vibrating loose should be prioritized for demolition.
9.	 Demolition work areas must be controlled within appropriate boundaries, and dedicated monitoring personnel must be 
assigned to strictly prohibit non-essential personnel from entering the warning line area.
10.	 Conduct legally required education and training, and implement education and training and hazard notification for 
personnel entering the site.
11.	 Conduct self-inspections of facilities/equipment.
Collision/
Being Struck 
Hazard
Uncontrolled work areas 
/ Construction vehicles 
striking personnel / 
Excavator operations striking 
construction personnel.
1.	 Control work areas/operation radii by fencing.
2.	 Strictly control entry of non-construction personnel into the work area. 
3.	 Limit maximum speed for vehicles within the work zone and implement pedestrian-vehicle separation.
4.	 Conduct legally required education and training, and implement education and training and hazard notification for 
personnel entering the site. 
5.	 Conduct self-inspections of facilities/equipment.
Drowning 
Hazard
Personnel are at risk of 
drowning during underwater 
pipe cutting operations.
1.	 Provide life jackets and lifebuoys; the diving operations supervisor must be present for full-time supervision.
2.	 Conduct education and training, self-inspections, on-site supervision by the operations supervisor, regular inspections, and 
daily patrols.
3.	 Ensure personnel wear safety helmets, reflective vests, safety shoes, and life jackets.
4.	 Implement warnings for the work area.
5.	 Conduct legally required education and training, and implement education and training and hazard notification for 
personnel entering the site (including boat licenses and qualifications for technical personnel, diving certifications, diving 
operations supervisor certifications, etc.).
6.	 Conduct self-inspections of facilities and equipment.
Oxygen 
Deficiency 
Hazard
Uninstalled/unused ventilation 
facilities, insufficient protective 
measures, and other unsafe 
behaviors and environments.
1.	 Establish and implement a hazard prevention plan.
2.	 Implement ventilation and air exchange.
3.	 Measure the concentration of oxygen, dangerous substances, and harmful substances within confined spaces.
4.	 Provide, use, and regularly maintain personal protective equipment/respirators.
5.	 Implement permit-to-work procedures and control for personnel entering the work area.
6.	 Conduct legally required education and training, and implement education and training and hazard notification for 
personnel entering the site.

▍Strengthening Occupational Safety PDCA
In 2024, BES implemented the BES Construction Management System, integrating 
it with a real-time audio-visual command center system. This mandates daily 
self-inspections with photo uploads, enhancing hazard identification and risk 
management at each site office and raising awareness of occupational safety. 
The process begins with pre-work education, managing the steps and details of 
occupational safety measures. Site offices are required to conduct self-inspections 
(including self-inspection records, identified deficiencies, and deficiency 
improvements). Additionally, daily close-out meetings are held for review and 
analysis (analyzing deficiencies and formulating improvement methods). These 
close-out meetings also involve discussing the next day's work items and risk types, 
identifying high-risk categories, confirming necessary occupational safety facilities, 
and assigning personnel for the next day's self-inspection, along with track and 
follow up on today's occupational safety deficiencies, today's self-inspection forms, 
and today's identified deficiencies.
Beyond statutory requirements, BES additionally mandates daily patrol reports 
with photographic evidence, uploaded simultaneously via the real-time audio-
visual command center system. In 2024, the self-inspection rate reached 83%, with 
an average of 1.7 deficiencies found per inspection. This demonstrates proactive 
efforts in on-site risk identification and improvement, as well as effective auditing.
▍Awareness Enhancement
▍Digital System Management
BES digitizes reporting for critical occupational safety, quality, and 
environmental information. This includes pre and post-earthquake, 
typhoon, and heavy rain inspections, as well as inspection results from 
occupational safety and environmental agencies, client inspections, 
experienced work hours (safety and environmental monthly reports), 
major incident express reports, and ISO corrective action requests. After 
the headquarter conducts an audit of a site office, the inspection results 
are digitized and sent to the site office via the EIP system. Tracking 
continues until improvements are confirmed complete before the case 
is closed. To demonstrate BES's commitment to occupational safety, the 
headquarter increased its inspection efforts starting in 2023, aiming to 
elevate occupational safety standards at site offices. 
Notes: 1. 	Self-inspection Rate = Actual Inspection Days by Field Personnel / Planned Inspection Days (Engineer 
Inspection Days = Workdays * 100% - 2 Days Off；Site Manager Inspection Days = Workdays * 70% - 2 Days 
Off；Assistant Site Manager Inspection Days = Workdays * 50% - 2 Days Off).
2. 	Number of Deficiencies Found = Number of Identified Deficiencies / Actual Inspection Days.
BES also ensures all partners adhere to occupational safety 
and health standards through a stringent contractor safety 
management system, thereby mitigating safety risks during 
construction. We require all contractors to sign a safety 
commitment letter and undergo pre-construction safety training, 
ensuring their workers understand risk prevention measures. In 
cases of severe violations, we will demand corrective actions as 
per contractual agreements and, depending on the situation, 
may issue stop-work orders or terminate cooperation to ensure 
safety standards are rigorously enforced.
Occupational accidents are often caused by unsafe individual 
behaviors and insufficient hazard identification. Therefore, 
BES actively promotes self-safety awareness and sensitivity to 
workplace hazards among workers. In addition to fostering 
employees' self-awareness of risks, BES also establishes 
robust occupational safety and health management at 
construction sites and provides comprehensive training for 
work crews to reduce occupational accidents.
In 2024, the headquarter conducted a total of 667 inspections-
including 37 inspections led by the Occupational Safety 
and Health Department manager;
147 routine inspections by the Occupational Safety and 
Health Department;
483 online inspections.
Site office supervisors conducted 1,052 walk-through managements.

▍Accident Notification, Investigation, and Follow-up Procedures
For high-risk work items, contractors are informed during the close-out meeting the day before construction, and necessary equipment is prepared. On the morning of 
construction, a kick-off meeting is held to announce precautions and confirm that workers are physically and mentally fit for the tasks. The on-site engineer then assesses and 
confirms this before workers sign the attendance sheet and begin work. BES also has an immediate stop-work policy, allowing workers to immediately halt operations and 
report to their supervisor or safety and health management personnel if they discover a hazardous work environment that could lead to injury or illness. They may also apply 
to their direct supervisor for reassignment to another position.

Cause 
Investigation
Review and 
Improvement 
Measures
	 Activate "Accident Investigation and Analysis Process": Safety and health management personnel will form an investigation 
team, including the on-site supervisor, relevant technical staff, and employee representatives. This team will conduct hazard 
identification and risk assessment at the accident site to analyze the root causes leading to the incident.
	 For major occupational accidents, a "Major Occupational Accident Investigation and Response Team" will be established. 
Department supervisors or designated personnel will serve as conveners and immediately proceed to the site with relevant 
department heads for inspection and verification. After submitting an "Accident Prevention Report" to the President, a review 
meeting for the major occupational accident investigation report will be convened within one week. The occupational safety 
and health business supervisor will serve as the convener, inviting department heads, employee representatives, and others 
to participate, with the Occupational Safety and Health Department explaining the circumstances and handling of the major 
occupational accident.
	 Investigation results will be used to formulate corrective and preventive measures based on the hierarchy of controls (engineering 
controls, administrative controls, personal protective equipment). These measures will be integrated into the occupational safety 
and health management system for continuous improvement. Accident reports and improvement plans will be regularly reviewed 
during safety meetings to prevent similar incidents from recurring.
	 In cases of major occupational accidents, photographic evidence will be collected along with the investigation report and 
submitted to the Occupational Safety and Health Department to be used as training case studies, aiming to prevent similar events 
from happening again.

Calculation methods and explanations are as follows:
Note 1: 	Total Annual Work Hours: This sums all workers' total annual work hours. For employees, it's calculated by adding actual work and overtime hours. For contractors, the annual data is approximated by multiplying 8 hours per day by the 
monthly number of personnel entering the facility and the number of working days per month.
Note 2: 	Lost Workdays: This refers to days unable to work (rest days). The calculation includes injury leave due to occupational accidents but excludes sick leave and menstrual leave.
Note 3: 	Recordable Occupational Injuries: This refers to accidental injuries sustained by workers while performing duties or within the workplace. The statistical basis does not include "commuting accidents" to and from work.
Note 4: 	Fatality Rate = (Number of fatalities due to occupational injury ÷ Total man-hours) × 1,000,000.
Note 5: 	Serious Occupational Injury: This refers to an injury resulting from an occupational accident that leads to disability or inability to recover to the pre-injury health status within six months (excluding fatalities).
Note 6: 	Serious Occupational Injury Rate = (Number of serious occupational injuries ÷ Total man-hours) × 1,000,000.
Note 7: 	Disabling Injury: This refers to injuries where a worker suffers death, permanent total disability, permanent partial disability, or temporary total disability due to an occupational accident.
Note 8: 	Disabling Frequency Rate (FR) = (Number of disabling injury occurrences ÷ Total man-hours) × 1,000,000.
Note 9: 	Disabling Severity Rate (SR) = (Number of lost days due to disabling injuries ÷ Total man-hours) × 1,000,000.
Note 10: Total Recordable Injury Rate (TRIR) = (Number of recordable occupational injuries [including serious occupational injuries, fatalities, and other recordable occupational injuries]) × 200,000 ÷ Total man-hours.
Note 11: Frequency-Severity Indicator (FSI) for Disabling Injuries = √[(FR × SR) ÷ 1,000].
Note 12: Calculation Method for Rates: Calculations are rounded to two decimal places, with the third decimal place truncated.

▍Occupational Diseases  GRI 403-10
During the reporting period, BES had no fatalities among 
employees or contractors due to occupational diseases. 
Furthermore, there were no recordable cases of occupational 
diseases. BES identifies potential occupational disease 
hazards at construction sites—such as prolonged exposure 
to dust, noise, vibration, and chemical substances—through 
occupational risk assessments, workplace environmental 
monitoring, and regular health examinations. Within the 
reporting period, BES found no cases of occupational diseases 
resulting from these hazards. To mitigate risks, BES implements 
a hierarchy of controls, including the provision of personal 
protective equipment (PPE), the enhancement of on-site 
ventilation, the establishment of noise and dust monitoring 
systems, and the delivery of regular occupational health 
education to ensure the health and safety of both employees 
and non-employees.
BES compiles occupational disease data in accordance with 
the ISO 45001 Occupational Health and Safety Management 
System and local labor regulations. This is done through regular 
health examinations, environmental monitoring reports, safety 
records, and medical feedback, ensuring the completeness and 
accuracy of the data. Additionally, BES conducts annual internal 
and external audits to confirm the effectiveness of its health 
management mechanisms and enhance the implementation of 
occupational disease prevention measures.
However, given that construction site workers tend to be older, 
personnel may experience dizziness, fainting, or other incidents 
due to personal illnesses or physiological factors. BES has now 
established a plan in accordance with the "Occupational Safety 
and Health Guidelines for Middle-Aged and Older Workers" 
issued by the Ministry of Labor. Dedicated nurses also assess 
workers' health status based on their health examination 
reports (refer to the "Employee Health Promotion" section of 
this report for details) and make adjustment as needed.
▍2024 Occupational Safety and Health Violation Statistics  GRI 2-27
In 2024, BES incurred one fine due to a major occupational accident, defined as a 
violation resulting from a "major occupational accident" under Article 37, Paragraph 
2 of the Occupational Safety and Health Act Additionally, there were 25 other fines 
for violations of occupational safety and health or labor-related regulations, totaling 
NTD 3,500,000. Regarding occupational safety and health facilities, BES continues to 
enhance education and training, actively implement self-inspections and walk-through 
management, and establish a company-wide reporting system for control. Furthermore, 
concerning violations of the Labor Standards Act, BES has also strengthened controls 
over evening and nighttime construction activities, ensuring all operations continue to 
develop on a compliant basis.
In 2024, one major occupational accident occurred. The following corrective actions were 
implemented based on the cause of the incident:
Note: 	Occupational diseases are recognized in accordance with regulations such as the 
"Occupational Disease Classification Table for Labor Occupational Accident Insurance".
1.	 For contractors entering the site: Before entry, thoroughly inform the contractor 
about the work environment, hazard factors, and necessary safety and health 
measures. Require the contractor, if subcontracting all or part of their work, to 
inform the sub-contractor according to the same regulations.
2.	 Strengthen and implement strict entry control for personnel and machinery: 
Prohibit anyone or any equipment found non-compliant with legal regulations 
during entry inspections from entering the workplace. Immediately stop and 
remove anyone found entering without adhering to regulations.
3.	 Implement key pre-operation checks, monthly regular inspections, and annual 
comprehensive inspections for construction vehicles.
4.	 Strengthen control over construction personnel and vehicle operations: 
Implement self-inspections and daily patrols. If unsafe conditions or behaviors 
are observed during patrols, immediately demand improvements, take photos, 
and record the findings to ensure operational safety.
5.	 Establish a safe operating procedure for construction vehicles: Break down pre-
operation, in-progress, post-operation, and abnormal situation handling into 
distinct tasks, and define corresponding safety actions and safety facilities/
measures.

3. Employee Health Promotion  GRI 403-3  403-6
BES cares deeply about the well-being of every employee. Beyond striving to create a friendly and secure work environment, 
we offer a comprehensive health service program to ensure each employee understands their physical condition. In 2024, the 
overall health check-up participation rate reached 98%. Following these check-ups, the company specifically engaged a health 
management consulting firm to provide on-site health services and occupational health and hygiene awareness sessions at both 
the headquarter and all site offices, offering employees a direct channel for health consultations.
In accordance with the Occupational Safety and Health Act, BES regularly arranges health examinations for employees. In recent 
years, the company's subsidies for health check-ups have exceeded legal requirements: employees with over 10 years of service 
receive NT15,000, while other employees receive NT8,000. The subsequent individual health examination reports are treated as 
confidential personal data, secured by a dedicated nurse with lock and/or document encryption. While employees can access 
their own reports, company nurses are also authorized to view them for health-related care, ensuring the implementation of the 
Labor Health Services Program and promoting health activities. There is no discrimination or disadvantageous treatment of any 
employee based on their individual health status as revealed in their health check-up reports.
▍Evaluation Process
▍Implementation Results
In 2024, our employees benefited from 12 on-site physician visits, each lasting 3 hours. We also 
employed a dedicated labor health nurse to provide full-time, specialized care for employee well-being. 
Furthermore, through a tiered management system, we identified high-risk groups based on indicators 
such as blood lipids, blood sugar, blood pressure, and other health metrics. For employees identified as 
high-risk, our dedicated physician and labor health nurse provided ongoing care and follow-up. Based 
on the statistical results from health check-ups, we invited healthcare professionals to conduct health-
focused workshops and provide consultation services to further enhance employee health. In addition to 
on-site medical and nursing services, we also hosted health lectures, encouraging employees to attend 
and learn effective health management strategies through these sessions.

In response to the specific characteristics of our industry, BES places particular emphasis 
on the risk of cardiovascular disease among middle-aged and older (45 years and 
above) employees within a 10-year period. We use a "Human Factors and Overload 
Questionnaire" to identify instances of overwork or health-related issues affecting 
job performance. Based on the questionnaire results, we review work patterns and 
develop improvement plans. In accordance with regulations, BES controls workplaces, 
equipment, raw materials, chemicals, vapors, gases, and dust that could cause illness, 
injury, disability, or death, ensuring employee safety.

conditions, noise, jet lag, irregular work, frequent business trips, and stressful work patterns. This helps evaluate the 
degree of employee workload.
▍	Community Communication and Impact Assessment
	
GRI 413-1  413-2
Before developing any construction sites, BES conducts community impact 
assessments and environmental identification procedures, establishing 
a management system in accordance with ISO 14001:2015 standards. 
All development projects require pre-construction briefing sessions, 
covering 100% of projects. In 2024, we held 30 community engagement 
events for urban renewal projects. In response to feedback from these 
briefings, BES adjusts construction plans where feasible. This includes 
measures like controlling construction hours, environmental monitoring, and 
pedestrian pathway planning, thereby strengthening trust and consensus 
with residents. For public construction projects, the owner conducts the 
environmental assessment, and BES proceeds with construction only after all 
relevant regulations are met. For private construction projects, we conduct 
neighboring property assessments, traffic impact assessments, and hazard 
impact assessments, among others. As of the end of the reporting year, 
our operations and construction sites in 2024 were assessed as having no 
significant negative impact on their respective communities. We received 
no reports of major community impact events (such as protests or formal 
complaints) recognized by regulatory authorities. BES will continue to uphold 
its "good neighbor" principle, fostering positive community relationships 
while ensuring both construction safety and environmental quality.
Environmental Impact Identification and Assessment
To effectively meet environmental management requirements, BES headquarter's 
Occupational Safety and Health Center oversees all Engineering Projects. Every 
project must comply with ISO 14001 environmental management system 
standards, which helps increase participant adherence to environmental 
regulations and reduces the frequency of fines due to environmental deficiencies. 
Assessment personnel (or team) conduct a comprehensive identification and 
evaluation of direct and indirect environmental aspects. This includes considering 
office operations, construction materials used, suppliers, stakeholder groups, 
engineering contractors, construction execution, project acceptance to waste 
disposal capabilities, energy and resource utilization, and future development. 
The goal is to achieve continuous improvement and ensure compliance with 
environmental regulations. BES also performs construction and ecological 
reviews in accordance with regulations to ensure comprehensive environmental 
protection measures are in place and to minimize potential impacts.

Community Communication
Before commencing public construction projects and urban renewal cases, BES conducts stringent site selection processes and holds pre-construction briefing sessions. 
These sessions inform neighboring residents about the overall construction plan, fostering mutual communication and coordination to build strong trust. If residents 
have suggestions during construction, they can reach out via contact numbers or face-to-face discussions. In 2024, BES held a total of 30 urban renewal briefing sessions, 
demonstrating our commitment to urban renewal and public service. To rebuild homes that better meet market demands and offer stability for landowners, BES has 
successfully completed two " salt-contaminated building" urban renewal projects in the Minsheng Community of Songshan District, Taipei City. Two more projects are 
currently under construction, as we continue our dedication to reconstructing old and salt-contaminated residences, providing more secure and quality homes for 
landowners and nearby residents. Furthermore, for projects such as the Formosa Plastics Building Urban Renewal and New Construction Project, environmental management 
is a priority from the outset. This includes planning construction routes, implementing environmental protection measures, controlling construction hours, setting up 
environmental monitoring systems, and managing vehicle access. In July 2024, a pre-demolition permit construction briefing session was held to explain the project overview 
and related plans.
Rigorous Development Site Selection Process
For all construction projects, BES follows a rigorous process to ensure comprehensive risk assessment during site selection:

Planning and Design
Disaster prevention and evacuation plans are integrated into the design. 
This includes planning for disaster safety zones as fire compartments 
within the building, adhering to building technical regulations. 
Simultaneously, BES utilizes planned road spaces around the site 
to design a comprehensive pedestrian system, ensuring adequate 
emergency evacuation routes and effectively enabling residents to be 
safely evacuated to nearby open spaces during fires or earthquakes.

Development and Impact of Investment and Support Services  GRI 203-1  413-1
Since 1970, BES has actively engaged in the development of industrial parks across Taiwan, completing 37 industrial zones to date. By constructing essential 
public infrastructure, facilitating land leasing and sales, and attracting investment, we've driven local industrial growth, created employment opportunities 
and economic value, promoted regional sustainable development, and improved residents' quality of life. Currently, key development projects for BES 
include the Changbin Industrial Park (Xianxi and Lunwei Districts) and the Yunlin Industrial Park. In 2024, we completed several significant infrastructure 
projects within these parks, continuing to advance related construction.
▍Community Revitalization and Urban Renewal
Adhering to principles of integrity, pragmatism, and fairness, BES is dedicated to the reconstruction of aging apartments and buildings affected by salt-
contaminated concrete. We've successfully integrated and revitalized the Yanshou Public Housing and Nangang Chenggong New City communities in Taipei 
City's Songshan District, encompassing a total of 700 salt-contaminated households. Our reconstructed project for the Yanshou Public Housing Zone I, "BES 
Biyange," was honored with the 2024 Urban Renewal and Hazardous Building Reconstruction Group Award, setting a benchmark for urban renewal. BES is 
also advancing the Formosa Plastics Building urban renewal project, undertaking block-level urban revitalization to rejuvenate urban functions and create a 
modern new look for the city center.
Total Investment Amount: From 1990 to 
December 31, 2024, cumulative investments 
reached NTD 55.389 billion, with NTD 1.812 
billion invested in 2024 alone.
Key Development Projects:
•	 Lunwei West District Metal Surface Treatment 
Zone (Electroplating Zone): Roads and Public 
Pipelines (Phase 1)
•	 Lunwei West 1st District (Phase 2): Roads and 
Public Pipelines
•	 Lunwei West 1st District (Phase 2): Drainage Main 
Line and Sluice Gate
•	 Xianxi District A2405 Road Embankment (Phase 2)
•	 Lunwei West 1st District (Phase 4): Roads and 
Public Facilities
The development of industrial parks and the attraction of investment not 
only directly drive economic growth but also have a profound direct and 
indirect impact on local industrial clusters, employment, and population 
growth. Through the provision of comprehensive public facilities and 
proactive investment promotion, various industries are attracted to invest 
and set up factories, further fostering sustainable economic development.
In this region, the primary focus is on developing the metal product 
manufacturing industry, with the establishment of a Metal Surface Treatment 
Zone (Electroplating Zone) to attract related industries. This has spurred the 
clustered development of industries in the area. As of 2024, there are 173 
metal product suppliers in the Changbin Industrial Park, accounting for 29% 
of industrial parks in Central Taiwan, and this number continues to grow. 
Concurrently, in collaboration with the Changhua County Government and 
the Ministry of Economic Affairs' Central Taiwan Office, BES has assisted in 
relocating illegal local factories into the industrial park (a cumulative total of 
25 factories by 2024). We enforce regulations within the park for the control 
of process wastewater, air pollution, and waste emissions, thereby reducing 
local environmental pollution and achieving green industrial development.
BES will continue to invest in the 
infrastructure of the Changbin 
Industrial Park, optimizing 
public facilities to attract 
more businesses to invest and 
establish factories. We plan 
to inject an additional NTD 10 
billion within the next four 
years to further enhance the 
industrial park's development. 
This will drive local economic 
growth and foster industrial 
innovation, ultimately achieving 
the sustainable development 
goals for local industries.

▍Donations  
BES actively responds to the United Nations Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) and the Taiwan Sustainable Development Goals set by the Executive 
Yuan's National Council for Sustainable Development through concrete actions. Before initiating any construction, we conduct rigorous development site 
selection and hold pre-construction briefing sessions. This allows us to choose suitable objectives and identify opportunities to simultaneously promote 
social prosperity and good neighborly relations during construction. We also focus on community development and local needs to collectively achieve SDG 3: 
Good Health and Well-being, and the broader goals of sustainable development.

▍Membership in Associations and Organizations  GRI 2 -28
BES actively participates in numerous domestic industry associations, societies, and academic organizations. This strengthens close ties and exchanges 
with various sectors, fosters collaboration for sustainable development, and drives industrial growth through active operational involvement. The public 
associations, societies, academic organizations, and non-profit organizations BES participates in are diverse, covering areas such as construction expertise, 
industry exchange and development, occupational safety and health, and corporate sustainable management, based on their organizational nature and the 
issues they advocate.

BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report
Message from the Management
About BES
About This Report
2024 Sustainability Highlights
2024 ESG Architectural Achievements
2024 BES’s Signature Projects
Sustainability Strategy and Management
Appendix
Robust Operations and Corporate Governance
Environmental Friendliness and Green Engineering
Happy Workplace and Social Impact
No.
Elements
Implementation
1
Description of the oversight and governance by the Board of 
Directors and the management on climate-related risks and 
opportunities.
BES has a Risk Management Task Force and a Sustainability Committee under its Board of Directors. The Board of 
Directors serves as the highest authority for climate risk governance, responsible for approving climate targets and 
overseeing the operation of the risk management system.
In 2024, a risk meeting was convened to identify risk issues and report them to the Board of Directors. The 
Sustainability Committee regularly assesses the potential impact of climate change on business and finance, and in 
2024, it approved the Greenhouse Gas Reduction Policy and Net-Zero Commitment. The promoting executive also 
signed a commitment letter to support the 1.5° C target in July of the same year.
The climate-related risks and opportunities contained in this report were compiled and analyzed by BES's Risk 
Management Task Force and Sustainability Committee. The final disclosure content has been incorporated into this 
report and was submitted to the Board of Directors for their awareness and confirmation upon completion, ensuring 
the governance level's oversight responsibility for climate-related strategies.
2
Describe how the identified climate risks and opportunities 
impact the company's business, strategy and finances (short-
term, medium-term, long-term).
In the short term (1-3 years), extreme weather events like typhoons and heavy rainfall will cause construction site 
shutdowns and equipment damage, increasing maintenance and insurance costs, and impacting revenue.
In the medium term (3-5 years), we may face transition pressures from strengthened climate regulations, carbon fees, 
and energy transformation.
Long-term (5-10+ years), the global net-zero transition trend will reshape market competitive conditions, affecting 
material procurement, design planning, and investment cost structures.
3
Description of the financial impact arising from extreme 
weather events and transitional actions.
Please refer to the "Climate Action (Material Topic)" chapter for details on the financial impacts and response 
measures related to climate change risks and opportunities.
4
Description of how the climate risk identification,
assessment, and management processes are integrated into 
the overall risk management system.
BES integrates climate risk identification into its overall enterprise risk management process. The Risk Management 
Task Force executes this through six steps: risk identification, risk analysis, risk assessment, risk response, risk 
reporting, and disclosure. The Sustainability Committee assists in overseeing ESG risks across all facets. Climate risks 
are also included in the annual risk report, which is submitted to the Board of Directors and the Audit Committee.
5
Description of the used scenarios, parameters, assumptions, 
analysis factors, and main financial impacts if scenario 
analysis is used to analyze or assess the resilience against 
climate change risks.
Please refer to the "Climate Action (Material Topic)" chapter for details on climate change scenarios, and the financial 
impacts and response measures related to climate change risks and opportunities.
6
Description of the content as well as the metrics and targets 
used for any transition plan to identify and manage physical 
risks and transition risks for any transition plan to respond or 
manage climate-related risks.
BES implements various measures to advance its risk management, including the adoption of LED lighting and 
energy-efficient air conditioning. The company also plans to introduce an Energy Management System (ISO 50001) 
and carbon footprint assessments (ISO 14064-1), along with BIM estimation tools. Furthermore, carbon data from 
existing projects will serve as the foundation for planning new ones. Key performance indicators for management 
include carbon emissions (tCO2e), electricity consumption, and water usage.
7
Description of the basis for pricing if an internal carbon price 
is used.
Although an official internal carbon pricing mechanism has not yet been formally implemented, BES has referenced 
domestic carbon fee planning. We have estimated the potential impact if the carbon fee were to be NTD 500 per ton, 
and this estimation has been incorporated into our risk and financial impact assessments.
8
Description of the activities covered, scope of greenhouse 
gas emissions, timeframes planned, annual progress and so 
on if climate-related targets are set; description of the sources 
and quantity of carbon credits or the quantity of Renewable 
Energy Certificates (RECs) for offset if carbon offset or recs 
are employed to achieve relevant targets.
BES has set 2023 as the base year for its carbon reduction targets. By 2030, the company aims to achieve an absolute 
reduction of 42% in Scope 1 and 2 emissions, and a 25% reduction in Scope 3 emissions. The long-term goal is to 
reach net-zero carbon emissions by 2050.
Currently, BES is not utilizing carbon credits or renewable energy certificates, focusing primarily on organizational 
reduction initiatives. Progress on carbon reduction is regularly reported to the Board of Directors for oversight.
9
GHG inventory and assurance status, reduction targets, 
strategies amd specific action plans.
Please refer to the table below for details.
TCFD / Climate-Related Information of Listed Companies (Please refer to the Climate Action chapter for details.)

Climate-Related Information of Listed Companies
▍GHG Inventory and Assurance Status
Please provide the greenhouse gas emissions (tonnes CO2e), intensity (tonnes CO2e/NTD million), and data coverage for the most recent two years.
In accordance with the Financial Supervisory Commission's (FSC) "Roadmap for Sustainable Development of TWSE/TPEx-Listed Companies," listed 
companies with a capital of NTD 10 billion or more are required to:
1. Complete their parent company's individual inventory by 2023.
2. Complete the inventory for subsidiaries included in consolidated financial reports by 2025.
BES Engineering has established a greenhouse gas (GHG) inventory mechanism based on the Greenhouse Gas Protocol (GHG Protocol), published by the 
World Business Council for Sustainable Development (WBCSD) and the World Resources Institute (WRI). Starting from 2024, BES will annually conduct a 
regular inventory of GHG emissions for its parent company and all subsidiaries included in its consolidated financial reports. This ensures a comprehensive 
understanding of GHG usage and emission status and verifies the effectiveness of reduction initiatives.
Furthermore, the GHG inventory data for the most recent two years has been compiled using the operational control approach, encompassing the GHG 
emissions of the parent company and all subsidiaries included in the consolidated financial reports. Details are provided below:

BES Engineering 2024 Sustainability Report
▍Greenhouse Gas (GHG) Reduction Targets, Strategies, and Concrete Action Plans
Please state the greenhouse gas (GHG) reduction base year and its data, reduction targets, strategies, and specific action plans, and the achievement 
status of these reduction targets.
GHG Reduction Targets
Using 2023 as the base year, achieve an absolute reduction of 42% in Scope 1 and Scope 2 greenhouse gas emissions by 2030 (equivalent to an annual reduction 
of 6%), and a 25% reduction in Scope 3 emissions (equivalent to an annual reduction of 3.6%).
Strategies and Action Plans
BES Engineering Company and its consolidated entities have integrated carbon management strategies into their operational planning. This includes planning 
for inventory matters and reduction targets. Future plans involve setting short, medium, and long-term goals based on inventory results and establishing 
departmental carbon reduction tracking indicators:
1. BES's greenhouse gas (GHG) inventory and verification timeline was reported at the 17th meeting of the 26th Board of Directors. Progress on interim targets will 
subsequently be reported to the Board quarterly to facilitate their oversight and control.
2. To comply with Taiwan Stock Exchange regulations, subsidiaries/sub-subsidiaries included in BES's consolidated financial statements must complete their 
inventory lists by March 2025, their inventory reports by June 2025, and undergo external verification starting in 2027.
3. Excluding six paper companies, BES Construction Corporation, and Hua Ding Enterprise Co., Ltd., which are consolidated into the head office's inventory, BES 
previously held a GHG inventory briefing meeting for 14 subsidiaries/sub-subsidiaries on November 25, 2022. The first progress tracking meeting was held on 
October 8, 2024, and subsequent progress tracking meetings will continue every two months starting from December 2024 until each subsidiary/sub-subsidiary 
completes its inventory by June 2025.
4. Currently, BES Engineering is conducting greenhouse gas (GHG) inventories for Scope 1 and Scope 2 emissions. In accordance with the Financial Supervisory 
Commission's (FSC) "Roadmap for Taiwan's Adoption of International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRS) Sustainability Disclosure Standards," Scope 3 GHG 
emissions will be required for disclosure starting in 2028. BES has already begun collecting Scope 3 data in October 2024, with the aim of disclosing information 
for Scope 1, 2, and 3 GHG inventories starting in 2026.
5. For the year 2023, the total GHG emissions for the entire company (including site offices) amounted to 7,884.827 tonnes CO2e/year. This was verified by an 
external assurance provider (SGS) on August 20, 2024, and reasonable assurance was obtained on September 18, 2024. 2023 has been set as BES's baseline year. 
For 2024, the total GHG emissions for the entire company (including site offices) and eight key subsidiaries/sub-subsidiaries amounted to 9,798.999 tonnes 
CO2e/year. This was verified by an external assurance provider (SGS) on May 22, 2025, and reasonable assurance was obtained on June 10, 2025.
6. BES will further manage and disclose emissions categories that contribute to the largest emissions in accordance with regulations. For categories not yet 
disclosed, continuous evaluation and inclusion in the inventory will be pursued. The company will also periodically review its carbon reduction baseline year 
and formulate short-, medium-, and long-term carbon reduction strategies based on science-based targets. These will be integrated into departmental tracking 
indicators and reported to the Board of Directors for oversight and control.
